Allah's Guarantee for Followers of the Quran
Ibn Abbas reports Allah's guarantee for Quran readers who act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's guarantee of guidance and happiness is conditional upon both reading and acting upon the Quran.

Core Idea
Allah guarantees no misguidance and no misery for those who read and act upon the Quran.

This lesson presents a powerful statement from Ibn Abbas that links reading the Quran with acting upon it. It clarifies the conditions for receiving Allah's promise of guidance in this world and happiness in the Hereafter. The source passage is a brief but profound hadith-like report that anchors this promise in a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the word 'تكفل' which implies a divine commitment.
2
Identify the two conditions and two promises
Find the conditions (reading and acting) and the two promises (no misguidance in this world, no misery in the Hereafter).
The promises are linked to the two realms: dunya and akhira.
3
Reflect on the proof verse
Ibn Abbas recites Quran 20:123 as evidence. Consider how the verse supports the guarantee.
The verse speaks about following Allah's guidance, which is exactly what reading and acting entails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنه: «تكفل الله لمن قرأ القرآن وعمل بما فيه بأن لا يضل الدنيا ولا يشقى في العقبى، ثم قرأ هذه الآية: ﴿ فَمَنِ اتَّبَعَ هُدَايَ فَلَا يَضِلُّ وَلَا يَشْقَى [طه: ۱۲۳] . ﴾
And Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'Allah has guaranteed for whoever reads the Quran and acts by what is in it that he will not go astray in this world nor be miserable in the Hereafter, then he recited this verse: "And whoever follows My guidance will not go astray and will not be miserable" (20:123).'
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage records a statement from Ibn Abbas that Allah has taken it upon Himself (takaffala) to protect the one who recites the Quran and acts upon it from two things: going astray in this world (dalal) and being miserable in the Hereafter (shaqa'). Ibn Abbas then recites Quran 20:123 as proof. This emphasizes that mere recitation is not enough; action is required for the guarantee to apply.

Key Terms
تكفل
القرآن
لا يضل
لا يشقى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The guarantee applies to merely reciting the Quran without acting upon it.
Correction: The passage explicitly says 'and acts by what is in it' – action is a necessary condition for the guarantee.

Checkpoint
What does Allah guarantee for the one who reads the Quran and acts by it, according to Ibn Abbas?
A) Wealth in this world
B) Paradise without accountability
C) No misguidance in this world and no misery in the Hereafter
D) Immediate forgiveness of all sins

Key Takeaway
Allah's guarantee of guidance in this world and happiness in the Hereafter is for those who both read the Quran and act upon it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever recited a verse of the Quran without asking yourself what it requires from you? What is one verse you recited today that you have not yet lived by, and what will you do about it before tonight?
?
Do you truly trust Allah's guarantee that reading and acting upon the Quran will protect you from misguidance and misery? If so, why do you still sometimes feel lost or anxious? What is missing in your relationship with the Quran?
?
You claim to act upon the Quran, but is there an area of your life—your speech, your dealings, your thoughts—where you ignore its guidance? What would it cost you to obey it fully? Are you willing to pay that price?

The Reality of Resurrection after Death
The commentator defines resurrection and provides Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that resurrection after death in Islamic creed refers to the physical restoration of life after the body's dissolution, supported by definitive Quranic texts.

Core Idea
Resurrection is the physical restoration of life after death, not a spiritual return or prophetic mission.

In this passage, the commentator of al-Fiqh al-Akbar clarifies a central article of faith: the resurrection after death. He specifies that this resurrection is the restoration of life after the body's initial form has perished, distinguishing it from the sending of prophets. He then cites two clear Quranic verses and points to other definitive proofs. Let's examine the precise meaning and its scriptural foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its English translation once to grasp the overall meaning without overanalyzing.
Pay attention to the restriction (qayd) in the definition.
2
Analyze the definition and distinction
Note how the definition includes a restriction to clarify that resurrection means restoration after perishing, not the sending of prophets.
The commentary explains that the prophetic mission is also obligatory belief but not the topic here.
3
Examine the Quranic proofs
Look at the two verses cited (23:16 and 36:79) and consider why they are considered definitive texts for physical resurrection.
These verses directly affirm resurrection as a physical event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبعث) أي الحياة (بعد الموت) قيد يفيد أن المراد به الإعادة بعد فناء هيئة البداية، لا بعث الأنبياء إلى الخلق وإن كان مما يجب الإيمان به أيضاً، ودليله قوله سبحانه وتعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ إِنَّكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ تُبْعَثُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون : ١٦] وقوله سبحانه: ﴿قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِي أَنْشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ﴾ [يس: ٧٩]، إلى غير ذلك من النصوص القاطعة والأدلة اللامعة.
And the resurrection: i.e., life (after death). A restriction that indicates that what is meant by it is the restoration after the dissolution of the initial form, not the sending of prophets to the creation, although that too is necessarily believed in. And its proof is the saying of Allah Most High: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be resurrected' [Quran 23:16] and His saying: 'Say: He will give them life who produced them the first time' [Quran 36:79], and other definitive texts and luminous proofs.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines the article of faith 'resurrection after death' (البعث بعد الموت). It specifies that 'resurrection' here means the restoration of life after the body's initial form (هيئة البداية) has perished, i.e., physical resurrection. It clarifies that it is not the sending of prophets (which is also obligatory to believe in). Then it provides two Quranic proofs: Surah al-Mu'minun 16 and Surah Ya-Sin 79, along with other clear texts and proofs. The commentator emphasizes that this is a definitive belief supported by luminous evidence.

Key Terms
بعث
إعادة
حياة
موت
يوم القيامة
نصوص قاطعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think resurrection is only spiritual or refers to the sending of prophets after death.
Correction: The passage specifies that resurrection after death means the physical restoration of life after the body's dissolution, not a spiritual return or prophetic mission.

Checkpoint
What does 'al-ba'th ba'da al-mawt' (resurrection after death) refer to specifically according to this passage?
A) The sending of prophets after death.
B) The restoration of life after the body's dissolution.
C) The creation of a new soul.
D) The spiritual survival after death.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection after death is the physical restoration of life after bodily dissolution, proven by definitive Quranic texts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does knowing that your resurrection will be physical—your very bones and flesh reassembled—change the way you think about the body you inhabit now? What one thing will you start doing today to honor it as the vessel that will be returned to you?
?
If you truly believed that every moment of your life is leading to a literal, physical re-creation of your existence, what single habit or pattern would you be most ashamed to have 'restored' along with your body? What will you do about it before that day?
?
The commentator distinguishes between 'resurrection after death' and 'sending of prophets'. Are you secretly assigning the hope of physical resurrection to some worldly return—a second chance, a revival of a dream—instead of the actual, bodily confrontation with your Creator? How will you realign your hope today?

The Essential Attributes of Angels
Sanusi enumerates angelic attributes and refutes gender attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core attributes of angels according to Sunni Islam: their servitude, infallibility, and freedom from human gender.

Core Idea
Angels are honored, infallible servants of Allah, free from gender.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary establishes the fundamental qualities of angels as understood in Sunni theology. Before we can explore their roles, we must first affirm what angels are not—they are not divine beings, not gendered, and not prone to sin. The text then refutes the false claim that angels are Allah's daughters, citing clear Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on angelic attributes
Read the Arabic passage that describes angels as honored servants, infallible, and free from masculinity and femininity. Then read the translation.
Notice the sequence: servitude -> infallibility -> genderlessness.
2
Understand the Quranic refutation
Examine the two Quranic verses that refute the notion that angels are female offspring of God. Consider why this refutation is placed here.
The verses emphasize that angels are servants, not daughters.
3
Connect to broader Islamic theology
Reflect on how these attributes distinguish angels from any form of shirk. Why is it important to affirm that angels have no gender?
This guards against anthropomorphism and idolatry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وملائكته بأنهم عباد مكرمون لا يسبقونه بالقول وهم بأمره يعملون، وأنهم معصومون ولا يعصون الله ومنزهون عن صفة الذكورية ونعت الأنوثية وقد أنكر الله في كتابه على من قال: إنهم بنات الله حيث قال: ﴿وَجَعَلُوا الْمَلَائِكَةَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ عِبَادُ الرَّحْمَنِ إِنَاثًا أَشَهِدُوا خَلْقَهُمْ سَتُكْتَبُ شَهَادَتُهُمْ وَيُسْأَلُونَ﴾ [الزخرف: ١٩]، وقال أيضاً: ﴿أَصْطَفَى الْبَنَاتِ عَلَى الْبَنِينَ مَا لَكُمْ كَيْفَ تَحْكُمُونَ﴾ [الصافات: ١٥٣-١٥٤]. وذكر في "جواهر الأصول" أن الملائكة ليس لهم حظ من نعيم الجنان ولا من رؤية الرحمن، كذا في شرح القونوي لـ"عمدة النسفي" وذكر أيضاً أنهم أجسام لطيفة هوائية تقدر على التشكل بأشكال مختلفة أولو أجنحة مثنى وثلاث ورباع، مسكنهم السماوات أي مسكن معظمهم قال وهذا قول أكثر المسلمين.
And His angels: that they are honored servants, they do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command; and that they are infallible and do not disobey Allah, and are free from the attribute of masculinity and the description of femininity. And Allah denied in His Book those who say they are daughters of Allah, where He said: 'And they have made the angels, who are servants of the Merciful, females. Did they witness their creation? Their testimony will be recorded, and they will be questioned' [az-Zukhruf 19]. And He also said: 'Has He chosen daughters over sons? What is the matter with you? How do you judge?' [as-Saffat 153-154]. And it is mentioned in 'Jawahir al-Usul' that the angels have no share of the bliss of Paradise nor of the vision of the Merciful. Likewise in the commentary of al-Qunawi on 'Umdat an-Nasafi. And he also mentioned that they are subtle aerial bodies capable of assuming different forms, having wings in twos, threes, and fours. Their dwelling is the heavens, i.e., the dwelling of most of them. He said: And this is the saying of the majority of Muslims.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines the attributes of angels according to Sunni Islam. It begins by stating that angels are honored servants who do not precede Allah in speech and act by His command, emphasizing their servitude and obedience. It then asserts their infallibility (ismah) and their being free from human gender attributes, in refutation of those who consider them female offspring of God. It supports this with two Quranic verses: one from az-Zukhruf condemning the designation of angels as females, and another from as-Saffat questioning the preference of daughters over sons. The passage then cites 'Jawahir al-Usul' and the commentary of al-Qunawi to state that angels have no share in the bliss of Paradise or the beatific vision. It further describes them as subtle aerial bodies that can assume various forms, possessing wings in multiples, and dwelling in the heavens. The last two points are attributed to the majority of Muslims.

Key Terms
ملائكة
عباد مكرمون
معصومون
ذكورية
أنوثية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That angels are female or have gender, and that they are Allah's daughters.
Correction: The passage states angels are free from masculinity and femininity, and refutes the idea that they are Allah's offspring.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about angels?
A) They are able to sin.
B) They have gender like humans.
C) They are honored servants who do not precede Allah in speech.
D) They are Allah's daughters.

Key Takeaway
Angels are infallible, genderless servants of Allah, and the Quran strongly rejects any notion of them being divine offspring.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that angels are honored servants who never precede Allah in speech. When you speak about Allah or make du'a, do you ever rush ahead of His command, demanding your own wishes rather than submitting? Where in your life do you need to learn the adab of waiting upon Allah's permission?
?
The Quran angrily challenges those who attributed daughters to Allah: 'What is the matter with you? How do you judge?' How often do you, in your heart, attribute to Allah any imperfection or likeness to creation? What would it mean for you to truly purify your belief about Allah from every human projection?
?
Sanusi asserts that angels are free from both masculinity and femininity. We often imagine Allah in human terms too. In what subtle ways do you still think of Allah with human qualities? What step will you take today to actively remember His transcendence?

Angelic Nature: Bodies, Wings, and Their Relationship to Paradise
Sanusi describes angelic physicality and their exclusion from paradise and vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical nature of angels as subtle aerial bodies with wings, and their lack of share in paradise and the beatific vision.

Core Idea
Angels are subtle aerial bodies with wings, dwelling in heavens, without share in paradise or vision.

This lesson continues Sanusi's description of angels by delving into their physical form and their status in the afterlife. According to the cited authorities, angels are not only spiritual beings but also possess subtle bodies capable of transformation. However, they do not partake in the pleasures of paradise nor see Allah—a point that distinguishes them from humans.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on angelic bodies
Read the Arabic passage that describes angels as subtle aerial bodies with wings and their dwelling. Then read the translation.
Focus on the terms 'أجسام لطيفة هوائية' and 'أجنحة مثنى وثلاث ورباع'.
2
Understand the ruling on paradise and vision
Note the statement that angels have no share of paradise's bliss or the vision of Allah. Consider why this is mentioned.
This is a point of theological debate; here it is stated as the view of the majority.
3
Reflect on the implications
Think about why angels, despite being sinless, do not experience paradise. How does this affect our understanding of their role?
It emphasizes that paradise and vision are rewards for human obedience, not angelic nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وملائكته بأنهم عباد مكرمون لا يسبقونه بالقول وهم بأمره يعملون، وأنهم معصومون ولا يعصون الله ومنزهون عن صفة الذكورية ونعت الأنوثية وقد أنكر الله في كتابه على من قال: إنهم بنات الله حيث قال: ﴿وَجَعَلُوا الْمَلَائِكَةَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ عِبَادُ الرَّحْمَنِ إِنَاثًا أَشَهِدُوا خَلْقَهُمْ سَتُكْتَبُ شَهَادَتُهُمْ وَيُسْأَلُونَ﴾ [الزخرف: ١٩]، وقال أيضاً: ﴿أَصْطَفَى الْبَنَاتِ عَلَى الْبَنِينَ مَا لَكُمْ كَيْفَ تَحْكُمُونَ﴾ [الصافات: ١٥٣-١٥٤]. وذكر في "جواهر الأصول" أن الملائكة ليس لهم حظ من نعيم الجنان ولا من رؤية الرحمن، كذا في شرح القونوي لـ"عمدة النسفي" وذكر أيضاً أنهم أجسام لطيفة هوائية تقدر على التشكل بأشكال مختلفة أولو أجنحة مثنى وثلاث ورباع، مسكنهم السماوات أي مسكن معظمهم قال وهذا قول أكثر المسلمين.
And His angels: that they are honored servants, they do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command; and that they are infallible and do not disobey Allah, and are free from the attribute of masculinity and the description of femininity. And Allah denied in His Book those who say they are daughters of Allah, where He said: 'And they have made the angels, who are servants of the Merciful, females. Did they witness their creation? Their testimony will be recorded, and they will be questioned' [az-Zukhruf 19]. And He also said: 'Has He chosen daughters over sons? What is the matter with you? How do you judge?' [as-Saffat 153-154]. And it is mentioned in 'Jawahir al-Usul' that the angels have no share of the bliss of Paradise nor of the vision of the Merciful. Likewise in the commentary of al-Qunawi on 'Umdat an-Nasafi. And he also mentioned that they are subtle aerial bodies capable of assuming different forms, having wings in twos, threes, and fours. Their dwelling is the heavens, i.e., the dwelling of most of them. He said: And this is the saying of the majority of Muslims.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines the attributes of angels according to Sunni Islam. It begins by stating that angels are honored servants who do not precede Allah in speech and act by His command, emphasizing their servitude and obedience. It then asserts their infallibility (ismah) and their being free from human gender attributes, in refutation of those who consider them female offspring of God. Misconception & Correction

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do angels possess?
A) A share of Paradise's bliss.
B) The ability to see Allah.

D) Dense physical bodies like humans.

Angels are subtle aerial beings with wings who dwell in the heavens, and they have no part in paradise or seeing Allah because those are rewards for human obedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that angels, despite their constant worship, have no share in Paradise or in seeing Allah. This reward is reserved for humans who obey. Does your daily life reflect gratitude for this immense privilege? What is one thing you will change today to make your obedience more sincere?
?
Angels are subtle beings that can assume forms, yet they are always aware of their servitude. You, as a human, have been given a dense body and free will. Are you using your will to serve Allah as the angels do, or are you distracted by the very materiality that makes you human? Commit to one act of obedience today that will be recorded by the angels.
?
If the highest of creation—the angels—do not see Allah, how should you view the hope of seeing Him in the afterlife? Does this hope move you to purify your heart from sins that veil it? Reflect on one attachment you need to release to prepare for that vision, and take a concrete step to let it go today.

Resurrection After Death: Definition and Proof
Sanusi defines resurrection, provides two Quranic proofs, and declares it a necessary belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the exact meaning of resurrection in Islamic theology and the definitive proofs that establish it as a necessary belief.

Core Idea
Resurrection is the recreation of the original body, and denying it is clear disbelief.

Sanusi now turns to a central eschatological belief: resurrection after death. He clarifies what resurrection means—restoration after annihilation—and distinguishes it from other meanings of the term. He then presents the scriptural evidence that makes this belief a necessity of faith. As you read, notice how the passage moves from definition to proof to the consequence of denial.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of 'ba'th'
Read the Arabic phrase 'wa al-ba'th ay al-hayah ba'd al-mawt' and note how Sanusi qualifies it: it means restoration after annihilation of the initial form, not the sending of prophets.
This nuance prevents confusion.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
Look for the two Quranic verses cited. The first is from Surah al-Mu'minun, the second from Surah Ya-Sin. Reflect on how each verse directly affirms resurrection.
Sanusi says there are many other texts, but these are key.
3
Grasp the theological weight
Read the quotation from 'al-Maqasid': belief in al-hashr (gathering) is a necessary tenet; denial is clear disbelief. Understand why this makes resurrection a non-negotiable belief.
This is a strong statement about the boundary of faith.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
The passage implicitly refutes reincarnation: resurrection is not a new cycle but the re-creation of the original body after annihilation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبعث) أي الحياة (بعد الموت) قيد يفيد أن المراد به الإعادة بعد فناء هيئة البداية، لا بعث الأنبياء إلى الخلق وإن كان مما يجب الإيمان به أيضاً، ودليله قوله سبحانه وتعالى: ثُمَّ إِنَّكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيِّمَةِ تُبْعَثُونَ ﴾ [المؤمنون : ١٦] وقوله سبحانه: ﴿ قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِى اَنْشَاهَا أَوَلَ مَرَّةٍ ﴾ [يس: ٧٩]، إلى غير ذلك من النصوص القاطعة والأدلة اللامعة. قال في "المقاصد" وبالجملة فالإيمان بالحشر من ضروريات الدين وإنكاره كفر باليقين.
And the resurrection: meaning life after death. A qualification indicating that what is meant is restoration after the annihilation of the initial form, not the sending of prophets to the creation, although that is also necessarily believed in. Its proof is His saying, exalted: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be resurrected' [al-Mu'minun 16], and His saying: 'Say: He will give them life who created them the first time' [Ya-Sin 79], and other definitive texts and shining proofs. He said in 'al-Maqasid': 'In short, belief in the gathering is from the necessities of the religion, and its denial is manifest disbelief.'
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'resurrection after death' (al-ba'th ba'd al-mawt) as meaning the restoration of life after death, specifically the recreation of the initial bodily form after its annihilation. It distinguishes this from another meaning of 'ba'th' (sending prophets), though belief in that is also obligatory. It then provides two Quranic proofs: verse from al-Mu'minun promising resurrection on the Day of Resurrection, and verse from Ya-Sin affirming that God who created the first time can give life again. It notes that there are many other definitive texts and proofs. Finally, it quotes from al-Maqasid that belief in the gathering (al-hashr) is a necessary tenet of religion (min daruriyyat al-din), and denying it is clear disbelief (kufr bi al-yaqin).

Key Terms
بعث
إعادة
فناء هيئة البداية
حشر
ضروريات الدين
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection means reincarnation or metempsychosis into a new form.
Correction: The passage clarifies that resurrection is the restoration of the original body after its annihilation, not a cycle of rebirth.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the term 'resurrection after death' (al-ba'th ba'd al-mawt) specifically mean?
A) The sending of prophets to guide humanity.
B) The restoration of life after the annihilation of the initial bodily form.
C) The spiritual survival of the soul without a body.
D) The reincarnation of the soul into a new body.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection after death is a clearly defined, Quranically proven belief that is a necessary tenet of Islam; denying it is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The lesson says that denial of resurrection is manifest disbelief. Is there any part of you that secretly doubts or downplays this reality? What will you do to strengthen your certainty that you will be raised again exactly as you are?
?
God's argument is that He who created you the first time can surely recreate you. Does your daily life reflect that same confidence in God's power, or do you act as if this world is all that matters?
?
Resurrection means your very own body will be restored. If you truly believed that every deed you do will be faced with that same body on the Day of Judgment, would you change anything about how you live today?

The Objection of Metempsychosis and Its Core Refutation
Sanusi answers the objection that resurrection implies metempsychosis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in bodily resurrection does not entail metempsychosis, and how Sanusi distinguishes the two based on the concept of original parts.

Core Idea
Resurrection is not metempsychosis because the resurrected body is made from the original parts of the first.

Some critics claim that believing in bodily resurrection logically leads to metempsychosis, the transfer of souls between bodies. Sanusi addresses this objection head-on, clarifying that resurrection is fundamentally different: it involves re-creating the body from its original components, ensuring personal identity. In this lesson, we examine the objection and Sanusi's decisive answer.

Guided Path
1
Hear the objection
Read the objection including the hadith and Rumi's quote. Understand why someone might think resurrection is metempsychosis.
2
Find the answer
Read Sanusi's response that metempsychosis only follows if the second body is not from original parts. Note the distinction.
3
Define metempsychosis
Notice that Sanusi points out that real metempsychosis proponents deny the afterlife, so equating the two is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: هذا قول بالتناسخ وهو انتقال الروح من بدن إلى بدن فإن البدن الثاني ليس هو الأول، لما ورد في الحديث: ((إن أهل الجنة جرد مرد و إن الجهنمي ضرسه مثل أحد)). ولأجل هذا المعنى وهو أن القول بالمعاد وحشر الأجساد قول بالتناسخ، قال جلال الدين الرومي رحمه الله: «ما من مذهب إلا وللتناسخ فيه قدم راسخ». فالجواب: أنه إنما يلزم التناسخ لو لم يكن البدن الثاني مخلوقاً من الأجزاء الأصلية للبدن الأوّل وإن سمي مثل ذلك تناسخا كان نزاعا في مجرد الاسم وتحقيق الرسم على أن التناسخ عند أهله هو رد الأرواح إلى الأشباح في الدنيا لا في الأخرى، فإنهم ينكرون الجنة والنار وسائر أمور العقبى ولذا كفروا. لا يقال قوله تعالى: ﴿ كُلَّمَا نَضِجَتْ جُلُودُهُمْ بَدَّلْنَاهُمْ جُلُودًا غَيْرَهَا ﴾ [النساء: ٥٦] يفيد أن يكون المثاب والمعاقب باللذات الحسية والآلام الجسمية غير من عمل الطاعة وارتكب المعصية؛ لأنا نقول العبرة في ذلك بالإدراك، وإنما هو الروح ولو بواسطة الآلات، وهو باق بعينه، وكذا الأجزاء الأصلية من البدن ولذا يقال لمن رؤي حال من الصبا في الشيوخة: إنه هو بعينه وإن بدلت الصور والهيئات بل كثير من الأعضاء والآلات، ولا يقال لمن جنى في الشباب فعوقب في المشيب إنه عقوبة لغير الجاني، فكبر ضرس الكافر بمنزلة ورم أعضائه. وفي "شرح المواقف : الأجزاء الأصلية هي الأجزاء الباقية من أوّل العمر إلى آخره. قال بعض الأفاضل: الأجزاء الأصلية هي الأجزاء الحاصلة في أول الفطرة وهي وقت تعلق الأرواح بالأشباح.
Then it was said: This is a statement of metempsychosis, which is the transfer of the soul from one body to another, for the second body is not the first, due to the hadith: 'The people of Paradise are beardless, and the molar of the Hellfire dweller is like Uhud.' And for this meaning, that belief in the return and gathering of bodies is a belief in metempsychosis, Jalal al-Din al-Rumi said: 'There is no sect except that metempsychosis has a firm foot in it.' The answer: That metempsychosis would only be necessary if the second body were not created from the original parts of the first body. And if such a thing is called metempsychosis, it is a dispute merely over the name and a verification of definition, given that metempsychosis according to its proponents is the return of souls to bodies in this world, not in the Hereafter. For they deny Paradise, Hellfire, and all matters of the afterlife, and therefore they are disbelievers. It cannot be said that His saying: 'Whenever their skins are roasted, We replace them with other skins' [an-Nisa 56] implies that the one rewarded and punished with sensory pleasures and bodily pains is other than the one who performed obedience and committed disobedience; because we say: The consideration in that is perception, and it is the soul, even if through instruments, and it remains identical. Similarly, the original parts of the body remain. Hence, one who is seen from youth in old age is said to be the very same, even if forms and shapes, indeed many organs and instruments, have changed. And it is not said of one who committed a crime in youth and is punished in old age that it is a punishment of other than the criminal. Thus the enlargement of the disbeliever's molar is like the swelling of his limbs. And in 'Sharh al-Mawaqif': The original parts are the parts that remain from the beginning of life to its end. Some eminent scholars said: The original parts are the parts that occur at the beginning of creation, which is the time when souls attach to bodies.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an objection that belief in bodily resurrection (al-ma'ad wa hashr al-ajsad) amounts to metempsychosis (al-tanasukh). The objector cites a hadith about the appearance of resurrected bodies to argue that the second body is not identical to the first, and quotes Jalal al-Din al-Rumi's statement that metempsychosis has a foothold in every sect. The answer distinguishes resurrection from metempsychosis: in resurrection, the second body is created from the original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya) of the first body, ensuring continuity of identity. If such creation is called metempsychosis, it is merely a verbal dispute. The answer further clarifies that metempsychosis, as held by its proponents, involves the return of souls to bodies in this world, not the afterlife, and its proponents deny the afterlife entirely, making them disbelievers. The passage then addresses a potential counterargument from Quran 4:56, which speaks of replacing skins in Hell. The answer explains that the soul (al-ruh) remains identical, and the original bodily parts persist, so the same person is punished. It uses an analogy: a person seen from youth to old age is considered the same person despite bodily changes, just as a criminal punished in old age is the same criminal. Finally, it quotes from Sharh al-Mawaqif and some virtuous scholars defining the original parts as those remaining from the beginning of life or from the initial creation when souls attach to bodies.

Key Terms
تناسخ
أجزاء أصلية
معاد
حشر أجساد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believing in bodily resurrection implies believing in metempsychosis (transmigration of souls).
Correction: Resurrection differs crucially: the resurrected body is reassembled from the original parts of the deceased body, ensuring identity, and metempsychosis proponents deny the afterlife, which Muslims affirm.

Checkpoint
According to the answer in the passage, when would belief in resurrection entail metempsychosis?
A) If the second body is created from the original parts of the first.
B) If the second body is NOT created from the original parts of the first.
C) If the soul is transferred to a different species.
D) If the afterlife is denied.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection does not entail metempsychosis because the resurrected body uses the original parts, and metempsychosis is a worldly concept that denies the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about meeting Allah with a body made from the same parts as your current one, does that make you more accountable for how you use your body? What change must you make today?
?
Sanusi warns that metempsychosis proponents deny the afterlife. Is there any area of your belief where you subtly deny the reality of the Hereafter by your actions? What one action today can prove your belief in the resurrection?
?
The objector used a hadith about different physical descriptions in the Hereafter to argue against bodily identity. Do you ever use apparent differences between this world and the next to avoid taking resurrection seriously? How does Sanusi's answer (original parts) anchor your faith?

The Quranic Challenge and the Continuity of Personal Identity
Sanusi addresses the Quranic counter-argument and upholds personal identity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse about replacing skins in Hell does not contradict personal identity, and how the soul and original parts ensure continuity.

Core Idea
Even when bodies change, the soul and original parts remain, so the same person is rewarded or punished.

A potential objection arises from the Quranic verse that says the skins of the dwellers of Hell will be replaced. Does this mean a different person is punished? Sanusi responds by explaining that identity is tied to the soul and the original parts of the body. In this lesson, we examine this argument and the definition of original parts that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Consider the objection
Read the objection from Quran 4:56 and why it seems to imply a different person is punished.
2
Understand the answer
Sanusi's response that the soul remains identical, and the original parts persist, so the same person is punished.
3
Define original parts
Examine the quotes from Sharh al-Mawaqif and others defining the original parts as those from the beginning of life or creation.

Resurrection Requires Gathering All Original Parts
Defines resurrection as gathering original parts and refutes denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why resurrection necessarily involves gathering all original physical parts and how this refutes alternative views.

Core Idea
Resurrection is the reassembly of all original parts — no substitution, no omission.

This lesson addresses a key doctrine of the afterlife: the physical resurrection of the body. The author argues that true resurrection requires gathering all original parts from birth to death, not just any matter. This principle refutes those who deny bodily resurrection as a gathering of parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, then the English translation. Notice how the author states his claim and supports it.
The Arabic uses technical terms like الأجزاء الأصلية and الحشر.
2
Identify the main claim
Find the sentence that states the necessity of gathering original parts. It appears right after the opening phrase.
The claim is that resurrection is only by gathering parts from beginning to end.
3
Understand the refutation
See how the author uses this principle to refute those who deny resurrection as gathering parts. The phrase 'falls' (سقط) indicates the refutation.
4
Examine the supporting evidence
The author mentions specific parts like foreskin, nails, hair, teeth as examples of what will be restored. Think about why these examples are chosen.
These are parts usually considered disposable but are still restored.
5
Reflect on divine will
Note that after gathering, Allah preserves or annihilates parts according to His will. This shows His sovereignty over the resurrected body.
The will applies to quantity, quality, and form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبما ذكرنا من اعتبار الأجزاء الأصلية في الحشر سقط ما قالوا في نفي الحشر بمعنى جمع الأجزاء أيضاً، على أن الحشر أولاً لا يكون إلا بجمع الأجزاء من أول العمر إلى آخره، وتحقيقا لمعنى الإعادة، كما ورد أنه سبحانه وتعالى يعيد القُلفَة والأجزاء المقطعة من الظفر والشعر والأجزاء المقلعة من السن وأمثال ذلك، ثم إنه سبحانه وتعالى يُبقي ما أراده ويعدم ما أراده على ما تعلقت به المشيئة في الكمية والكيفية والهيئة.
And by what we mentioned of considering the original parts in the resurrection, what they said in denying the resurrection in the sense of gathering the parts also falls; that the resurrection first is only by gathering the parts from the beginning of life to its end, and a realization of the meaning of re-creation, as it has come that He, glorified and exalted, returns the foreskin and the cut parts of the nail and hair and the extracted parts of the tooth and the like of that; then He, glorified and exalted, preserves what He wills and annihilates what He wills according to what the will has attached to in quantity, quality, and form.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage argues for the necessity of gathering all original physical parts in resurrection. The author states that by affirming the role of original parts, the arguments of those who deny resurrection as a gathering of parts are refuted. Resurrection necessarily involves reassembling all parts from the beginning to the end of one's life, fulfilling the true meaning of re-creation. Evidence is provided from transmitted reports that Allah will restore even small parts like the foreskin, nail clippings, hair, extracted teeth, etc. Additionally, Allah retains or annihilates parts as His will determines in terms of quantity, quality, and form, emphasizing divine sovereignty over the resurrected body.

Key Terms

الحشر
الإعادة
المشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is impossible for Allah to gather parts.
B) The original parts must be gathered to truly realize re-creation.
C) Resurrection is only spiritual, not physical.
D) The will of Allah is irrelevant to the form of resurrection.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection meaningfully requires the gathering of the very parts each person had in life, not merely any matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every part of your body—every hair, every nail, every cell—will be gathered and returned to you on the Day of Resurrection? How does this belief affect the way you treat your body now, in terms of purity, modesty, and gratitude? What would change in your daily habits if you lived with this awareness?
?
If nothing is lost or substituted in your resurrection, and every original part of you testifies to your deeds, what does that mean for the sins you commit in secret or the parts of your body you use in disobedience? Will you still be able to claim ignorance or forgetfulness when your own toenails and hair follicles are brought back to witness?
?
Imagine your body—the same hair, the same nails, the same foreskin—is reassembled and then shaped by Allah’s will. Are you prepared to face Him with that exact, unaltered body, the body that performed every action of your life? What change must you begin today so that, on that day, the gathering brings you joy rather than dread?

Resurrection of All Beings: The General Rule
Lists beings resurrected based on transmitted reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah resurrects all categories of beings—including the insane, children, jinn, devils, and animals—based on transmitted reports, and that this is a matter of sam'iyyat (text-based knowledge).

Core Idea
All beings, regardless of intellect or species, will be raised.

Before discussing the specific case of the miscarried fetus, Imam Abu Hanifa's creed affirms that Allah resurrects all categories of created beings. This includes not only rational humans but also the insane, children, jinn, devils, and even animals and insects. The basis for this is not rational argument but rather the reports (akhbar) transmitted in revelation. Let us examine the passage that establishes this foundational truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the first sentence
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice the comprehensive list: المجانين، الصبيان، الجن، الشياطين، البهائم، الحشرات، الطيور.
2
Understand the basis
The reason given is 'للأخبار الواردة في ذلك' (due to the reports). This indicates that resurrection of these beings is a matter of sam'iyyat (textual knowledge), not rational deduction.
Contrast this with rational proofs for resurrection of humans.
3
Connect to the next section
The author then moves to a specific question (the miscarried fetus), showing that although the general rule is clear, there are details requiring further examination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه سبحانه وتعالى كما العقلاء يحيي المجانين والصبيان والجن والشياطين والبهائم والحشرات والطيور للأخبار الواردة في ذلك. وأما السقط الذي لم تتم أعضاؤه هل يحشر؟ فروي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه إذا نفخ فيه الروح يحشر وإلا فلا، وهو الظاهر؛ لأن المذهب المختار عند الأبرار هو الحشر المركب من الروح والجسد. وقول القونوي: والذي يقتضي مذهب علمائنا أنه إذا كان استبان بعض خلقه يحشر وهو قول الشعبي وابن سيرين مدفوع بأن هذا الحكم حكم فقهي يترتب عليه بعض الأمور الدنيوية ولا تقاس عليه الأحوال الأخروية.
Then know that He, glorified and exalted, like the intellectual beings, gives life to the insane, children, jinn, devils, animals, insects, and birds, due to the reports transmitted concerning that. As for the miscarried fetus whose limbs are not complete, will it be resurrected? It is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that if the spirit was blown into it, it is resurrected, otherwise not, and that is apparent; because the chosen doctrine among the pious is the resurrection composed of spirit and body. And the statement of al-Qunawi: 'What the doctrine of our scholars necessitates is that if some of its creation became apparent, it is resurrected, and that is the saying of al-Sha'bi and Ibn Sirin' is rejected because this ruling is a juristic ruling pertaining to some worldly matters, and eschatological states are not analogized to it.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage declares that Allah resurrects all categories of beings: the insane, children, jinn, devils, animals, insects, and birds, based on transmitted reports. It then addresses a specific question: whether a miscarried fetus that did not develop complete limbs is resurrected. Two views are presented: a narration from Abu Hanifa states that resurrection occurs only if the spirit was breathed into it; otherwise not. This is described as the apparent position because the chosen doctrine is a resurrection composed of both spirit and body. Al-Qunawi's opinion, supported by al-Sha'bi and Ibn Sirin, argues that if some parts of the fetus became distinct, it is resurrected. The author rejects this, explaining that such a ruling is a juristic (fiqh) ruling pertaining to worldly matters and cannot be analogized to eschatological conditions, which operate on different principles.

Key Terms
الحشر
المجانين
الصبيان
الجن
الشياطين
البهائم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only rational humans will be resurrected.
Correction: The passage asserts that all beings, including animals, jinn, and children, are resurrected based on textual reports.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the resurrection of the beings listed?
A) Rational deduction
B) Transmitted reports
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Personal opinion

Key Takeaway
All categories of created beings—insane, children, jinn, devils, animals, insects, and birds—will be resurrected based on revealed reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The resurrection includes every creature—even the smallest insect. Do you truly live with the awareness that you will meet Allah, and that every being will be brought back? How would your daily actions change if this certainty filled your heart? Commit to one habit this week that reminds you of the Day of Resurrection.
?
You share the reality of resurrection with jinn, devils, and animals. Do you treat Allah's creatures—whether humans, animals, or jinn—with the respect due to beings that will be held accountable? Write down one specific way you can improve your treatment of Allah's creation, starting today.
?
If you believed that every being you encounter—the insane, children, animals, and even the smallest insect—will be resurrected, how would that change your compassion and sense of responsibility toward them? Name one creature you saw today and resolve to treat it with the honor it will have on that Day.

The Miscarried Fetus: When is it Resurrected?
Debates resurrection of miscarried fetus based on spirit or limb formation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate regarding the resurrection of a miscarried fetus with incomplete limbs, and the difference between juristic rulings on fetal development and eschatological resurrection.

Core Idea
Resurrection of the fetus depends on the spirit being blown into it.

After establishing the general resurrection of all beings, the passage delves into a specific case: the miscarried fetus (السقط) whose limbs were not fully formed. Does it rise on Judgment Day? The answer is not straightforward, and there are differing opinions among scholars. This lesson explores the narration from Abu Hanifa and the rebuttal of al-Qunawi's view, highlighting a key distinction between worldly juristic principles and the rules of the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question
Read the Arabic passage and note the question: 'السقط الذي لم تتم أعضاؤه هل يحشر؟' (the miscarried fetus whose limbs are not complete, will it be resurrected?).
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's view
The narration from Abu Hanifa says resurrection occurs if the spirit was blown in; otherwise not. Reflect on why spirit is the criterion.
The author calls this 'الظاهر' (the apparent view).
3
Understand the rejection of al-Qunawi
Al-Qunawi argued that if some parts are distinct, the fetus is resurrected. The author rejects this by distinguishing fiqhi (juristic) rulings for this world from eschatological matters (الأحوال الأخروية).
Find the phrase 'حكم فقهي' and understand its implication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه سبحانه وتعالى كما العقلاء يحيي المجانين والصبيان والجن والشياطين والبهائم والحشرات والطيور للأخبار الواردة في ذلك. وأما السقط الذي لم تتم أعضاؤه هل يحشر؟ فروي عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه إذا نفخ فيه الروح يحشر وإلا فلا، وهو الظاهر؛ لأن المذهب المختار عند الأبرار هو الحشر المركب من الروح والجسد. وقول القونوي: والذي يقتضي مذهب علمائنا أنه إذا كان استبان بعض خلقه يحشر وهو قول الشعبي وابن سيرين مدفوع بأن هذا الحكم حكم فقهي يترتب عليه بعض الأمور الدنيوية ولا تقاس عليه الأحوال الأخروية.
Then know that He, glorified and exalted, like the intellectual beings, gives life to the insane, children, jinn, devils, animals, insects, and birds, due to the reports transmitted concerning that. As for the miscarried fetus whose limbs are not complete, will it be resurrected? It is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that if the spirit was blown into it, it is resurrected, otherwise not, and that is apparent; because the chosen doctrine among the pious is the resurrection composed of spirit and body. And the statement of al-Qunawi: 'What the doctrine of our scholars necessitates is that if some of its creation became apparent, it is resurrected, and that is the saying of al-Sha'bi and Ibn Sirin' is rejected because this ruling is a juristic ruling pertaining to some worldly matters, and eschatological states are not analogized to it.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage declares that Allah resurrects all categories of beings: the insane, children, jinn, devils, animals, insects, and birds, based on transmitted reports. It then addresses a specific question: whether a miscarried fetus that did not develop complete limbs is resurrected. Two views are presented: a narration from Abu Hanifa states that resurrection occurs only if the spirit was breathed into it; otherwise not. This is described as the apparent position because the chosen doctrine is a resurrection composed of both spirit and body. Al-Qunawi's opinion, supported by al-Sha'bi and Ibn Sirin, argues that if some parts of the fetus became distinct, it is resurrected. The author rejects this, explaining that such a ruling is a juristic (fiqh) ruling pertaining to worldly matters and cannot be analogized to eschatological conditions, which operate on different principles.

Key Terms

الروح
الجسد
الأخبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A miscarried fetus that shows some development of limbs is resurrected because worldly fiqh considers it as a complete being.
Correction: According to the author, the criterion for resurrection is the presence of the spirit, not limb formation, and worldly juristic rulings cannot be analogized to eschatological states.

Checkpoint

A) If it has developed limbs
B) If the spirit was blown into it
C) If it was born alive
D) Always resurrected

Key Takeaway
The resurrection of a miscarried fetus depends on the breathing of the spirit, and worldly juristic rulings cannot be used to deduce rules of the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson distinguishes between worldly judgments and the reality of the afterlife. Are there areas in your life where you are more concerned with outward appearances (like physical development) than with what God sees—the presence of the spirit?
?
The resurrection of a miscarried fetus depends on the spirit, not on worldly criteria. Does your certainty about your own resurrection rest on your deeds and outward piety, or on the gift of the spirit God breathed into you?
?
The author rejects analogy from this world to the next. Are you guilty of projecting worldly expectations onto God's mercy and justice, rather than accepting His revealed standards for the afterlife?

The Afterlife in Fiqh al-Akbar: Understanding the Imam's Statements
Commentary on the Imam's mention of the afterlife and resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the commentator's explanation of the Imam's statements about the afterlife, including the variant reading that connects the Last Day with resurrection after death and the two possible interpretations of that resurrection.

Core Idea
The Imam's words on the afterlife are rich with meaning, inviting careful study.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the Imam's concise statements about the afterlife. He points out a variant reading that links the Last Day with resurrection after death, leading to two possible interpretations. The commentator also reveals the Imam's pedagogical strategy of summarizing first and detailing later. By understanding this, you will appreciate the depth and precision of the Imam's teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage twice

The commentator explains that the Imam summarized at the beginning to alert the reader to what will be detailed later. Consider how this teaching method helps the reader.
This shows the Imam's systematic approach.

Qira'at and Divine Speech: When Two Readings Become Two Verses
Classification of variant readings based on meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the recitation of multiple readings relates to the divine speech according to this passage.

Core Idea
When readings differ in meaning, both are spoken by Allah; when identical, one is spoken but both permitted.

This lesson examines a subtle theological question: when we have two variant readings (qira'at) of a single Quranic verse, does that mean Allah spoke both? The answer depends on whether the meanings differ. If different meanings, both are revealed as separate divine utterances; if the meaning is the same, only one is originally spoken but a license is given to recite both.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if... then...'
2
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two cases based on whether the readings have different or same meaning. Find each case and its ruling.
The key terms are 'قراءتان' and 'آيتين'.
3
Understand the reasoning
Ask yourself why the author distinguishes based on meaning. The commentary explains: each distinct meaning corresponds to a distinct divine utterance, preserving the unity of speech when meaning is shared.
This connects to the broader principle that divine speech is one in essence.
4
Reflect on the license
Notice that in the second case, Allah gave a license (rukhkhas) to recite both despite only one being spoken. Consider how this shows divine flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا كان في الآية قراءتان، فإن كان لكل قراءة معنى غير الأخرى، فالله تعالى تكلم بهما جميعا وصارت القراءتان بمنزلة الآيتين وإن كانت القراءتان معناهما واحد فالله تعالى تكلم بأحدهما ورخص بأن يقرأ بهما جميعا كما ذكره الفقيه أبو الليث.
As for when there are two readings (qira'atan) in a verse, if each reading has a meaning different from the other, then Allah, Exalted, spoke them both, and the two readings become like two verses. And if the two readings have one meaning, then Allah, Exalted, spoke with one of them and gave license (rukhkhas) that both be recited, as mentioned by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage addresses a theological issue regarding the qira'at (variant readings of the Qur'an). The author presents the view that when two readings of the same verse have different meanings, God actually spoke both readings, and they are effectively like two distinct verses. However, if the readings share the same underlying meaning, then God only spoke one of them, but He permitted the recitation of both for ease. This is attributed to the Hanafi scholar Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi. The reasoning maintains that the eternal speech is one, but its expressions can vary with divine permission.

Key Terms
قراءتان
آيتين
رخص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All variant readings are equally the direct word of God regardless of meaning.
Correction: According to this passage, only when readings differ in meaning are both considered spoken by Allah; when meanings are the same, only one is the original speech, though both may be recited with permission.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when two qira'at have different meanings?
A) Only one is valid
B) Both are spoken and are like two verses
C) Neither is from Allah
D) The later abrogates the earlier

Key Takeaway
The status of variant readings depends on whether their meanings differ: if different, both are divine speech; if same, only one is but both are permitted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you reflect on the fact that even when two readings have the same meaning, both are permitted as a mercy? How does this affect your reverence for each word?

The passage teaches that some readings are spoken by Allah even if they differ. Do you treat each qira'ah as a divine revelation, or do you favor one over the other? What would change if you truly believed each is from Allah?
?

Why the Torah and Quran Are Called Allah's Speech
The author explains the principle of attribution: revealed books are called Allah's speech because He originated their meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the revealed books (Torah and Quran) are called Allah's speech, based on the principle that Allah is the originator of their composition.

Core Idea
Revealed books are Allah's speech because He originated their composition.

The Qur'an and Torah are made of human language and writing, yet Muslims call them Allah's speech. How can that be? In this passage, the author explains the key principle of attribution: what matters is who originated the composition, not the physical medium. This is illustrated with the analogy of hadith: you say a hadith is the Prophet's speech because he originated its words.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of attribution
Read the passage and notice that it connects the Torah and Quran to Allah by saying 'mabda' nazmiha' (originator of their composition). This is the key concept.
2
Analyze the hadith analogy
The author compares revealed books to hadith: when you recite a hadith, you attribute it to the Prophet because he originated its wording. Similarly, Allah originated the wording of the revealed books.
This analogy helps clarify the logic of attribution.
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites two verses where Allah's speech is referred to. Note how these verses support the attribution of the recited text to Allah.
The verses show that even the recitation of these books can be called hearing Allah's speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما يقال : المنظوم العبراني الذي هو التوراة والمنظوم العربي الذي هو القرآن كلامه سبحانه؛ لأن كلماتهما وآياتهما أدلة كلامه وعلامات مرامه، ولأن مبدأ نظمها الله تعالى ألا ترى أنك إذا قرأت حديثا من الأحاديث قلت هذا الذي قرأته وذكرته ليس قولي من بل قول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم؛ لأن مبدأ نظم ذلك القول من الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام. ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿ أَفَتَطَعُونَ أَن يُؤْمِنُوا لَكُمْ وَقَدْ كَانَ فَرِيقٌ مِنْهُمْ يَسْمَعُونَ كَلمَ اللهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ٧٥] ، وقوله عزوجل: ﴿وَإِنْ أَحَدٌ مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِينَ اسْتَجَارَكَ فَاجِرَهُ حَتَّى يَسْمَعَ كَلمَ اللهِ ثُمَّ ابْلِغْهُ مَأْمَنَهُ ﴾ [التوبة : ٦]
And it is only said: the Hebrew composition which is the Torah and the Arabic composition which is the Quran are His speech, Glorified; because their words and verses are evidences of His speech and signs of His intent, and because Allah Most High is the originator of their composition. Do you not see that when you read a hadith from among the ahadith, you say: 'This that I have read and mentioned is not my saying but the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him)' because the originator of the composition of that saying is the Messenger (peace be upon him). And from this is His statement: 'Do you hope that they will believe you when a party of them used to hear the word of Allah?' [al-Baqara 75], and His statement: 'And if anyone of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection so that he may hear the word of Allah, then convey him to his place of safety' [al-Tawba 6].
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage provides the reasoning for why created, physical books (Torah and Quran) are called the speech of Allah. The author draws an analogy: when you recite a hadith, you say it is the speech of the Prophet, not yours, because the originator of its wording (mabda' nazm) is the Prophet. Similarly, the words and verses of the Torah and Quran are evidences (adilla) and signs ('alamat) of Allah's speech, but the ultimate originator of their composition (mabda' nazmiha) is Allah Himself. Therefore, they are attributed to Allah as His speech. Two Quranic verses are cited where the Jews heard 'the word of Allah' (kalam Allah) and where polytheists are to be allowed to hear 'the word of Allah', supporting the attribution of the revealed text to Allah.

Key Terms
منظوم عبراني
منظوم عربي
مبدأ نظم
كلم الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the created letters and sounds of the Quran cannot be called Allah's speech because they are physical and temporal.
Correction: The passage explains that the Quran is called Allah's speech because He is the originator of its composition (mabda' nazmiha), not because the physical words are eternal or uncreated. The attribution is based on origin, not substance.

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a miracle.
B) Because Allah is the originator of its composition.
C) Because the Prophet recited it.
D) Because it is old.

Key Takeaway
The attribution of the Quran to Allah as His speech is based on Him being the originator of its composition, not on the physical medium of the words.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Evaluating the Hadith on the Createdness of the Quran
The author evaluates and interprets a hadith on takfir for saying the Quran is created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the hadith threatening takfir for saying 'the Quran is created' is not reliably attributed and how it can be interpreted consistently with Sunni belief.

Core Idea
The hadith against calling the Quran 'created' is weak and actually targets those who call it 'fabricated'.

This short passage from the sharh examines a hadith sometimes used to condemn those who say the Quran is created. The author finds it unauthentic, and even if considered, provides a plausible interpretation that defuses the threat. Let's see how the author handles this potentially divisive report.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author's two-part critique: first regarding authenticity, then regarding interpretation.
The passage is concise; each sentence carries weight.
2
Understand the authenticity ruling
The author declares the hadith 'ghayr thabit' (not established). Moreover, it is a solitary (ahad) report, which in creedal matters does not furnish certainty.
This is a methodological point: ahad hadith cannot establish beliefs.
3
Analyze the interpretive option
The author suggests that 'makhluq' in the hadith could mean 'mukhtalaq' (fabricated), i.e., that the person is saying the Quran is invented by humans. This interpretation removes the apparent contradiction with the Sunni position on the Quran's verbal nature.
Notice how this protects the consensus without rejecting the hadith outright.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حديث من قال: إن القرآن مخلوق فقد كفر)). (۱) فغير ثابت، مع أنه من الآحاد وقابل للتأويل في بيان المراد، والقول بأن المراد بالمخلوق المختلق بمعنى المفترى.
And as for the hadith: 'Whoever says: the Quran is created has disbelieved' – it is not established, and moreover it is a solitary (ahad) hadith and is open to interpretation in clarifying the intended meaning, and the saying that what is meant by 'created' (makhluq) is 'fabricated' (mukhtalaq) in the sense of 'invented' (muftara).
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage critically examines a hadith that is sometimes used to anathematize those who say the Quran is created. The author judges the hadith as not authentic (ghayr thabit). Even if considered, it is a solitary (ahad) report, which in matters of belief does not yield certainty. Moreover, the hadith can be interpreted: the word 'makhluq' (created) might be understood as 'mukhtalaq' (fabricated), i.e., the claim that the Quran is a human invention. Thus, the hadith would be condemning those who say the Quran is fabricated, not those who say it is created as an attribute. This nuanced interpretation protects the consensus of Ahl al-Sunna that the verbal Quran is not uncreated in its physical form.

Key Terms
حديث
مخلوق
مختلق
آحاد
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Muslims believe that any mention of the Quran being 'created' is an act of disbelief, citing this hadith.
Correction: The hadith is not authentic, and even if considered, it likely refers to calling the Quran 'fabricated' (mukhtalaq), not affirming its created attribute.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the word 'makhluq' in the hadith 'Whoever says the Quran is makhluq has disbelieved'?
A) As 'created' in the sense of temporal.
B) As 'fabricated' or 'invented'.
C) As 'perfect'.
D) As 'eternal'.

Key Takeaway
The hadith threatening takfir is unreliable and can be interpreted to refer to calling the Quran fabricated, not created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The author offers an interpretation to avoid takfir. Do you seek to find charitable interpretations of difficult texts, or do you rush to condemn? What change do you need to make in your heart?

The Greatest Bliss of Paradise: Seeing God and Hearing His Speech
The author describes seeing God's face and hearing His speech as the greatest bliss of Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why seeing God's face and hearing His speech is considered the greatest bliss of Paradise, and how the deprivation of these blessings is the ultimate punishment for disbelievers.

Core Idea
The greatest joy of Paradise is seeing Allah and hearing His speech; denial of that denies Paradise's essence.

In this passage, the author discusses the highest reward for the people of Paradise: the vision of Allah's face and the hearing of His speech. He warns that denying this blessing is to deny the very spirit of Paradise, as its delight is incomplete without it. He then contrasts this with the punishment of the disbelievers, who are deprived of Allah's speech and veiled from Him, supporting his argument with three Quranic verses. This lesson will help you grasp the centrality of divine communication and vision in Islamic eschatology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the strong opening statement and the contrasting description of punishment. Pay attention to the Quranic citations.
The passage is short but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the main claim and its support
The author claims that seeing God's face and hearing His speech is the best bliss. He supports this by saying that denying it denies the spirit of Paradise, and then contrasts with the punishment of disbelievers using three verses.
Contrast is a key rhetorical device here.
3
Examine the three Quranic verses
Read each verse cited: al-Baqarah 2:174, al-Mu'minun 23:108, and al-Mutaffifin 83:15. Understand how they describe the disbelievers' punishment—deprivation of speech and veiling.
The first verse is about not being spoken to, the second about being despised and not speaking, the third about being veiled.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Consider why seeing and speaking with God is the ultimate joy. This connects to the broader theological principle that the highest reward is loving and knowing God directly.
This counters any doubt about the possibility of seeing God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أفضل نعيم الجنة رؤية وجهه وسماع كلامه، فإنكار ذلك إنكار لروح الجنة الذي ما طابت لأهلها إلا به، كما أن أشد العذاب للكفار عدم تكليمه لهم ووقوع الحجاب كما أخبر عنهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يُكَلِّمُهُمُ اللهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ [البقرة : ١٧٤] . أي تكليم تكريم، وقال في آية : أخرى لهم: ﴿وَاخْسَوافِيهَا وَلَا تُكَلِّمُونِ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ۱۰۸] ، وبقوله تعالى: كَلَّا إِنَّهُمْ عَنْ رَّبِّهِمْ يَوْمَةٍ تَمَحْجُوبُونَ ﴾ [المطففين: ١٥ ] .
The best bliss of Paradise is seeing His face and hearing His speech. Denying that is denying the spirit of Paradise, which is not delightful to its inhabitants except by it. Likewise, the most severe punishment for the disbelievers is His not speaking to them and the occurrence of the veil, as He informed about them in His statement: 'And Allah will not speak to them on the Day of Resurrection' (al-Baqarah 2:174) – that is, a speech of honor. And He said in another verse to them: 'Be despised therein and do not speak to Me' (al-Mu'minun 23:108), and by His statement: 'No! Indeed, they will be veiled from their Lord on that Day' (al-Mutaffifin 83:15).
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a statement about the highest reward in Paradise: seeing God's face and hearing His speech. The author asserts that denying this is denying the very spirit of Paradise, because the joy of Paradise is incomplete without it. He contrasts this with the punishment of the disbelievers: they will be deprived of God's speech and will be veiled from Him. He cites three Quranic verses: the first from al-Baqarah says Allah will not speak to them on the Day of Resurrection, which he interprets as a speech of honor (takrīm). The second from al-Mu'minun says 'be despised and do not speak to Me,' referring to the punishment of the dwellers of Hell. The third from al-Mutaffifin states that they will be veiled from their Lord. Thus, the greatest blessing is the opposite: seeing and conversing with God.

Misconception: Some people might think that seeing God is impossible or that the greatest joy of Paradise is merely physical pleasures like gardens and rivers.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the greatest bliss is seeing God's face and hearing His speech, and that denying this denies the spirit of Paradise. This is supported by Quranic evidence about the punishment of disbelievers being veiled and not spoken to.

?

What one change will you make this week to ensure you are not among the veiled?
?

Will you repent and affirm this truth with your heart and tongue?

The Greatest Bliss: Vision of Allah and Hearing His Speech
Refutes denial of beatific vision and hearing Allah's speech in Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the vision of Allah and hearing His speech are considered the greatest bliss of Paradise, and how denying them contradicts the clear Quranic texts.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah and hearing His speech are the very spirit of Paradise.

The author of our text makes a bold claim: the best thing about Paradise is not its physical delights, but the vision of Allah's face and hearing His speech. He argues that denying these blessings would strip Paradise of its essence. This lesson unpacks that claim and examines the Quranic evidence he provides.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the strong language: 'the spirit of Paradise'.
2
Identify the two essential blessings
The author identifies two elements as the greatest bliss: vision of Allah's face and hearing His speech. Why are these so central?
3
Contrast with the punishment of disbelievers
The author contrasts the bliss of believers with the punishment of disbelievers: being veiled from Allah and not spoken to. This highlights the importance of these blessings.
The worst punishment is the opposite of the greatest bliss.
4
Examine the three Quranic proofs
Read each verse cited and see how it supports the author's claim. Verses about not speaking (2:174, 23:108) and being veiled (83:15).
Note the interpretation 'speech of honor' for 2:174.
5
Reflect on the doctrinal significance
Consider why this teaching matters for Islamic faith. It affirms the literal reality of these eschatological experiences.
This counters metaphorical interpretations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أفضل نعيم الجنة رؤية وجهه وسماع كلامه، فإنكار ذلك إنكار لروح الجنة الذي ما طابت لأهلها إلا به، كما أن أشد العذاب للكفار عدم تكليمه لهم ووقوع الحجاب كما أخبر عنهم بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا يُكَلِّمُهُمُ اللَّهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٧٤] أي تكليم تكريم، وقال في آية أخرى لهم: ﴿وَاخْسَؤُوا فِيهَا وَلَا تُكَلِّمُونِ ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١٠٨]، وبقوله تعالى: ﴿كَلَّا إِنَّهُمْ عَنْ رَبِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ لَمَحْجُوبُونَ ﴾ [المطففين: ١٥].
The best bliss of Paradise is the vision of His face and hearing His speech. Denying that is denying the spirit of Paradise, which is not pleasant for its people except through it. Indeed, from their Lord that Day they will be veiled' (83:15).
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage affirms two delights of Paradise: the vision of Allah's face (ru'ya) and hearing His speech (kalam). It states that denying these is denying the very essence (ruh) of Paradise, which only becomes delightful through them. Conversely, the worst punishment for disbelievers is being denied both: Allah will not speak to them honorably and they will be veiled from seeing Him. The author supports this with three verses: one stating Allah will not speak to certain people on Judgment Day (interpreted as a speech of honor, not general speech), another where the damned are told not to speak to Allah, and a third clearly stating that on that day they will be veiled from their Lord. The passage thus establishes the reality of these eschatological blessings.

تكليم تكريم
حجاب
نعيم الجنة

Misconception: Some claim beatific vision is metaphorical and not literal.
Correction: This passage treats the vision and speech as literal, real blessings, and their denial is likened to denying the spirit of Paradise.

Checkpoint

A) Palaces and rivers
B) Vision of Allah's face and hearing His speech
C) Eternal life without death
D) Meeting the prophets

Key Takeaway

The Uncreatedness of the Quran: Consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah
Affirms unanimous agreement that Quran is uncreated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all Ahl al-Sunnah, from the four schools and the early and later generations, agree that the Quran is uncreated.

Core Idea
The Quran is not created; this is the unanimous position of Ahl al-Sunnah.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary summarizes a foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunnah. Before delving into later theological disputes, we must first grasp the non-negotiable agreement that the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah. Let us see how this consensus is described.

Guided Path
1
Read the consensus statement
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the inclusive language: 'Ahl al-Sunnah, all of them... agree'.
The phrase 'من أهل المذاهب الأربعة وغيرهم' emphasizes universality.
2
Identify the key terms
Note the term 'القرآن غير مخلوق' (the Quran is uncreated). This is the central point.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this agreement is important. It distinguishes Ahl al-Sunnah from those who say the Quran is created.
This consensus is a touchstone of orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة فأهل السنّة كلهم من أهل المذاهب الأربعة وغيرهم من السلف والخلف متفقون : على أن القرآن غير مخلوق، ولكن بعد ذلك تنازع المتأخرون في أن كلام الله هل هو معنى واحد قائم بالذات أو أنه حروف وأصوات تكلم الله بعد أن لم يكن متكلما أو أنه لم يزل متكلما إذا شاء ومتى شاء وكيف شاء، وأنّ نوع الكلام قديم، وهو مختار الإمام والطحاوي، والنزاع بين أهل القبلة إنما هو في كونه مخلوقا خلقه الله أو هو كلامه الذي تكلم به وقام بذاته.
And in summary, Ahl al-Sunnah, all of them from the people of the four schools and others from the Salaf and Khalaf, agree that the Quran is uncreated. But after that, the later scholars disputed concerning the speech of God: is it one meaning subsisting in the essence, or is it letters and sounds with which God spoke after having not been speaking, or that He has not ceased to speak when He wills, whenever He wills, and however He wills, and that the type of speech is eternal, and this is the choice of al-Imam and al-Tahawi. And the dispute among the people of the qibla is only concerning whether it is created which God created, or it is His speech with which He spoke and which subsists in His essence.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a classification and summary of the Ahl al-Sunnah position on the Quran and the subsequent dispute about the nature of God's speech. It first affirms the unanimous agreement of Ahl al-Sunnah from all schools and generations that the Quran is not created. Then it notes that later scholars differed on how to understand God's speech: whether it is a single meaning subsisting in the divine essence, or letters and sounds indicating that God spoke after a time of not speaking, or that He has always been speaking whenever He wills. The author indicates that the view that the type of speech is eternal is the choice of Abu Hanifa and al-Tahawi. He concludes by stating that the real point of contention among Muslims is only whether the speech is created by God or is His own speech subsisting in His essence.

Key Terms
القرآن غير مخلوق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think there is a dispute among Ahl al-Sunnah about whether the Quran is created.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that all Ahl al-Sunnah agree it is uncreated. The later disputes are about the nature of God's speech, not about creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who agrees that the Quran is uncreated?
A) Only the four schools
B) Only the Salaf
C) All Ahl al-Sunnah from the four schools and others
D) Only the later scholars

Key Takeaway
The uncreatedness of the Quran is a unanimous belief of all Ahl al-Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe the Quran is not created, or do you sometimes treat it as merely a human text? In what ways does your daily interaction with the Quran reflect your belief in its uncreatedness? Commit to one specific change in how you approach the Quran from today.
?
If the Quran is the uncreated speech of Allah, what does that demand of you when you recite it, listen to it, or even hold it? Are you giving it the reverence it deserves? What would it cost you to treat every verse as the very words of your Creator?
?
This lesson says all Ahl al-Sunnah agree the Quran is uncreated. Is your heart at peace with that truth, or do you harbour doubts? Search yourself: do you accept it as a matter of faith, or do you intellectually reject it? If you find any resistance, bring that to Allah in sincere supplication.

The Dispute on the Nature of Divine Speech
Lists later disputes on nature of God's speech and concludes with real issue

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunnah agree the Quran is uncreated but differ on how to understand God's speech.

Having established the consensus on the uncreatedness of the Quran, we now turn to the subtler theological debate among later scholars about the nature of God's attribute of speech. The passage mentions three positions and singles out the view that the type of speech is eternal, which was chosen by Abu Hanifa and al-Tahawi.
