Three Later Positions on Ta'wil
Survey of three later scholars' views on ta'wil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct positions on ta'wil held by later scholars: prohibition, conditional acceptance, and context-based permissibility.

Core Idea
Later scholars disagreed on ta'wil: prohibition, conditional acceptance, or context-based need.

After covering the positions of the early generations (Salaf) and the Khalaf, the author now presents the views of three influential later scholars—Imam al-Haramayn, Ibn Daqiq al-'Id, and Ibn al-Humann. Their positions range from absolute prohibition to nuanced conditional acceptance, showing that the issue of ta'wil is not black and white. This passage helps us appreciate the spectrum of scholarly opinion within the broader Sunni tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a sense of the content. Notice the sequence of scholars mentioned.
The passage begins by referencing earlier interpretations before focusing on the three scholars.
2
Identify the three positions
As you read, extract the specific ruling on ta'wil for each scholar: what did Imam al-Haramayn ultimately say? What condition did Ibn Daqiq al-'Id place? How did Ibn al-Humann distinguish between contexts?
Write them down: 1) Prohibition, 2) Conditional acceptance (close vs. far meaning), 3) Need-based permissibility.
3
Compare each position with the Maturidi stance
Note that the passage explicitly aligns Imam al-Haramayn's final position with the Maturidi school. Consider how the other positions relate to this mainstream view.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Many people think ta'wil is either always allowed or always prohibited. This passage shows a spectrum. Think about how these nuanced views help in dealing with difficult scriptural passages.
The misconception field addresses this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد سبق تأويلات بعض الخلف، وقد قيل: إنه أحكم، لكنه نقل بعض الشافعية أن إمام الحرمين كان يتأول أولاً ثم رجع في آخر عمره وحرم التأويل ونقل إجماع السلف على منعه، كما بين ذلك في "الرسالة النظامية" وهو موافق لما عليه أصحابنا الماتريدية. وتوسط ابن دقيق العيد فقال : يقبل التأويل إذا كان المعنى الذى أول به قريبا مفهوما من أن تدعو تخاطب العرب، ويتوقف فيه إذا كان بعيدا، وجرى ابن الهمام على التوسط بين الحاجة إلى التأويل لخلل في فهم العوام، وبين أن لا تدعو الحاجة لذلك المرام بحسب اختلاف المقام.
And there have preceded the interpretations (ta'wilat) of some of the later scholars (khalaf), and it was said: it is more precise. But some Shafi'is reported that Imam al-Haramayn used to do ta'wil initially, then he retracted in the end of his life and prohibited ta'wil, and reported the consensus of the Salaf on forbidding it, as he explained in 'al-Risala al-Nizamiyya', and this agrees with what our Maturidi companions hold. And Ibn Daqiq al-'Id took a middle path: he said ta'wil is accepted if the meaning to which one interprets is close and understood from the address of the Arabs, and he suspends judgment if it is far. And Ibn al-Humann proceeded on a middle course between the need for ta'wil due to a defect in the understanding of the common people, and between the absence of need for that purpose, according to the difference of context.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of ta'wil (allegorical interpretation) of divine attributes among later scholars. It begins by noting that some later scholars (khalaf) practiced ta'wil, and some said it is more judicious. However, it reports from Shafi'i sources that Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) initially practiced ta'wil but later retracted and forbade it, transmitting the consensus of the Salaf on prohibiting it, as explained in his work 'al-Risala al-Nizamiyya'. This position is said to align with the Maturidi school. Then two mediating positions are mentioned. First, Ibn Daqiq al-'Id accepted ta'wil conditionally: if the interpreted meaning is close and understood from Arabic discourse, it is accepted; if it is far, he withholds judgment. Second, Ibn al-Humann took a middle course based on context: sometimes there is a need for ta'wil due to confusion among common people, but other times there is no such need. Thus, the scholars differ in their approach, with some absolutely prohibiting ta'wil (like the later Juwayni) and others allowing it conditionally.

Key Terms
التأويل (ta'wil)
إمام الحرمين (Imam al-Haramayn)
ابن دقيق العيد (Ibn Daqiq al-'Id)
ابن الهمام (Ibn al-Humann)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume ta'wil is either always permissible or always forbidden, with no middle ground.
Correction: This passage shows a spectrum: absolute prohibition (Imam al-Haramayn later view), conditional acceptance (Ibn Daqiq), and context-based permission (Ibn al-Humann). The issue is nuanced.

Checkpoint
What was the condition for accepting ta'wil according to Ibn Daqiq al-'Id?
A) The interpretation must be needed to protect the faith of common people.
B) The interpretation must be based on a close and linguistically clear meaning.
C) The interpretation must be done only by a mujtahid.
D) Ta'wil is unconditionally accepted.

Key Takeaway
Later Sunni scholars differed on ta'wil: from absolute prohibition to conditional and context-based permission, reflecting a spectrum of methodological approaches.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a verse about Allah's attributes that seems to imply a human-like quality, do you immediately try to reinterpret it, or can you accept that you may not fully comprehend its meaning? Which of the three scholars' approaches most closely matches your natural inclination, and why does that matter for your faith?
?
Imam al-Haramayn changed his view on ta'wil entirely in his later years. Are you willing to revise your theological positions when confronted with compelling evidence from the Salaf, or do you cling to what you've been taught out of comfort or pride? What would it take for you to change a deeply held belief?
?
Ibn al-Humann permitted ta'wil when there was a 'defect in the understanding of the common people.' Have you ever simplified or reinterpreted a divine attribute to make it easier for someone else to accept, even if it deviated from the precise understanding of the Salaf? How will you balance the need to protect others from confusion with the duty to preserve the truth as the early Muslims understood it?

The Covenant of Alastu with Adam's Progeny
Definition of the covenant of Alastu with Adam's progeny.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the event of the covenant (mithaq) when Allah addressed the souls of Adam's progeny and they affirmed His lordship.

Core Idea
The covenant with Adam's offspring was a real event, establishing the innate belief in God.

This passage describes the extraordinary event where Allah extracted all of Adam's descendants from his loins, endowed them with intellect, and addressed them directly. Their affirmation of His lordship constitutes the original faith that every human is born with.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage describing the extraction, intellect, address, and affirmation. Notice the specific details about the form of tiny ants and the right-left spreading.
This sets the scene for the covenant.
2
Identify the components
Break down the event: extraction, intellect, address, commands, affirmation, and the result (faith and fitrah). Each component is significant.
The affirmation 'Bala' is the core of the covenant.
3
Understand the significance
Reflect on why this event is important for theology: it establishes the fitrah and the accountability of all humans.
This event is a proof for the necessity of belief in God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخرج ذرية آدم عليه السلام من صلبه على صور الذر، فجعل لهم عقلاً، فخاطبهم وأمرهم بالإيمان ونهاهم عن الكفر فأقروا له بالربوبية، فكان ذلك منهم إيمانا، فهم يولدون على تلك الفطرة. فإن الحديث الجامع المانع قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ((اعملوا فكل ميسر لما خلق له)). أخرج ذرية آدم (عليه السلام) أي طبقة بعد طبقة إلى يوم القيامة من صلبه أي أولاً ثم أخرج من أصلاب أبنائه وترائب بناته نسلهم على صور الذر أي على هيئة النمل الصغير بعضها بيض وبعضها سود وانتشروا إلى يمين آدم ويساره فجعل لهم عقلا فخاطبهم أي حين أشهدهم على أنفسهم بقوله تعالى: اَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۲]. وأمرهم بالإيمان أي والإحسان ونهاهم عن الكفر أي والكفران فأقروا له بالربوبية أي ولأنفسهم بالعبودية حيث قالوا بلى فكان ذلك منهم أي قولهم: بلى الذي صدر عنهم إيمانا أي حقيقيا أو حكميا فهم يولدون على تلك الفطرة يعني كما قال الله سبحانه: فِطْرَتَ اللَّهِ الَّتِي فَطَرَ النَّاسَ عَلَيْهَا ﴾ [الروم:۳۰] وكما قال صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم: ((كل مولود يولد على فطرة الإسلام، فأبواه يهودانه أو ينصرانه أو يمجسانه حتى يعرب عنه لسانه إما شاكرا وإما كفورا)). وهذا معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا هَدَيْنَهُ السَّبِيْلَ إِمَّا شَاكِرَ أَوَ إِمَّا كَفُوران [الإنسان: ٣]. والحاصل أن عهد الميثاق ثابت بالكتاب وهو قول الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ اَخَذَرَبُّكَ مِنْ بَنِي آدَمَ مِنْ ظُهُورِهِمْ ذُرِّيَّتَهُمْ ﴾ الآية [الأعراف: ١٧٢]، وبالسنة وهو الحديث الثابت المروي في المصابيح وغيره وتحقيقهما في كتب التفسير وشروح الحديث المنير على ما بيناه في محلهما، خلافا للمعتزلة حيث حملوا الآية والحديث على المعنى المجازي كما دفعناه في موضعهما.
He brought out the offspring of Adam (peace be upon him) from his loins in the form of tiny ants, gave them intellect, addressed them, commanded them to believe and forbade them from disbelief, so they affirmed His lordship, and that was from them faith, so they are born upon that innate disposition. For the comprehensive and definitive hadith is his saying (peace and blessings be upon him): 'Act, for everyone is facilitated to that for which he was created.' He brought out the offspring of Adam (peace be upon him), meaning generation after generation until the Day of Resurrection, from his loins, meaning first, then brought out from the loins of his sons and the collarbones of his daughters their progeny in the form of tiny ants, meaning in the shape of small ants, some white and some black, and they spread to the right of Adam and his left. He gave them intellect and addressed them, meaning when He made them testify against themselves with His saying: 'Am I not your Lord? They said, Yes' [Al-A'raf: 172]. And He commanded them to believe, meaning and to do good, and forbade them from disbelief, meaning and ingratitude. So they affirmed His lordship, meaning and for themselves servitude, when they said 'Yes'. So that was from them, meaning their saying 'Yes' which issued from them, faith, either real or legal. So they are born upon that innate disposition, as Allah the Exalted said: 'The fitrah of Allah upon which He created mankind' [Ar-Rum: 30], and as the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'Every child is born upon the fitrah of Islam, then his parents make him a Jew, a Christian, or a Magian until his tongue expresses him either as grateful or ungrateful.' And this is the meaning of His saying: 'Indeed, We guided him to the way, either grateful or ungrateful' [Al-Insan: 3]. The summary is that the covenant of the pledge is established by the Book, which is the saying of Allah: 'And when your Lord took from the children of Adam, from their loins, their offspring' [Al-A'raf: 172], and by the Sunnah, which is the authentic hadith reported in al-Masabih and others, and their verification is in books of tafsir and commentaries of the illuminating hadith as we have explained in their places, contrary to the Mu'tazila who interpreted the verse and hadith metaphorically as we have refuted in their places.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage defines the event of the divine covenant (mithaq) with Adam's progeny and establishes the innate disposition (fitrah) of monotheism. It begins by describing the extraction of all descendants from Adam's loins in the form of tiny ants, endowed with intellect, and addressed by Allah with the question 'Am I not your Lord?' to which they affirmed. This affirmation constitutes their faith, either real or legal, and they are born upon that fitrah. The author then cites the hadith 'Act, for everyone is facilitated...' as a comprehensive statement. The commentary expands each phrase: the extraction is successive generations, the form is like small ants, and the address is the verse of Alastu. The faith of the progeny is their verbal affirmation 'Yes'. The fitrah is supported by Qur'anic verse (Ar-Rum 30) and the hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitrah...' which explains that parents may change the child's religion. The author then asserts that the covenant is established by both the Qur'an (Al-A'raf 172) and authentic hadith, contrary to the Mu'tazila who interpret these metaphorically. The refutation is referenced but not detailed here.

Key Terms
ذرية
عهد الميثاق
ألست بربكم
فطرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The covenant with Adam's progeny is merely a metaphorical story.
Correction: The author affirms it as a real historical event where Allah directly addressed the souls of future humans.

Checkpoint
What did the progeny of Adam affirm when addressed by Allah?
A) Their own existence
B) That Allah is their Lord
C) That they will be prophets
D) That they will be believers

Key Takeaway
The covenant of Alastu is a real event where Allah addressed all human souls, establishing the innate belief in His lordship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that every soul was given intellect and addressed directly by Allah, and you were among those souls. How does the knowledge that you once personally affirmed His lordship affect the way you live today? Will you let that memory shape your next moment of doubt?
?
This covenant declares that you are born upon the fitrah of belief. Yet, if you find yourself distant from that fitrah, what specific steps will you take tonight to return to the affirmation you once made?
?
If the reality of this covenant is true—that Allah brought you out and gave you intellect—then your existence has a purpose. Are you living as though that purpose is the center of your life, or are you distracted by lesser things? What will you change starting tomorrow?

The Innate Disposition (Fitrah) and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Proof of fitrah from Qur'an and Hadith, and refutation of Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural proofs for the fitrah and the refutation of the Mu'tazila who interpret the covenant metaphorically.

Core Idea
The fitrah is affirmed by both Qur'an and Hadith, and the Mu'tazila's metaphorical interpretation is rejected.

After describing the covenant event, the author provides scriptural evidence for the fitrah from the Qur'an and the Sunnah. He then refutes the Mu'tazila who reinterpret the covenant figuratively, affirming the literal reality of the event.

Guided Path
1
Read the supporting texts
Read the hadith 'Act, for everyone is facilitated...' and the verse of fitrah (Ar-Rum 30) and the hadith 'Every child is born upon the fitrah...' as cited. Understand how they support the fitrah.
These texts are the proof for the fitrah.
2
Understand the summary
Note the author's conclusion that the covenant is established by both the Book and the Sunnah. This is a standard Sunni position.
The author also references tafsir and hadith commentaries for verification.
3
Identify the refutation
The Mu'tazila interpret the covenant metaphorically. The author refutes this, asserting the literal reality. Reflect on why this matters for theology.
This is a sectarian discussion.

Children of Polytheists and the Unreached
Argument that children of polytheists are not in Hell and the unreached are excused.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that children of polytheists are not automatically in Hell, and that those who have not received the Islamic call are excused from punishment unless they explicitly profess disbelief.

Core Idea
No punishment without revelation: children and the unreached are excused.

This passage addresses a sensitive theological question: what happens to children of polytheists and people who never received the Islamic call? The commentator refutes a harsh view and explains the basis for excuse from divine punishment, grounding it in the Qur'anic principle that Allah does not punish until He sends a messenger.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the Arabic text once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: the commentator first addresses children of polytheists, then those unreached by the call.
The passage cites Qur'an 17:15 and references contradictory hadiths.
2
Identify the two rulings
Identify the ruling on children of polytheists (they are not in Hell) and the ruling on those unreached by the call (they are excused unless they explicitly hold disbelief). Note the conditions for excuse.
The key condition is that the person neither expresses faith nor disbelief and holds no contrary belief.
3
Reflect on 'not obligated by mere intellect'
Consider the statement that the unreached are 'not obligated by mere intellect'. This is a key theological principle: accountability depends on receiving the message, not just on rational capacity.
This distinguishes the position from those who say intellect alone can obligate belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا، وقال الشارح: ظهر من هذه المسألة وما يتعلق بها من الأدلة أن القول بأن أطفال المشركين في النار متروك، فكيف لا وقد جعل الشرعُ البالغ الجاهل بالله ممن لم تبلغه الدعوة معذورا، يعني بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِبِينَ حَتَّى نَبْعَثَ رَسُولًا ﴾ [الإسراء:١٥]، وأما الأحاديث فمتعارضة في هذا الباب وقد جمعنا بينها في "شرح المشكاة" على ما ظهر لنا من طريق الصواب. وقد قال فخر الإسلام وكذا نقول في الذي لم تبلغه الدعوة: إنه غير مكلف بمجرد العقل، وإنه إذا لم يصف إيمانا ولا كفرا ولم يعتقد على شيء، أي مما يكون منافيا للإيمان ولا موافقا للعصيان كان معذورا، وإذا وصف الكفر وعقده أو عقده ولم يصفه لم يكن معذورا وكان أهل النار مخلدا.
This. And the commentator said: It appears from this issue and the evidences related to it that the statement that the children of polytheists are in the Fire is abandoned, for how could it not be when the Law has made the adult ignorant of Allah who has not received the call excused, meaning by His saying: 'And We were not to punish until We sent a messenger' [Al-Isra: 15]. As for the hadiths, they are contradictory on this topic, and we have reconciled between them in 'Sharh al-Mishkat' according to what appeared to us as the correct way. And Fakhr al-Islam said, and we say the same regarding one whom the call has not reached: that he is not obligated by mere intellect, and that if he does not express faith nor disbelief and does not believe in anything, meaning something that is contrary to faith or in accordance with disobedience, he is excused. But if he expresses disbelief and holds it firmly, or holds it firmly without expressing it, he is not excused and is among the people of the Fire eternally.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on two categories: children of polytheists and those who have not received the da'wah (call of Islam). The commentator states that the view that children of polytheists are in Hell is abandoned (matruk). The proof is that Islamic law makes a baligh (adult) who is ignorant of Allah and has not received the call excused, based on Qur'an 17:15 ('We do not punish until We send a messenger'). Regarding contradictory hadiths on this topic, the author claims to have reconciled them in his work Sharh al-Mishkat. Then he cites Fakhr al-Islam's position: a person not reached by the call is not mukallaf (obligated) by mere intellect alone. If such a person does not explicitly profess faith or disbelief, and holds no belief that contradicts faith or accords with disobedience, he is excused. However, if he explicitly professes disbelief and holds it firmly, or holds it firmly without expressing it, he is not excused and will be eternally in Hell. This clarifies the boundary of excuse based on the absence of the call.

Key Terms
أطفال المشركين
من لم تبلغه الدعوة
المعذور
غير مكلف بالعقل
فخر الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think children of polytheists automatically go to Hell.
Correction: This passage refutes that view, stating it is abandoned (matruk), and offers the Qur'anic principle that punishment only comes after sending a messenger.

Checkpoint
According to Fakhr al-Islam in this passage, when is a person who has not received the call excused?
A) Always
B) If he does not express faith nor disbelief and holds no contrary belief
C) Only if he believes in Allah
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Children of polytheists are not in Hell, and those unreached by the call are excused unless they explicitly hold disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that people who haven't received Islam clearly are automatically doomed? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what specific change are you willing to make in your attitude toward them?
?
If you were among those who never received the call, would you be excused? What does that reveal about your own reliance on Allah's mercy versus your deeds?
?
The passage says that holding disbelief firmly without expressing it still makes one not excused. What beliefs are you holding firmly in your heart right now? Are they aligned with faith, or is there any hidden defiance? Commit to examining your inner convictions today.

The Ruling on Children of Polytheists and the Unreached
The commentator clarifies the ruling on children of polytheists and those not reached by the call.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic ruling on people who never received the prophetic call—including children of polytheists—and the conditions under which they are excused from punishment.

Core Idea
Not receiving the call is a valid excuse for ignorance of Allah.

This lesson addresses a sensitive theological question: what happens to people who never heard about Islam? The commentator explains that children of polytheists and adults who never received the message are not automatically punished. The Quranic principle of no punishment before sending a messenger is central.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own presentation come through.
Pay attention to the Quranic verse cited.
2
Identify the key categories
The passage mentions three groups: children of polytheists, adults not reached by the call, and those who manifest disbelief. Notice the different rulings for each.
The ruling for children is said to be 'abandoned'.
3
Understand the condition for being excused
The commentator quotes Fakhr al-Islam: a person is excused if they do not manifest faith or disbelief and do not hold any belief contrary to faith. If they manifest or hold disbelief, they are not excused.
This nuance is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا، وقال الشارح: ظهر من هذه المسألة وما يتعلق بها من الأدلة أن القول بأن أطفال المشركين في النار متروك، فكيف لا وقد جعل الشرعُ البالغ الجاهل بالله ممن لم تبلغه الدعوة معذورا، يعني بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كُنَّا مُعَذِبِينَ حَتَّى نَبْعَثَ رَسُولًا ﴾ [الإسراء:١٥]، وأما الأحاديث فمتعارضة في هذا الباب وقد جمعنا بينها في "شرح المشكاة" على ما ظهر لنا من طريق الصواب. وقد قال فخر الإسلام وكذا نقول في الذي لم تبلغه الدعوة: إنه غير مكلف بمجرد العقل، وإنه إذا لم يصف إيمانا ولا كفرا ولم يعتقد على شيء، أي مما يكون منافيا للإيمان ولا موافقا للعصيان كان معذورا، وإذا وصف الكفر وعقده أو عقده ولم يصفه لم يكن معذورا وكان أهل النار مخلدا.
This, and the commentator said: It appeared from this issue and the proofs related to it that the statement that the children of the polytheists are in the Fire is abandoned. How not, when the Law has made the adult ignorant of Allah who has not been reached by the call excused, meaning by His exalted saying: 'And We never punish until We send a messenger' (17:15). As for the hadiths, they are conflicting in this chapter, and we have reconciled them in 'Sharh al-Mishkat' according to what appeared to us as the correct way. And Fakhr al-Islam said, and similarly we say concerning one who has not been reached by the call: he is not obligated by mere reason, and if he does not manifest faith nor disbelief, and does not hold any belief, i.e., something that is contrary to faith nor in agreement with disobedience, he is excused. But if he manifests disbelief and holds it, or holds it without manifesting it, he is not excused and is an inhabitant of the Fire eternally.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (ḥukm) on the fate of children of polytheists and adults who never received the message. The commentator (al-shāriḥ) states that the opinion that children of polytheists are in the Fire is abandoned. He supports this by citing the principle that even an adult who is ignorant of God and has not been reached by the call is excused, based on the verse 'And We never punish until We send a messenger' (17:15). He acknowledges that the ḥadīths on this topic are conflicting, and he reconciles them in his work Sharḥ al-Mishkāt. He then quotes Fakhr al-Islam that one who has not been reached by the call is not obligated by mere reason; if he does not manifest faith or disbelief, and does not hold any belief contrary to faith, he is excused. However, if he manifests disbelief and holds it, or holds it without manifesting it, he is not excused and will be eternally in Hell.

Key Terms
أطفال المشركين
لم تبلغه الدعوة
معذور
شرح المشكاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all who disbelieve are punished equally, regardless of whether they received the message.
Correction: This passage shows that ignorance due to not receiving the call is a valid excuse. Those who never heard about Islam and do not manifest or hold disbelief are not punished.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the ruling on an adult who has never been reached by the call and does not manifest faith or disbelief?
A) He is punished as a disbeliever.
B) He is excused and not punished.
C) He is considered a believer.
D) He is judged according to his innate nature.

Key Takeaway
Those who never received the call and do not manifest or hold disbelief are excused from punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone who does not believe as you do, assuming they are simply stubborn or evil, without considering whether they have truly understood the message? How can you cultivate a heart that gives others the excuse of ignorance that Allah Himself grants?
?
The passage teaches that those who have not been reached by the call are excused—but you have been reached. What will you do today to ensure that your own response to the call is not one of mere intellectual assent but of living faith that saves you from the Fire?
?
If you were to be judged by the standard applied to those who have received the call—without the excuse of ignorance—would you be found faithful? Name one area where you have been careless in seeking or acting upon knowledge of Allah, and commit to addressing it this week.

The Primordial Covenant and the Test of Forgetting
Commentator describes the mīthāq event and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first interpretation of the primordial covenant (mīthāq) and how the commentators respond to the objection that we do not remember it.

Core Idea
Forgetting the covenant is part of the test, not an excuse.

This passage from the commentary on al-Fiqh al-Akbar presents the first interpretation of the primordial covenant between God and humanity. The commentator describes the event vividly and then anticipates a natural objection: if this covenant happened, why don't we remember it? The answer reveals a key principle about divine testing and the role of faith in the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Read the covenant narrative
Read the Arabic and translation describing how God brought forth Adam's offspring, gave them intellect and speech, and addressed them directly. Notice the direct quote 'Am I not your Lord?'
This sets the stage for the objection.
2
Identify the objection
The objector asks: if this happened, why don't we remember it despite our best efforts? This is a natural question that challenges the binding nature of the covenant.
The objection assumes memory is necessary for accountability.
3
Understand the answer
The answer explains that God made us forget as a trial. The world is a place of testing, and belief in the unseen is required. Forgetting does not remove the proof.
Note the Quranic evidence about deeds being enumerated even if forgotten.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظهر آدم عليه السلام فأخرج من ظهره كل ذريته فنشرها بين يديه جميعا، وصورهم وجعل عقولا يعلمون بها وألسنا ينطقون بها، ثم كلمهم قبلاً أي عيانا، يعاينهم آدم عليه السلام، وقال: أَلَسْتُ بِرَبِّكُمْ قَالُوا بَلَى شَهِدْنَا وتلاها إلى قوله تعالى: الْمُبْطِلُونَ. فإن قيل: فما وجه إلزام الحجة بهذه الأية ونحن لا نذكر هذا الميثاق وإن تفكرنا وجهدنا جهدنا في ذلك بالاتفاق؟ أجيب بأن الله سبحانه وتعالى أنسانا ذلك ابتلاء؛ لأن الدنيا دار ابتلاء وعلينا الإيمان بالغيب ابتداء ولو تذكرنا ذلك لزال الابتلاء وما احتجنا إلى تذكير الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام وليس كل ما ينسى بالمرة تزول به الحجة وتثبت به المعذرة. قال الله تعالى في حق أعمالنا: ﴿ أَحْصَاهُ اللَّهُ وَنَسُوهُ ﴾ [المجادلة: ٦]، وأخبر أنه سيثيبنا ويجازينا.
Adam (peace be upon him) appeared, then God brought forth from his back all his offspring and spread them before him all together, and formed them and gave them intellects by which they know and tongues by which they speak, then He spoke to them face to face, that is, directly, with Adam (peace be upon him) witnessing them, and said: 'Am I not your Lord?' They said: 'Yes, we testify.' And He recited until His saying: 'those who falsify.' If it is said: What is the basis of establishing the proof with this verse while we do not remember this covenant even if we think and exert our utmost effort in that by agreement? The answer is that Allah, the Exalted and Glorified, made us forget that as a trial, because this world is a domain of trial and we must believe in the unseen from the beginning. If we had remembered that, the trial would have ceased and we would not have needed the reminders of the prophets (peace be upon them). Not everything that is forgotten entirely removes the proof and establishes an excuse. Allah says concerning our deeds: 'Allah has enumerated it and they have forgotten it' [Mujadila: 6], and He informed that He will reward us and recompense us.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer unit within the commentary on the mīthāq (primordial covenant). The commentator first describes the first interpretation of the covenant: that God actually gathered all of Adam's offspring before him, endowed them with intellects and speech, addressed them directly asking 'Am I not your Lord?', and they testified. Then an objector asks: if this covenant really happened, why don't we remember it despite our best efforts? The answer is that God made us forget it deliberately as a trial. This world is a domain of trial, so belief in the unseen is required; if we remembered, there would be no test and no need for prophets. Moreover, forgetting does not automatically remove the binding argument: God mentions that people forget their own deeds (Quran 58:6), yet they are still held accountable. Thus the covenant remains a valid proof even if not recalled.

Key Terms
ميثاق
ذرية
ابتلاء
إيمان بالغيب
حجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Forgetting the covenant means it is not binding on us.
Correction: The passage explains that forgetting is part of the divine trial and does not remove the proof.

Checkpoint
According to the answer to the objection, why did God make people forget the covenant?
A) Because they were not responsible for it.
B) To test them through faith in the unseen.
C) Because the covenant was not binding.
D) Because they had no intellect.

Key Takeaway
The primordial covenant remains a binding proof even though we do not remember it, because forgetting is a test requiring faith in the unseen.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Because you don't remember the day you testified to Allah's lordship, do you live as if that testimony never happened? What would change if you truly believed that you have already sworn allegiance to Him, even if you can't recall it?
?
The passage says forgetfulness is a trial. What if your spiritual laziness is actually part of God's test for you? Are you passing or failing that test when you ignore your fard obligations?
?
If the covenant is still a binding proof despite your forgetfulness, then how much weight does your ignorance carry? Are you willing to stand before Allah and claim forgetfulness as an excuse, knowing that He made you forget intentionally to see if you would seek Him without memory?

The Second Interpretation of the Mīthāq and the Mu'tazila Position
Commentator presents the second interpretation of the mīthāq and critiques the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second interpretation of the mīthāq as a natural process of innate testimony, its compatibility with the first, and the Mu'tazila's rationalist critique.

Core Idea
The mīthāq is witnessed not just by a primordial gathering, but by creation itself.

The commentator now presents the view of the 'people of investigation,' who understand the covenant as an ongoing testimony through the design of creation. He then explains why the Mu'tazila reject the literal gathering and favor a metaphorical reading, rooted in their principle of prioritizing reason over revelation. This lesson unpacks both positions and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the shift from the first interpretation to the second.
The passage is divided into three parts: the second view, a compatibility remark, and the Mu'tazila critique.
2
Identify the two interpretations and their compatibility
The first interpretation was a literal gathering of all offspring; the second sees the 'bringing forth' as the natural process of reproduction and the 'testimony' as the innate signs of oneness. The commentator says both can be combined.
3
Analyze the Mu'tazila critique and the doctrine of souls before bodies
The Mu'tazila reject the first interpretation because it defies normal reason; they prefer a metaphorical reading. The passage also asserts the creation of souls before bodies based on a hadith.
This shows the tension between rationalism and transmitted texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني قول أرباب النظر وأصحاب العقول، وهو أنه تعالى أخرج الذرية وهم الأولاد من أصلاب آبائهم، وذلك الإخراج أنهم كانوا نطفة، فأخرجها الله تعالى إلى أرحام الأمهات وجعلها علقة ثم مضغة حتى جعلهم بشرا سويا وخلقا كاملا أشهدهم على أنفسهم بما ركب فيهم من دلائل الوحدانية، فبالإشهاد بالدلالة صاروا كأنهم قالوا بلى، قيل وهذا القول لا ينافي الأول، إذ الجمع بينهما ممكن، فتأمل. وأما المعتزلة فقد أطبقوا على أنه لا يجوز تفسير الآية بالوجه الأول ومالوا إلى الوجه الثاني وجعلوه من باب التمثيل، وهذا منهم بناء على أن كل ما لا يدركه العقل لا يجوز القول به لما عرف من أصلهم من تقديم العقل على النقل، ثم الآية تدل على أن الله تعالى خلق الأرواح مع الأجساد أو قبلها وهو الصحيح لخبر: ((إن الله تعالى خلق الأرواح قبل الأجساد بخمسمائة ألف سنة)). وأن الخطاب والجواب كان للأرواح والأجساد كما يبعثون بهما في الميعاد.
The second is the statement of the people of investigation and the possessors of intellects, and it is that He brought forth the offspring, and they are the children from the loins of their fathers, and that bringing forth is that they were a drop of fluid, then Allah brought it out into the wombs of mothers and made it a clot, then a lump of flesh, until He made them a sound human being and a perfect creation. He made them testify against themselves by the signs of oneness that He placed in them, so by the testimony through indication they became as if they said 'Yes.' It is said: This statement does not contradict the first, because combining both is possible, so reflect. As for the Mu'tazila, they have unanimously held that it is not permissible to interpret the verse according to the first view, and they inclined to the second view and made it a metaphorical representation. This from them is based on the principle that whatever the intellect does not perceive, it is not permissible to speak of it, due to what is known of their fundamental principle of giving precedence to the intellect over transmitted texts. Then the verse indicates that Allah created the souls with the bodies or before them, and that is the correct view, according to the report: 'Allah created the souls five hundred thousand years before the bodies.' And the address and response was for the souls and bodies, just as they will be resurrected with both on the appointed day.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the mīthāq by presenting a second interpretation. According to the people of investigation, the 'bringing forth' refers to the natural process of human reproduction: from a drop of fluid, to a clot, to a lump of flesh, culminating in a fully formed human. The 'testifying against themselves' is through the innate signs of divine unity (tawḥīd) that God placed within them, so the very design of creation speaks as if they testified. The commentator notes that this second view does not contradict the first; both can be accepted together. Then he turns to the Mu'tazila, who reject the first interpretation (a real gathering of all offspring) because it involves a suprarational event. Their principle is to give precedence to the intellect over transmitted reports (al-'aql qabl al-naql). They interpret the verse metaphorically. The passage then adds that the verse also indicates the creation of souls before bodies (or with them), citing a hadith about souls being created five hundred thousand years before bodies. The address and response in the covenant involved both souls and bodies, consistent with the resurrection of both.

Key Terms
أرباب النظر
إشهاد بالدلالة
تمثيل
تقديم العقل على النقل
خلق الأرواح قبل الأجساد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking the two interpretations are mutually exclusive and cannot both be true.
Correction: The commentator explicitly says the second view does not contradict the first and that combining both is possible.

Checkpoint
What is the Mu'tazila's reason for rejecting the first interpretation of the mīthāq?
A) They believe the intellect is subordinate to revelation.
B) They give precedence to the intellect over transmitted texts.
C) They follow the first interpretation.
D) They reject the second interpretation.

Key Takeaway
The mīthāq can be understood both as a literal primordial gathering and as an innate testimony through creation; the Mu'tazila reject the literal due to their rationalist prioritization of intellect over revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look at your own life—your body, your existence from a single drop to who you are today. Where do you see the signs of Allah's oneness in that story? And when you see them, do you say 'Yes' with your heart, or has familiarity silenced that testimony? What will you do today to listen to that testimony again?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted that only what the intellect can perceive is acceptable. Now be honest: where have you let your own reasoning limit what you accept from Allah's revelation? Is there a truth in this lesson—like the soul before the body, or a covenant beyond your memory—that your mind struggles with? Will you submit to it even if you cannot fully grasp it?
?
The commentator says both interpretations can be combined. Think of a tension in your own faith—perhaps between God's mercy and justice, or between destiny and human effort. Have you assumed they must be in conflict? What if, like this passage, they can both be true? How would that change the way you live with that tension starting today?

The Rank of Elite Angels Versus Common Believers
Clarification of the relative rank of angels and believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic scholarly consensus regarding the relative status of elite angels, common believers, and prophets, and why this issue is not considered essential to faith.

Core Idea
Elite angels outrank common believers but remain below prophets.

This passage from al-Fiqh al-Akbar addresses a nuanced question of celestial hierarchy: How do the highest angels compare to ordinary believers and prophets? The author presents the majority view while noting that this knowledge is not required for salvation. Let’s examine the text and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, focusing on the names and the comparative terms 'أفضل' and 'دون مرتبة'.
Notice the phrase 'على الأصح من أقوال المجتهدين' indicating scholarly consensus.
2
Understand the restriction to 'people'
The author explains why earlier discussions focused on humans: because elite angels are a special case. They are not included in the general category of 'people' for comparison.
3
Identify the three tiers
The passage establishes a clear hierarchy: prophets and messengers at the top, then elite angels, then common believers. The author specifically names four archangels and two groups of angels as examples of the elite.
The word 'روبيين' is uncertain; some interpret it as 'spiritual beings' or 'cherubim'.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal weight
Note the author’s final remark: this issue is not necessary for religious certainty. This teaches us that not all theological details carry equal importance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتقييد بالناس لأن خواص الملائكة كجبرائيل وميكائيل وإسرافيل وعزرائيل وحملة العرش والكروبيين روبيين من الملائكة المقربين أفضل من عوام المؤمنين وإن كانوا دون مرتبة الأنبياء والمرسلين على الأصح من أقوال المجتهدين، مع أنه لا ضرورة إلى هذه المسألة في أمر الدين على وجه اليقين.
And the restriction to people is because the elite of the angels, such as Gabriel, Michael, Israfil, Azrael, the bearers of the Throne, and the cherubim – rūbiyīn from the intimate angels – are better than the common believers, although they are below the rank of the prophets and messengers, according to the most correct of the sayings of the mujtahids, along with the fact that there is no necessity for this matter in the religion definitively.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal clarification regarding the relative status of angels and believers. The author notes that the earlier discussion was restricted to 'people' (humans) because the elite angels are superior to ordinary believers. He lists specific high-ranking angels: Gabriel, Michael, Israfil, Azrael, the bearers of the Throne, and the cherubim (with an uncertain term 'rūbiyīn'). However, these angels are still below the rank of prophets and messengers. This is the strongest opinion among the mujtahids. The author adds that this issue is not necessary for religious certainty, implying it is a minor point.

Praying Behind the Righteous and Sinful
Proves permissibility of praying behind any Muslim with hadith and Companion example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that praying behind any Muslim, regardless of their righteousness, is permissible, as established by hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Even a sinful imam does not invalidate the prayer behind him.

This lesson explores a crucial aspect of Sunni theology: the validity of praying behind any Muslim imam, whether righteous or sinful. Based on a direct prophetic command and the actions of the Companions, the passage affirms that the prayer is valid and does not need to be repeated, even if the imam is openly sinful. We will examine the evidence and the practical ruling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow from the statement to the evidence to the ruling to the historical example.
Notice how the author uses both a hadith and a Companion's action as proof.
2
Identify the hadith evidence
Find the Prophet's command: 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' Note that the hadith is narrated by al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi, with an addition including janazah and jihad.
3
Analyze the ruling on abandoning congregation
Understand the position that abandoning Friday and congregational prayers behind a sinful imam is considered innovation. The correct view is to pray and not repeat.
This shows the importance of unity in prayer despite differences.
4
Reflect on the historical example
Consider the incident of Ibn Mas'ud praying behind al-Walid ibn 'Uqbah, who led four rak'ahs for Fajr due to intoxication. Ibn Mas'ud's witty response 'We have been with you since today in an increase' demonstrates that the prayer was valid.
This illustrates that even major sin by the imam does not invalidate the followers' prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا في قوله الله رحمه تعالى: (والصلاة خلف كل بر وفاجر) أي صالح وطالح (من المؤمنين) جائزة أي لقوله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم: (صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر)). أخرجه الدار قطني عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه وكذا البيهقي، وزاد قوله: ((وصلوا على كل بر وفاجر، وجاهدوا مع كل بر وفاجر)) . فمن ترك الجمعة والجماعة خلف الإمام الفاجر فهو مبتدع عند أكثر العلماء، والصحيح أنه يصليها ولا يعيدها. وكان ابن مسعود وغيره يصلون خلف الوليد بن عقبة بن أبي معيط وكان يشرب الخمر، حتى أنه صلى بهم الصبح مرة أربعا ثم قال: أزيدكم؟ فقال ابن مسعود: «ما زلنا معك منذ اليوم في زيادة».
And likewise in His statement – may Allah have mercy on him –: 'And the prayer behind every righteous and sinful person' – i.e., the good and the wicked – 'from the believers is permissible', i.e., due to his statement (peace and prayer be upon him): 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' Al-Daraqutni narrated it from Abu Hurayrah (may Allah be pleased with him), and likewise al-Bayhaqi, and he added his statement: 'And pray over every righteous and sinful person, and wage jihad with every righteous and sinful person.' So whoever abandons Friday prayer and congregation behind an unjust imam is an innovator in the opinion of most scholars, and the correct view is that he prays it and does not repeat it. And Ibn Mas'ud and others used to pray behind al-Walid ibn 'Uqbah ibn Abi Mu'ayt, who used to drink wine, so much so that he once led them in the morning prayer performing four rak'ahs and then said: 'Shall I increase you?' So Ibn Mas'ud said: 'We have been with you since today in an increase.'
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage establishes the permissibility of praying behind any Muslim, whether righteous or sinful. The author begins by citing the statement of the author (Abu Hanifa) that praying behind every righteous and sinful person from the believers is permissible, based on the Prophet's command to pray behind every righteous and sinful person. He then provides the hadith narration from al-Daraqutni and al-Bayhaqi, which also includes praying over (janazah) and waging jihad with both kinds. The passage then addresses the ruling: whoever abandons Friday and congregational prayers behind a sinful imam is considered an innovator (mubtadi') by most scholars; the correct position is to pray and not repeat it. The author then gives a historical example: Ibn Mas'ud and others prayed behind al-Walid ibn 'Uqbah, a governor known for drinking wine. In one incident, al-Walid led the morning prayer in a drunken state and performed four rak'ahs instead of two, then asked if they wanted more. Ibn Mas'ud wittily replied that they had been with him in an increase since that morning. This illustrates that despite the imam's sinfulness, the prayer was valid and did not need to be repeated.

Key Terms
الصلاة خلف البر والفاجر
بر

The Beatific Vision: Proofs and Transcendence
The commentator proves the vision of Allah in the afterlife and describes it without modality or direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural proofs for the Beatific Vision in the Hereafter and how the Salaf affirmed it while negating modality, direction, and any physicality.

Core Idea
The Beatific Vision is real, but without how, where, or distance.

The possibility of seeing Allah in the Hereafter is a foundational belief of Ahl al-Sunnah. This passage presents the key Quranic and prophetic evidences while carefully guarding against any anthropomorphic misunderstanding. The commentator shows that affirmation of vision does not imply physicality, direction, or limitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the full English translation. Let the flow of proofs and explanations settle before analyzing.
Notice the shift from proof to qualification.
2
Identify the three main proofs
Find the Quranic verses and hadiths cited as evidence for the vision. The passage uses two Quranic verses (75:22-23 and 83:15) and two hadiths (the moon vision and the veil lifting).
These are the core textual evidence.
3
Understand the qualifications
After establishing the vision, the commentator emphasizes it is without modality (kayfiyyah), direction (jihat), distance, connection, separation, indwelling, or union. This safeguards transcendence.
This is the tanzih aspect.
4
Grasp the ru'yah vs idrak distinction
The final part cites verse 6:103 and explains that 'idrak' (comprehension) is more specific than 'ru'yah' (vision), so we affirm vision but deny that any sight can fully comprehend Allah.
This resolves apparent contradiction with the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والله تعالى يُرى بصيغة المجهول، أي ينظر إليه بعين البصر (في الآخرة) أي القيامة يوم لقوله تعالى: وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَيد أي يوم القيامة نَاضِرَة ، أي حسنة منعمة بهية مشرقة متهللة إلى رَيْهَا نَاظِرَةٌ [القيامة : ۲۲ - ۲۳] ، أي تراه عيانا بلا كيفية ولا جهة ولا ثبوت مسافة، ومن يرى ربه لا يلتفت إلى غيره. ولقوله تعالى: كَلَّا إِنَّهُمْ ، أَي الكفار عَنْ رَّبِّهِمْ ، أَي عن رؤية فلا يرونه أو عن رحمة ربهم وكرامة ربهم يَوْمَيذٍ تَمَحْجُوبُونَ ﴾ [المطففين: ١٥]، أي لممنوعون، أي بخلاف الأبرار والمؤمنين فإنهم في نظر ربهم ،مقربون، ولقوله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم كما في الصحيحين وغيرهما: ((إنكم سترون ربكم كما ترون القمر ليلة البدر، لا تضامون في رؤيته)) . (١) وفي رواية: ((لا تضارون)) . (٣) وهو حديث مشهور، في الصحيحين وغيرهما مذكور. وقد رواه أحد وعشرون من أكابر الصحابة. ويراه المؤمنون وهم في الجنة بأعين (رؤوسهم لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام على ما رواه مسلم: ((إذا دخل أهل الجنة الجنة يقول الله تبارك وتعالى : تريدون شيئا أزيدكم؟ فيقولون: ألم تبيض وجوهنا، ألم تدخلنا الجنة وتنجينا من النار ؟ قال فيرفع الحجاب، أي عن وجوه أهل الجنة، فينظرون إلى وجه الله سبحانه، فما أعطوا شيئا أحب إليهم من النظر إلى ربهم، ثم تلا قوله تعالى: وَلِلَّذِينَ أَحْسَنُوا الْحُسُنَى أي الجنة العليا وَزِيَادَة )). (٣) [يونس: ٢٦]، أي النظر إلى وجه المولى وهو قول الأكثر من السلف بلا تشبيه أي رؤية مقرونة بتنزيه لا مكنونة بتشبيه ولا كيفية أي في الصورة ولا كميّة أي في الهيئة المنظورة، ولا يكون بينه وبين خلقه مسافة أي لا في غاية من القرب ولا في نهاية من البعد، ولا بوصف الاتصال ولا بنعت الانفصال ولا بالحلول والاتحاد كما يقوله الوجودية المائلون إلى الاتحاد فذات رؤيته ثابتة بالكتاب والسنة إلا أنها متشابهة من حيث الجهة والكمية والكيفية فنثبت ما أثبته النقل وننفي عنه ما نزهه العقل، كما أشار إلى هذا المعنى قوله تعالى: لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ [الأنعام: ١٠٣]، أي لا تحيط به الأبصار في مقام الإبصار، فإن الإدراك أخص من الرؤية.
And Allah Almighty is seen (passive voice), meaning He is looked at with the eye of sight in the Hereafter, i.e. the Day of Resurrection, due to His statement: 'Faces on that Day, i.e. the Day of Resurrection, will be radiant, i.e. beautiful, blessed, bright, beaming, looking at their Lord' [75:22-23], i.e. they see Him with their own eyes without modality (kayfiyyah), without direction (jihat), and without the establishment of distance. Whoever sees his Lord does not turn to anyone else. And due to His statement: 'No! Indeed, they, i.e. the disbelievers, from their Lord, i.e. from seeing their Lord, or from the mercy of their Lord and the honor of their Lord, on that Day will be veiled' [83:15], i.e. prevented, meaning unlike the righteous and the believers, for they are in the sight of their Lord, brought near. And due to the saying of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, as in the two Sahihs and others: 'Indeed you will see your Lord as you see the moon on the night of the full moon, you will not compete in seeing Him.' And in another narration: 'you will not be harmed in seeing Him.' It is a well-known hadith, mentioned in the two Sahihs and elsewhere, narrated by twenty-one of the major Companions. And the believers see Him while they are in Paradise with the eyes of their heads, due to his saying, peace be upon him, according to what Muslim narrated: 'When the people of Paradise enter Paradise, Allah, Blessed and Exalted, says: Do you desire something more for you? They say: Have You not whitened our faces, have You not admitted us to Paradise and saved us from the Fire? He said: Then the veil is lifted, i.e. from the faces of the people of Paradise, and they look at the Face of Allah the Exalted. And they have not been given anything more beloved to them than looking at their Lord. Then he recited His statement: 'For those who do good is the best (i.e. the highest Paradise) and more' [10:26], i.e. the vision of the Face of the Lord. This is the saying of the majority of the Salaf, without comparison (tashbih), i.e. a vision accompanied by transcendence (tanzih), not contained in comparison, and without modality (kayfiyyah), i.e. in form, and without quantity (kammiyyah), i.e. in the seen state, and there is no distance between Him and His creation, i.e. not in the extreme of nearness nor in the extreme of distance, nor with the description of connection nor with the attribute of separation, nor by indwelling or union as the existentialists who incline toward union say. So the reality of His vision is established by the Book and Sunnah, but it is ambiguous (mutashabiha) in terms of direction, quantity, and modality. So we affirm what the transmitted texts affirm and we negate from Him what the intellect declares Him free from, as alluded to by His statement: 'Vision does not comprehend Him' [6:103], i.e. perceptions do not encompass Him in the station of seeing, for comprehension (idrak) is more specific than vision (ru'yah).
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal proof and explanation of the Beatific Vision (ru'yat Allah) in the Hereafter. It begins by stating that Allah will be seen (passive voice) with the eyes in the afterlife. The commentator provides three proofs: first, Quranic verses (75:22-23) about faces looking at their Lord; second, the verse (83:15) that disbelievers are veiled, implying believers see; third, the famous hadith from Sahihayn comparing it to seeing the moon. Then he adds a hadith from Muslim about the people of Paradise seeing Allah after the veil is lifted. The explanation emphasizes that this vision is real but devoid of modality (kayf), direction (jihat), quantity (kammiyyah), distance, connection, separation, indwelling, or union. It is a vision accompanied by transcendence (tanzih). The passage then quotes the verse (6:103) 'Vision does not comprehend Him' to clarify that 'comprehension' (idrak) is more specific than vision (ru'yah), so ru'yah is affirmed while idrak is denied. The final statement summarises the methodology: affirm what revelation affirms, negate what reason negates.

رؤية
بلا كيفية
بلا جهة
تشبيه
تنزيه
إدراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Seeing Allah implies He has a physical form or is located in a direction.
Correction: The Salaf affirm a real vision but without modality (kayfiyyah), direction (jihat), distance, or any physical attributes. It is a vision of tanzih.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between 'ru'yah' (vision) and 'idrak' (comprehension)?
A) Ru'yah is only for believers, idrak for all.
B) Idrak is more specific than ru'yah, so vision is affirmed while comprehension is denied.
C) Ru'yah happens in this world, idrak in the next.
D) They are synonyms.

Key Takeaway
The Beatific Vision is established by revelation and is understood as a real seeing of Allah that transcends any physical or spatial concepts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly long to see your Lord, or are you content with the pleasures of this world? What does your daily life say about that?
?
The disbelievers are veiled from seeing Allah. Are there any veils you have placed between yourself and your Lord through your actions?
?
You will see Allah with your own eyes, but without how or where. Does that thought stir awe in your heart, or do you try to imagine it in a limited way? The lesson says we affirm the vision but negate any likeness. Are you willing to accept that mystery without reducing it to your own comprehension?

Seeing Allah in Dreams: Positions and Methodological Critique
Presents two positions on seeing Allah in dreams and critiques Qadikhan's suggestion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main positions among scholars regarding seeing Allah in dreams and why engaging in discussion of such matters is preferred over avoidance.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah in dreams is debated: either impossible or possible without likeness, and silence is not always golden.

This passage from the sharh addresses a disputed theological question: can believers see Allah in their dreams? Some scholars, including al-Maturidi, argue it is impossible because dreams involve images, and Allah transcends form. Others permit it but with strict conditions, citing reports from early saints. The author also critiques Qadikhan's advice to avoid discussing the topic, asserting that theological inquiry is necessary.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two positions
Read the passage once to get an overview. Note that there are two positions: denial by some (including al-Maturidi) and conditional permission by others.
This is a debate within the same school.
2
Examine the proof for denial
Look at the argument: dreams involve images (khayal wa mithal), and Allah is transcendent above that. This is a tanzih-based argument.
3
Examine the conditions for permission and narrated examples
The permissive view insists on seeing without modality, direction, etc. They rely on reports from Abu Yazid, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and others. Consider how these reports are used as evidence.
These are not prophetic reports but saintly experiences.
4
Analyze the criticism of Qadikhan's stance
Qadikhan suggested refraining from discussion is good. The author rejects this, arguing that refraining does not achieve the goal of verifying truth and establishing rulings.
This highlights the importance of theological engagement.
5
Reflect on theological methodology
Think about why the author includes this critique. It underscores the necessity of rational and textual inquiry in kalam, even for sensitive topics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا، وذهبت طائفة من مثبتي الرؤية استحالة رؤية الله تعالى في المنام، منهم الشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي. قيل وعليه المحققون واحتجوا بأن ما يُرى في المنام خيال ومثال، والله تعالى ينزه عن ذلك، وجوزها بعض أصحابنا، لكن بلا كيفية وجهة ومقابلة وخيال ومثال متمسكين بالمحكي عن السلف، كما روي عن أبي زيد قال: رأيت ربي في المنام، فقلت: كيف الطريق إليك؟ فقال اترك نفسك وتعال. وقيل: رأى أحمد بن حنبل ربه في المنام فقال: يا أحمد كل الناس يطلبون مني إلا أبا يزيد فإنه يطلبني. ولعل سببه أنه قيل لأبي يزيد: ما تريد؟ فقال : أريد أن لا أريد. وروي عن حمزة الزيات وأبي الفوارس شاه بن شجاع الكرماني ومحمد بن علي الحكيم الترمذي والعلامة شمس الأئمة الكردري أنهم رأوه تعالى في المنام، وسيأتي بعض ما يتعلق بهذه المسألة على وجه التكملة. وأما قول قاضيخان: إن ترك الكلام في هذه المسألة حسن. فغير مستحسن؛ لأن ترك الكلام لا يفيد تحقيق المرام وتثبيت الأحكام.
This, and a group of those who affirm the vision [of Allah] considered seeing Allah in a dream impossible, among them Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. It is said that the verifiers are upon this. They argued that what is seen in a dream is an image and likeness (khayal wa mithal), and Allah is exalted above that. And some of our companions permitted it, but without modality, direction, opposition, image, or likeness, adhering to what is narrated from the predecessors. As narrated from Abu Yazid who said: I saw my Lord in a dream, so I said: How is the way to You? He said: Leave yourself and come. And it was said: Ahmad ibn Hanbal saw his Lord in a dream and said: O Ahmad, all people ask from Me except Abu Yazid, for he asks for Me. Perhaps the reason is that Abu Yazid was asked: What do you want? He said: I want not to want. And it is narrated from Hamza al-Zayyat, Abu al-Fawaris Shah ibn Shuja' al-Kirmani, Muhammad ibn Ali al-Hakim al-Tirmidhi, and the scholar Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari that they saw Him in a dream, and some related to this matter will come later as a completion. As for the statement of Qadikhan: 'Refraining from speech on this matter is good,' it is not approved, because refraining from speech does not bring about the attainment of the goal and the establishment of rulings.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of seeing Allah in dreams. The author first states that a group of those who affirm the beatific vision (including al-Maturidi) considered seeing Allah in a dream impossible. Their proof is that whatever is seen in a dream is a mental image (khayal wa mithal), and Allah is transcendent beyond such forms. However, some of the author's fellow scholars (from the Hanafi/Maturidi school) permitted it, but with strict conditions: without modality (kayfiyya), direction (jiha), opposition (muqabala), image (khayal), or likeness (mithal). They rely on reports from the pious predecessors (salaf). The author then cites several examples: the story of Abu Yazid al-Bistami seeing Allah and being told to leave himself; Ahmad ibn Hanbal also reportedly saw Allah; and others such as Hamza al-Zayyat, etc. The author then criticizes Qadikhan's opinion that it is better to refrain from discussing this matter. The author argues that refraining does not achieve the goal of verifying the truth and establishing the rulings, implying that engagement is necessary. Thus the passage both presents the doctrinal disagreement and defends the legitimacy of discussing it.

Key Terms
المنام (al-manam)
خيال (khayal)
مثال (mithal)
تنزيه (tanzih)
السلف (al-salaf)
قاضيخان (Qadikhan)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that all scholars deny seeing Allah in dreams.
Correction: The passage shows that while some deny it (e.g., al-Maturidi), others permit it with conditions, citing reports from the salaf.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main argument of those who deny seeing Allah in dreams?
A) It is impossible because Allah is not visible at all.
B) Dreams contain images (khayal wa mithal), and Allah is exalted above that.
C) The Prophet never saw Allah.
D) No one has ever claimed to see Allah in a dream.

Key Takeaway
Theological discussion is necessary; refraining from debate does not lead to truth or establish rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a difficult theological debate like this one, do you tend to stay silent or engage? What does your response say about your commitment to truth?
?
The salaf who saw Allah in a dream asked 'How is the way to You?' and the answer was 'Leave yourself and come.' What is the 'self' you need to leave behind to truly seek Allah?
?
If refraining from discussion does not accomplish the truth, what discomfort are you avoiding by not grappling with hard religious questions? Will you step into that discomfort today?

The Balance and Book Apply to Disbelievers and the Righteous
The author explains that the Quranic verses about the balance and book pertain to disbelievers and the righteous.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quranic verses about the balance and book (mizan and kitab) are specifically about disbelievers and the righteous, not about sinful believers, and that the mention of sinners is to keep them between hope and fear.

Core Idea
The scales and book of deeds primarily weigh the righteous and disbelievers, not the disobedient.

This lesson clarifies a common misinterpretation of Quranic verses about the balance (mizan) and the book (kitab). The author, Imam al-Sanusi, teaches that these verses are specifically about disbelievers and the righteous, not about sinful believers. He also explains a related hadith about the people of al-A'raf and the meaning of the verse 'So We will not establish for them any weight.'

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author states 'the correct view is' indicating a clarification.
2
Identify the main claim and its exceptions
The author says the balance/book verses are specific to disbelievers and the righteous. Find where he mentions the disobedient and why they are mentioned.
The purpose is to keep them between hope and fear.
3
Understand the people of al-A'raf and the verse about weight
Read the part about the hadith of equal deeds and the verse 'So We will not establish for them any weight.' Ask: What does 'weight' mean here?
The author explains it means 'any measure or consideration' because the basis is righteous deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالصواب أن آية الميزان والكتاب وأكثر ما وقع في القرآن المجيد من الوعد والوعيد فهو مختص بالكفار والأبرار، وما ذكر فيه حال العصاة والفجار ليكونوا بين الخوف والرجاء في تلك الدار بين المقام في دار القرار وفي دار البوار، نعم قد ورد أن من استوت حسناته وسيئاته فهو من أهل الأعراف، فيتأخر دخوله في الجنة عن أهل المعرفة والإنصاف والمجاهدين في المصاف والقائمين بأنواع الطاعة من الصلاة والطواف والاعتكاف وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿ فَلَا تُقِيمُ لَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ وَزُنًا ﴾ [الكهف : ١٠٥]، أي مقدارا واعتبارات عند الله. لأن مداره الأعمال الصالحة
The correct view is that the verse of the balance and the book, and most of what occurs in the noble Qur'an of promise and threat, is specific to the disbelievers and the righteous. And what is mentioned therein about the condition of the disobedient and the wicked is so that they may be between fear and hope in that abode, between staying in the abode of permanence and the abode of destruction. Yes, it has been reported that whoever's good deeds and bad deeds are equal is among the people of al-A'raf, so his entry into Paradise is delayed relative to the people of knowledge, fairness, and the mujahideen in the battlefield, and those who engage in various types of obedience like prayer, circumambulation, and i'tikaf. And as for His statement, the Exalted: 'So We will not establish for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight' [al-Kahf: 105], meaning any measure or consideration with Allah, because the basis of that is righteous deeds.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage classifies the applicability of the Quranic verses about the balance (mizan) and the book (kitab). The author asserts that these verses are specifically about disbelievers and the righteous, not about the disobedient believers. The mention of the disobedient is to keep them between hope and fear. He then cites a hadith that those with equal deeds are from al-A'raf and delayed. He then explains the verse 'So We will not establish for them any weight' as meaning no measure or consideration, because the basis is righteous deeds. This guards against misunderstanding that the balance applies to all, whereas here it is for disbelievers.

فَلَا تُقِيمُ لَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ وَزُنًا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Quranic verses about the balance and book apply to all people, including sinful believers, in the same way.
Correction: The author clarifies that these verses are specifically about disbelievers and the righteous; sinful believers are addressed separately with hope and fear, and those with equal deeds are from al-A'raf.

Checkpoint

A) All people equally
B) Disbelievers and the righteous
C) Only the righteous
D) Only the disobedient

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verses about the balance and book are specifically addressed to disbelievers and the righteous; sinful believers are kept between hope and fear, and those with equal deeds are delayed from Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your deeds were weighed today, would you be among the righteous whose weight is established, or among those who rely on hope without action? What one change can you make today to tip the scale?
?
The disobedient believer is left between hope and fear. Does your relationship with Allah lean more toward hope (trusting His mercy) or fear (awareness of His justice)? How does that balance drive you to obedience?
?
The people of al-A'raf have equal deeds and are delayed from Paradise. Are you content with being average, or do you strive for the ranks of the righteous? What specific step will you take this week to increase your good deeds?

Why 'Mawazin' Is Plural in the Quran
Three reasons for the plural 'mawazin' in the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rhetorical reasons scholars give for the Quran's use of the plural form 'mawazin' for the scales of deeds.

Core Idea
The plural 'mawazin' is a rhetorical device, not a literal plurality of scales.

The Quran often uses plural forms where singular might be expected, and this is never accidental. In this passage, the author explains why the word 'mawazin' (scales) appears in the plural even though the scale of deeds is one. The reasons highlight the richness of Quranic expression and its theological depth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice that the passage begins by stating the puzzle: the plural form is used while the scale is one.
2
Identify the three reasons
The passage lists three possible explanations. Try to spot each one and understand the linguistic or theological logic behind it.
The reasons are separated by 'أو' (or).
3
Reflect on the author's conclusion
The author ends by affirming the plural is definite. Consider how each reason relates to the overall purpose of conveying divine justice.
This connects to the broader topic of sam'iyyat (matters heard from revelation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ذكر الموازين بلفظ الجمع والحال أن الميزان واحد نظرا إلى كثرة الخلق على سبيل مقابلة الجمع بالجمع، أو لأجل كبر ذلك الميزان، عبر عنه بلفظ الجمع في ميدان البيان، أو جمع موزون، ولا شك في جمعه.
Then He mentioned 'the scales' in the plural form, while the scale is one, due to the multitude of creation by way of matching plural with plural, or because of the greatness of that scale, He expressed it in the plural form in the field of elucidation, or as a plural of a weighed thing, and there is no doubt about its plural.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is an interpretative explanation. The author addresses why the Quran uses 'mawazin' (plural) when referring to the balance while it is essentially one. He offers three possibilities: 1) matching the plurality of people (jama' muqabala), 2) emphasizing the enormity of the scale, 3) the plural referring to the things weighed (موزون). He concludes that the plural is definite.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran uses plural 'mawazin' because there are multiple scales.
Correction: The plural is rhetorical, either for matching the plurality of people, emphasizing greatness, or referring to the things weighed. There is only one scale of justice.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Quran's use of plural 'mawazin' is a deliberate rhetorical choice, not a literal multiplicity of scales.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The source says the plural might match the multitude of creation. Do you realize that your deeds are among countless others being recorded? Does that make you feel insignificant, or does it drive you to strive harder? How will you ensure your deeds are not lost in the crowd but are heavy on that single scale?

Refuting al-Qunawi on What Is Weighed
The author refutes al-Qunawi's view that only weighty deeds are weighed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author rejects al-Qunawi's narrowing of what is weighed on the Day of Judgment and affirms that all deeds, both good and bad, are weighed.

Core Idea
All deeds are weighed, not only the weighty ones.

Al-Qunawi, a scholar, suggested that only deeds that have weight and significance with Allah are weighed on the Balance. The author of this text corrects this view, emphasizing that the weighing is more general — every act of obedience and disobedience is weighed to manifest the distinction between the allies and enemies of Allah. In this lesson, we examine the author's refutation and the underlying wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Qunawi's claim and its rejection
Read the passage and identify al-Qunawi's statement and the author's immediate correction. Notice the author says 'it is not absolutely true' and expands the scope to all deeds.
Al-Qunawi's view is too restrictive.
2
Grasp the modality and wisdom
Consider the author's mention of weighing scrolls or embodying deeds, and the ultimate purpose: distinguishing allies from enemies, resulting in joy or misery, displaying bounty and justice.
The modality is left open, but the wisdom is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قول القونوي : إن الموزون هو العمل الذي له وزن وخطر عنده سبحانه، فليس على إطلاقه بل الموزون أعم من الطاعة والمعصية حتى يظهر الثقل والخفة بحسب ما تعلقت به الإرادة والمشيئة، ويتوقف فيه على بيان كيفيته سواء يقال بوزن صحائف الأعمال أو بتجسيم الأقوال والأفعال، والحكمة فيه ظهور حال الأولياء من الأعداء، فيكون للأولين أعظم السرور وللآخرين أعظم الشرور وفي الحقيقة إظهار الفضل والعدل في يوم الفصل.
As for the saying of al-Qunawi: 'That which is weighed is the deed that has weight and significance with Him, the Glorified,' it is not absolutely true. Rather, that which is weighed is more general than obedience and disobedience, so that heaviness and lightness appear according to what the will and volition are attached to. And it depends on explaining its modality, whether it is said by weighing the scrolls of deeds or by embodying the words and actions. And the wisdom in it is the manifestation of the state of the allies from the enemies, so that for the former there is the greatest joy and for the latter the greatest evils. In reality, it is the manifestation of bounty and justice on the Day of Decision.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a refutation. Al-Qunawi claimed that only weighty deeds (with significance) are weighed. The author disagrees, stating that all deeds — both obedience and disobedience — are weighed to show differences in weight. He leaves the modality open (scrolls or embodiment). The wisdom is to distinguish allies from enemies, resulting in joy for the former and misery for the latter, thereby showing bounty and justice.

Key Terms

الموزون
صَحَائِف الأعمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Correction: All deeds, both obedient and disobedient, are weighed to show their relative weight according to divine will.

Checkpoint

D) Al-Qunawi said no deeds are weighed.

Key Takeaway
All deeds, good and bad, are weighed on the Day of Judgment to manifest the distinction between the righteous and the wicked.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Imam Abu Hanifa's Affirmation of the Balance and the Book
Imam Abu Hanifa affirms the balance and the book with Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam Abu Hanifa explicitly affirmed the reality of the balance and the book based on Quranic revelation, and why this is important in Sunni creed.

Core Idea
The balance and the book are literal realities affirmed by the Qur'an.

This passage from Imam Abu Hanifa's Al-Wasiyya provides a concise affirmation of two key eschatological matters: the weighing of deeds on a literal balance and the reading of one's personal book of deeds. The Imam grounds these beliefs directly in Quranic verses, showing that they are not allegorical but real events of the Hereafter. This lesson examines his words and their significance for Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation

2

3
Consider the importance of the evidence
Reflect on why Imam Abu Hanifa chose to cite these verses. They show that his creed is based on revelation, not reason alone. This is a hallmark of Sunni theology.
4
Reflect on the literal interpretation
Think about how this passage supports the Sunni position that descriptions of the afterlife are to be taken literally, not allegorized. The Imam does not offer any figurative interpretation.
This connects to the common misunderstanding mentioned in the source.
