Wisdom of the Balance and Giving the Book
The author explains the wisdom behind the balance and the giving of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the wisdom behind the balance on the Day of Judgment and the sequence of giving the book of deeds.

Core Idea
The balance reveals deeds; the book is given before the scale.

In this passage, the author explains why the balance is placed on the Day of Judgment—to make known the exact measures of deeds. He then elaborates on the Quranic verses describing the receipt of the book in the right or left hand, clarifying the terms and the sequence of these events. This lesson will guide you through the deduction and the scriptural support for the order of the balance and the book.

Guided Path
1
Understand the wisdom of the balance
Read the opening sentence about the purpose of the balance. Reflect on why the servants need to know the measures of their deeds.
The wisdom is tied to transparency of reward and punishment.
2
Examine the Quranic descriptions
Read the verses about receiving the book in the right hand or behind the back. Note the different outcomes for each group.
The right hand leads to easy reckoning; the left hand leads to destruction.
3
Determine the sequence
Consider the author's conclusion that giving the book precedes the balance, based on the verse 'he will be judged with an easy reckoning' and the hadith.
This sequence contradicts a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي هذا الاستدلال إيماء إلى أن الحكمة في وضع الميزان للعباد حال المعاد إنما هو معرفة العباد بيان مقادير أعمالهم ليتبين لهم الثواب والعقاب بحسب اختلاف أحوالهم وفيه إشعار بأن إعطاء كتاب الأعمال في أيدي العمال حق أيضاً لقوله تعالى: فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَبُهُ بِيَمِينِهِ فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِسَابًا يَسِيرًا لأي سهلا لا يناقش فيه، وهو أن يجازي على الحسنات ويتجاوز عن السيئات وَيَنْقَلِبُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ مَسْرُ وَران أي بما في الجنة من الحور العين والآدميات أو إلى عشيرته المؤمنين أو إلى فريق المؤمنين وَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَبَه وَرَاءَ ظَهْرِها أي بشماله من وراء ظهره فَسَوْفَ يَدْعُوَاتُبُورًا أي هلاكا يقول : ياتبوراه ويضل سَعِيرًا أي يدخل النار وَإِنَّهُ كَانَ فِي أَهْلِه ، أي في الدنيا مسروران [الانشقاق : ۷-۱۳]، أي باتباع هواه وبدنياه في الكفر بطراً بالمال والجاه، فارغا عن الآخرة. فبين الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله أن الحساب وإعطاء الكتاب متقاربان، فكان حكمهما واحداً حيث لا ينفكان، فلم يذكره الإمام على حدة لابتغاء الاكتفاء، (1) والظاهر أن إعطاء الكتاب قبل ميزان الحساب لقوله تعالى: فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِسَابًا يَسِيرًا [الانشقاق: ٨]، فتفسيره ورد في السنة أن من نوقش في الحساب يوم القيامة عذب.
And in this deduction there is an indication that the wisdom in placing the scale for the servants at the time of the return is only for the servants to know the measures of their deeds so that the reward and punishment become clear to them according to the difference of their states. And in it there is a suggestion that giving the book of deeds into the hands of the workers is also true, according to His statement, the Exalted: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be judged with an easy reckoning' [al-Inshiqaq: 7-8], i.e., easy, without detailed questioning, and he will be rewarded for good deeds and pardoned for bad deeds, 'and he will return to his family joyful' [al-Inshiqaq: 9], i.e., with what is in Paradise of houris and human companions or to his believing relatives or to the group of believers. 'But as for he who is given his book behind his back' [al-Inshiqaq: 10], i.e., in his left hand from behind his back, 'he will call for destruction' [al-Inshiqaq: 11], i.e., destruction, saying 'O woe to me!' 'and he will enter a blazing fire' [al-Inshiqaq: 12]. 'Indeed, he was among his people, in the world, joyful' [al-Inshiqaq: 13], i.e., following his desire and his worldly life in disbelief, arrogantly with wealth and status, heedless of the hereafter. So the Great Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, explained that the reckoning and giving of the book are close, so their ruling is one, as they are inseparable. Thus the Imam did not mention them separately to suffice. And the apparent view is that the giving of the book is before the scale of reckoning, according to His statement: 'He will be judged with an easy reckoning' [al-Inshiqaq: 8]. Its explanation is reported in the Sunnah that whoever is examined in the reckoning on the Day of Resurrection will be punished.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage provides theological exposition and deduction. The author explains that the wisdom of the balance (mizan) is to make known the exact measures of deeds, determining reward and punishment. He then elaborates on the Quranic verses about receiving the book in the right or left hand, explaining the terms. He concludes that giving the book and the reckoning are closely related, and the book is given before the scale based on the verse 'he will be judged with an easy reckoning,' supported by a hadith that detailed examination leads to punishment.

Key Terms
الحكمة
الميزان
الكتاب
الحساب
اليمين
الشمال
وراء الظهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The book of deeds is given after the balance is performed.
Correction: The author argues that the apparent view is that the book is given before the scale, referencing the verse about easy reckoning.

Checkpoint

A) The balance comes first
B) The book is given before the balance
C) They happen simultaneously
D) The order is not specified

Key Takeaway
The balance reveals the exact measures of deeds, and the book of deeds is given before the scale to allow for an easy reckoning for the believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Clarifying the Use of 'Or' in al-Umda
Refutation of Mu'tazila and clarification of wording in al-Umda.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila denial of the balance, reckoning, and book is unfounded, and why the word 'or' in describing the book's delivery does not imply doubt but reflects different Quranic verses.

Core Idea
The 'or' in al-Umda is not doubt but a faithful rendering of two distinct Quranic accounts.

This lesson addresses two things: first, the Mu'tazila's rejection of certain eschatological realities despite clear evidence; second, a potential confusion in a key Matn text where the word 'or' might seem to suggest uncertainty. The author firmly refutes both misapprehensions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila denial
The passage opens by criticizing the Mu'tazila for denying the balance, reckoning, and book, despite decisive proofs. Recognize that this is a theological refutation.
The author uses strong language: 'deficient intellects'.
2
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how the author moves from general refutation to a specific clarification about wording.
3
Examine the 'or' issue
Focus on the second part: the wording in al-Umda that a disbeliever's book is given 'in his left hand or from behind his back.' The author explains that 'or' does not indicate doubt but accounts for differences in Quranic verses.
The sentence is incomplete but the intended meaning is clear.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how theological assertions must be understood in light of scriptural sources, and that variations in expression can be due to multiple revealed accounts.

Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and clarification. First, the author condemns the Mu'tazila for denying the balance, reckoning, and book despite decisive evidence. Second, he addresses a potential confusion in a work called 'al-Umda' where it says the disbeliever's book is given 'in his left hand OR from behind his back.' This might imply doubt, but the author explains the 'or' is due to two different Quranic verses, not uncertainty. The scale and book of deeds reveal the exact measures of our actions for fair recompense.

Sanusi explains the profound wisdom behind the divine balance and the book of deeds. These are not arbitrary tests but tools for the servants to know their deeds' magnitudes. The passage also defends these realities against those who deny them, grounding the argument in explicit Quranic verses.

وفي هذا الاستدلال إيماء إلى أن الحكمة في وضع الميزان للعباد حال المعاد إنما هو معرفة العباد بيان مقادير أعمالهم ليتبين لهم الثواب والعقاب بحسب اختلاف أحوالهم وفيه إشعار بأن إعطاء كتاب الأعمال في أيدي العمال حق أيضاً لقوله تعالى: فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَابَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِسَابًا يَسِيرًا أي سهلا لا يناقش فيه، وهو أن يجازي على الحسنات ويتجاوز عن السيئات وَيَنْقَلِبُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ مَسْرُورًا أي بما في الجنة من الحور العين والآدميات أو إلى عشيرته المؤمنين أو إلى فريق المؤمنين وَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَابَهُ وَرَاءَ ظَهْرِهِ أي بشماله من وراء ظهره فَسَوْفَ يَدْعُو ثُبُورًا أي هلاكا يقول: يا ثبوراه ويَصْلَى سَعِيرًا أي يدخل النار وَإِنَّهُ كَانَ فِي أَهْلِهِ أي في الدنيا مَسْرُورًا [الانشقاق: 7-13]، أي باتباع هواه وبِدنياه في الكفر بطراً بالمال والجاه، فارغا عن الآخرة. فبين الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله أن الحساب وإعطاء الكتاب متقاربان، فكان حكمهما واحداً حيث لا ينفكان، فلم يذكره الإمام على حدة لابتغاء الاكتفاء. (1) والظاهر أن إعطاء الكتاب قبل ميزان الحساب لقوله تعالى: فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِسَابًا يَسِيرًا [الانشقاق: 8]، فتفسيره ورد في السنة أن من نوقش في الحساب يوم القيامة عذب. وقد أنكر المعتزلة الميزان والحساب والكتاب بعقولهم الناقصة مع وجود الأدلة القاطعة في كل من هذه الأبواب. وأما ما وقع في "العمدة" من أن كتاب الكافر يعطى بشماله أو من وراء ظهره فيوهم أنه شاك متردد في أمره وليس كذلك، بل ذكره بأو لاختلاف ما جاء في الآيتين، وهو إما محمول على الشك. فبعضهم يعطى بشماله وهو القريب من الإسلام وبعضهم يعطى من وراء ظهره وهو المدبر بالكلية عن قبول الأحكام، وهي كتب كتبها الحفظة أيام حياتهم إلى حين مماتهم، كما قال الله تعالى: أَمْ يَحْسَبُونَ أَنَّا لَا نَسْمَعُ سِرَّهُمْ وَنَجْوَاهُمْ بَلَى وَرُسُلُنَا لَدَيْهِمْ يَكْتُبُونَ [الزخرف: 80]، أي جميع أفعالهم وأحوالهم، وفيه رد على من زعم أن الملائكة ليس لهم اطلاع على بواطن الخلق.
And in this inference there is a hint that the wisdom in setting up the balance for the servants at the time of the return is only that the servants know the measures of their deeds so that reward and punishment become clear to them according to the difference of their states. And in it there is an indication that giving the book of deeds into the hands of the doers is also true because of His statement the Exalted: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be reckoned with an easy reckoning' (Al-Inshiqaq 7-8) meaning easy, in which there is no scrutiny, and that is that he is rewarded for good deeds and pardoned for evil deeds. 'And he will return to his family joyful' (Al-Inshiqaq 9) meaning by what is in Paradise of houris and human women, or to his believing relatives, or to the group of believers. 'But as for he who is given his book behind his back' (Al-Inshiqaq 10) meaning with his left hand from behind his back, 'he will call for destruction' (Al-Inshiqaq 11) meaning perdition, saying 'O destruction!' 'And he will burn in a blazing fire' (Al-Inshiqaq 12) meaning he enters the Fire. 'Indeed, he was among his family joyful' (Al-Inshiqaq 13) meaning in the world, i.e., following his desire and his worldly life in disbelief, insolently delighting in wealth and status, heedless of the Hereafter. So the Great Imam (may Allah have mercy on him) explained that the reckoning and the giving of the book are close together, so their ruling is one as they are inseparable, so the Imam did not mention them separately seeking conciseness. (1) And the apparent is that the giving of the book precedes the scale of reckoning because of His statement the Exalted: 'He will be reckoned with an easy reckoning' (Al-Inshiqaq 8), and its interpretation has come in the Sunna that whoever is scrutinized in the reckoning on the Day of Resurrection will be punished. And the Mu'tazila denied the balance, the reckoning, and the book with their deficient intellects despite the existence of decisive evidence in each of these subjects. As for what occurred in 'al-'Umdah' that the book of the disbeliever is given with his left hand or from behind his back, it suggests that he is a doubter, hesitant in his affair, but it is not so; rather he mentioned it with 'or' due to the difference in what came in the two verses, and it is either interpreted as doubt. Some of them are given with their left hand, and they are those close to Islam, and some of them are given from behind their back, and they are those who totally turn away from accepting the rulings. And these are books written by the recording angels during their days of life until the time of their death, as Allah the Exalted said: 'Or do they think that We hear not their secrets and their private conversation? Yes, and Our messengers (angels) are with them recording' (Az-Zukhruf 80), meaning all their actions and states. And in it is a refutation of those who claim that the angels have no knowledge of the inner states of creatures.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the wisdom behind the scale (mizan) and the book of deeds on the Day of Judgment, as well as a refutation of the Mu'tazila who deny these. It begins by stating that the purpose of setting up the balance is for the servants to know the exact quantities of their deeds, so that reward and punishment are clear based on their different states. It also asserts that giving the book of deeds to each person is a reality, supported by Quranic verses from Surat al-Inshiqaq (7-13). The passage then explains these verses: the one who receives his book in his right hand will have an easy reckoning, meaning no harsh scrutiny, and will return to his family joyfully—interpreted as enjoying the pleasures of Paradise. The one who receives his book behind his back (i.e., in his left hand) will call for destruction and enter the Fire. The Great Imam (Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him) indicates that the reckoning and the giving of the book are closely related and cannot be separated, so he did not discuss them separately for brevity. The passage then notes that the giving of the book precedes the weighing of deeds, citing the verse 'he will be reckoned with an easy reckoning' and a hadith that those who are scrutinized in the reckoning will be punished. It strongly refutes the Mu'tazila who deny the balance, reckoning, and book, calling their intellects deficient despite the clear evidences. The passage also addresses a potential confusion from the book 'al-'Umdah' regarding whether the disbeliever's book is given with his left hand or from behind his back, explaining that the 'or' indicates different scenarios depending on the person's state: some are close to Islam, others are totally turned away. Finally, it cites the Quranic verse from Az-Zukhruf (80) to affirm that the recording angels write all actions and states, and this refutes those who deny the angels' knowledge of inner matters.

الكتاب
الحساب
المعتزلة
الحفظة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The use of 'or' in describing how the disbeliever receives his book means the text is uncertain.
Correction: The author clarifies that 'or' is used due to different scenarios: some disbelievers receive their book with the left hand, others from behind the back.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the Imam (Abu Hanifa) did not mention the reckoning and the giving of the book separately?
A) Because they are impossible to separate.
B) Because they are both denied by the Mu'tazila.
C) For brevity, as they are close together and their ruling is one.
D) Because the book is given before the reckoning.

Key Takeaway
The scale and book of deeds are real and serve to show the exact measures of deeds, and the Mu'tazila's denial is refuted by clear Quranic evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you realize that every secret thought and private moment is recorded by the angels, what hidden sin are you still clinging to that you would be ashamed to see in your book? Will you repent from it today, before it is too late?
?
The book is given to some in their right hand (joy) and to others from behind (destruction). If you were to die right now, which hand do you truly expect to receive your book in? What change in your daily life would make that expectation certain?
?
The Mu'tazila denied the scale and book because their intellects could not grasp them. Are there any Islamic teachings about the unseen that you hesitate to fully accept because they seem illogical to you? Are you willing to submit your reason to revelation, as the righteous scholars did, even when it contradicts your assumptions?

The Reality of Qisas on the Day of Judgment
Explains the doctrine of qisas between people on the Day of Judgment and its proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of retribution (qisas) on the Day of Judgment, how it is carried out through good deeds and sins, and its scriptural proof.

Core Idea
On Judgment Day, justice is served by transferring good deeds and sins, not money.

This lesson explains the reality of qisas—retribution between people—on the Day of Judgment. The author begins by defining qisas as punishment by equivalence, then clarifies that since there is no material currency, compensation takes place through good deeds and sins. He then provides a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that illustrates this principle and warns believers to settle their disputes before that day.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the full English translation to grasp the flow.
Notice the technical terms like 'al-qisas' and 'al-hasanat'.
2
Understand the definition of qisas
Identify how the author defines qisas: punishment by equivalence between opponents on the Day of Resurrection. Note that it involves taking good deeds from the wrongdoer.
3
Identify the mechanism of retribution
Find the explanation that if the wrongdoer has good deeds, they are taken proportionally; if not, the sins of the wronged are placed on him.
This is the core doctrine: transfer of hasanat and sayyi'at.
4
Note the hadith proof
Locate the hadith of the Prophet (saw) that supports this. It emphasizes settling wrongs now before there is no currency.
The hadith about the bankrupt (muflis) is started but cut off.
5
Reflect on the implication
Think about how this teaching encourages believers to seek forgiveness and settle disputes in this life.
Connects to practical piety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقصاص أي المعاقبة بالمماثلة فيما بين الخصوم أي من نوع الإنسان والعباد يوم القيامة أي بالحسنات كما في نسخة حق أي ثابت يعني بأخذ حسنات الظالم وإعطائها للخصوم في مقابلة المظالم، إذ ليس هناك الدنانير والدراهم، فإن لم يكن لهم أي للظلمة الحسنات أي بأن لم يوجد لهم الطاعات أو فنيت لكثرة السيئات طرح وفي نسخة: فطرح السيئات أي وضع سيئات المظلومين عليهم أي على رقبة الظالمين جائز وحق وفي نسخة: حق جائز وكلاهما للتأكيد، ومعناهما ثابت وجائز عقلا ووارد نقلا، فيجب الاعتماد على هذا الاعتقاد لما ورد من أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: من كانت له مظلمة لأخيه فليتحلله اليوم قبل أن لا يكون دينار ولا درهم إن كان له عمل صالح أخذ منه بقدر مظلمته وإن لم يكن له حسنات أخذ سيئات صاحبه فحمل عليه. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام لأصحابه الكرام: أتدرون من المفلس؟ قالوا: المفلس فينا من...
And Al-Qisas (retribution), meaning punishment by equivalence between the opponents (i.e., among human beings and servants) on the Day of Resurrection, i.e., with good deeds according to one version, is true (haqq), meaning established. It means taking the good deeds of the wrongdoer and giving them to the opponents in exchange for the wrongs, since there are no dinars or dirhams there. If the wrongdoers do not have good deeds, i.e., if they have no acts of obedience or their good deeds have been exhausted due to many sins, then the sins of the wronged are placed upon them (the wrongdoers). This is permissible (ja'iz) and true (haqq) – in another version: 'true, permissible' – both for emphasis. Their meaning is that it is established and permissible rationally and transmitted textually, so one must rely on this belief because of what has come that he (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'Whoever has a wrong against his brother, let him seek his pardon today before there is no dirham and no dinar. If he has righteous deeds, they will be taken from him in proportion to his wrong; and if he has no good deeds, some of the bad deeds of his fellow will be taken and laid upon him.' And he (peace and blessings be upon him) said to his noble companions: 'Do you know who the bankrupt (muflis) is?' They said: 'The bankrupt among us is...'
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage defines and proves the reality of al-Qisas (retribution) between people on the Day of Judgment. It begins by stating that Qisas is punishment by equivalence between opponents (people and servants) on the Day of Resurrection. Since there are no material currencies like dinars and dirhams, the retribution takes place through good deeds: the good deeds of the wrongdoer (the one who oppressed) are taken and given to the wronged (the one who was oppressed) in proportion to the wrong. If the wrongdoer has no good deeds (either because he performed no acts of obedience or his good deeds have been exhausted due to many sins), then the sins of the wronged are placed upon the wrongdoer. The passage emphasizes that this is both rationally permissible and textually established (thabit), and therefore must be believed. It then cites a hadith where the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) warns that if someone has a wrong against his brother, he should seek a deal now before there is no currency; instead, if he has good deeds, they will be taken in proportion to the wrong, and if not, the sins of the wronged will be placed on him. The passage also begins to quote another hadith about the bankrupt (muflis), but it is cut off, implying that the bankrupt is one who comes with good deeds but also has wrongs, and his good deeds are given to others until nothing remains, then sins are placed on him.

Key Terms
القصاص (al-qisas)
الخصوم (al-khusum)
المظالم (al-mazalim)
الحسنات (al-hasanat)
السيئات (al-sayyi'at)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qisas is only physical retaliation in this world (e.g., eye for an eye) and does not apply to the afterlife.
Correction: The passage clarifies that on the Day of Judgment, qisas is not physical but involves the transfer of good deeds and sins, as there will be no material currency.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is retribution exacted if the wrongdoer has no good deeds on the Day of Judgment?
A) He will be punished in hell without further action.
B) The sins of the wronged are placed upon the wrongdoer.
C) The wrongdoer is made to pay with actual money.
D) The wrongdoer's bad deeds are doubled.

Key Takeaway
Qisas on the Day of Judgment operates through the transfer of good deeds and sins, as established by hadith, and believers are urged to settle their disputes in this life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a person you have wronged, even in a small way. Are you carrying the weight of that wrong? Today, will you seek their forgiveness, knowing that on the Day of Judgment your own good deeds may be taken away because of it? What specific step will you take to make amends?
?
If you are the one who has been wronged, does your heart demand revenge? This lesson tells you that on the Day of Judgment, justice will be served perfectly. Can you forgive now, trusting that Allah will not let you lose? What would it cost you to let go of that grudge today?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) called the one who wrongs others and then loses his good deeds a 'bankrupt'. Do you have any relationships or interactions where you have acted unjustly? How will you ensure you are not among the bankrupt on that Day? Write down one area you need to address and a concrete action to start today.

Retribution Through Good and Bad Deeds
Explains the mechanism of qisas with deeds and the hadith of the bankrupt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how retribution between opponents on Judgment Day operates through the exchange of good and bad deeds, based on Quranic and prophetic evidence.

Core Idea
On Judgment Day, justice is served by transferring good deeds or bad deeds — not money.

This passage from the sharh explains the doctrine of qisas (retribution) between individuals on the Day of Judgment. Since there will be no currency, Allah will use our deeds as the medium of exchange. The author cites the Quran and a famous hadith to establish this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two scenarios: taking good deeds from oppressor or giving bad deeds of the oppressed.
2
Identify the mechanism of qisas
The passage presents two ways retribution occurs: either good deeds are taken from the oppressor, or if he has none, the bad deeds of the wronged are placed on him. This is the core idea.
3
Study the supporting Quranic verse
The passage cites Quran 43:80 about angels recording all deeds. Notice how this refutes those who deny angels' knowledge of inner states.
The verse supports the idea that all deeds are accounted for.
4
Examine the hadith of the bankrupt
The Prophet ﷺ describes the true bankrupt: one who comes with prayers, fasting, and charity but has wronged others. His good deeds are given to his victims, and if exhausted, their sins are placed on him.
This hadith illustrates the mechanism in a vivid narrative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقصاص فيما بين الخصوم يوم القيامة حق، فإن لم يكن لهم الحسنات طرح السيئات عليهم جائز وحق على الجمع بينهما كما أشرنا إليها، وإما للتنويع، فبعضهم يعطى بشماله وهو القريب من الإسلام وبعضهم يعطى من وراء ظهره وهو المدبر بالكلية عن قبول الأحكام، وهي كتب كتبها الحفظة أيام حياتهم إلى حين مماتهم، كما قال الله تعالى: أَمْ يَحْسَبُونَ أَنَّا لَا نَسْمَعُ سِرَّهُمْ وَنَجُوابِهِم أَي ما يخفونه من الغير وما يتكلمون به فيما بينهم على أي نسمعها وَرُسُلُنَا أي الحفظة لَدَيْهِمْ يَكْتُبُونَ ﴾ [الزخرف: 80]، أي جميع أفعالهم وأحوالهم، وفيه ردّ على من زعم أنّ الملائكة ليس لهم اطلاع على بواطن الخلق. والقصاص أي المعاقبة بالمماثلة فيما بين الخصوم أي من نوع الإنسان والعباد يوم القيامة أي بالحسنات كما في نسخة حق أي ثابت يعنى بأخذ حسنات الظالم وإعطائها للخصوم في مقابلة المظالم، إذ ليس هناك الدنانير والدراهم، فإن لم يكن لهم أي للظلمة الحسنات أي بأن لم يوجد لهم الطاعات أو فنيت لكثرة السيئات طرح وفي نسخة: فطرح السيئات أى وضع سيئات المظلومين عليهم أي على رقبة الظالمين جائز وحق وفي نسخة: حق جائز وكلاهما للتأكيد، ومعناهما ثابت وجائز عقلا ووارد نقلا، فيجب الاعتماد على هذا الاعتقاد لما ورد من أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: من كانت له مظلمة لأخيه فليتحلله اليوم قبل أن لا يكون دينار ولا درهم إن كان له عمل صالح أخذ منه بقدر مظلمته وإن لم يكن له حسنات أخذ سيئات صاحبه فحمل عليه . وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام لأصحابه الكرام أتدرون من المفلس؟ قالوا: المفلس فينا من لا درهم له ولا متاع فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: إن المفلس من يأتي يوم القيامة بصلاة وصيام وصدقة وقد شتم هذا وقذف هذا وأكل مال هذا وسفك دم هذا وضرب هذا، فيعطى هذا من حسناته وهذا من حسناته فإن فنيت حسناته قبل أن يقضى ما عليه أخذ من خطاياهم فطرحت عليه ثم طرح في النار. ثم هذا في حق العباد، وقد ورد في خصومة الحيوانات أنه سبحانه يقتص للشاة الجماء من القرناء ثم يقول لها: كوني ترابا وحينئذ يقول الكافر الظالم الفاجر : لَيْتَنِي كُنتُ تُرَابًا [النبأ: 40].
The retribution between the opponents on the Day of Judgment is true. If they (the oppressors) do not have good deeds, the evil deeds (of the oppressed) are thrown upon them; it is permissible and true. The combination of the two (has been indicated) as we have referred to, or it (the giving) is for diversification: some are given with their left hand—they are those close to Islam; and some are given from behind their back—they are those who have completely turned away from accepting the rulings. They are books that the recording angels wrote during their (the people's) lives until their deaths, as Allah Almighty said: 'Or do they think that We hear not their secrets and their private conversation? Yes, [We do], and Our messengers (angels) are with them recording.' (Az-Zukhruf 43:80) — i.e., all their actions and states. And in this is a refutation of those who claim that the angels have no knowledge of the inner states of creation. And 'al-qisas' means punishment by equivalence between the opponents i.e., among humans and servants on the Day of Judgment — i.e., by (exchange of) good deeds, as in one version — 'haqq' means established: it means taking the good deeds of the oppressor and giving them to the opponents in exchange for the wrongs, since there are no dinars and dirhams there. If they (the oppressors) do not have good deeds — i.e., if they have no acts of obedience or they have been exhausted due to many evil deeds — then the evil deeds (of the oppressed) are thrown — and in one version: 'then thrown' — i.e., the evil deeds of the wronged are placed upon them, i.e., upon the neck of the oppressors; 'ja'iz wa haqq' (permissible and true) — and in one version: 'haqq ja'iz' — both are for emphasis, meaning established and permissible rationally and transmitted textually, so it is obligatory to rely on this belief because of what has been reported: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever has a wrong against his brother, let him seek his pardon today before there is no dinar and no dirham; if he has righteous deeds, some of them will be taken in proportion to his wrong; if he has no good deeds, then evil deeds of his companion will be taken and loaded upon him.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to his noble companions: 'Do you know who the bankrupt is?' They said: 'The bankrupt among us is one who has no dirham and no property.' He said: 'The bankrupt is one who comes on the Day of Judgment with prayer, fasting, and charity, but he insulted this one, slandered that one, consumed the wealth of this one, shed the blood of that one, and beat this one. Then this one will be given from his good deeds, and that one from his good deeds. If his good deeds are exhausted before he settles what is due, then some of their sins will be taken and thrown upon him, and then he will be thrown into the Fire.' Then this (retribution) is concerning the servants. And it has been reported concerning the dispute of animals that He (Glory be to Him) exacts retribution for the hornless sheep from the horned one, then He says to it: 'Be dust!' And at that time the disbelieving, oppressive, immoral person says: 'O would that I were dust!' (An-Naba' 78:40).
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the concept of al-qisas (retribution) on the Day of Judgment as an established truth in Islamic theology. It begins by affirming that retribution between opponents (al-khusum) is true (haqq). The commentator explains the mechanism: if the oppressor has no good deeds to give in compensation, the evil deeds of the wronged are placed upon the oppressor. This is both permissible (ja'iz) and true (haqq), rationally and textually. The passage then clarifies two possible ways of giving on that Day: some receive their book in their left hand (those close to Islam but rebellious), and some receive it from behind (those completely averse). Then it cites Qur'an 43:80 about angels recording deeds, refuting those who deny angels' knowledge of inner states. The commentator then unpacks the term 'qisas' as punishment by equivalence using good deeds instead of money, citing a hadith urging reconciliation before Judgment Day. He also relates the famous hadith about the true bankrupt (muflis) who will have his good deeds distributed to those he wronged; if none remain, their sins are placed on him. The passage concludes by extending this retribution to animals, where the aweless sheep gets retribution from the horned one, after which they become dust—a cause for the disbeliever to wish the same. The overall argument follows the source's order: definition, textual proof from Qur'an and hadith, and an eschatological illustration.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that retribution on Judgment Day involves physical currency or is only about punishment without compensation.
Correction: The passage clarifies that retribution uses good and bad deeds as exchange, not money, and can involve compensation to the wronged through transfer of deeds.

Animal Retribution and the Disbeliever's Envy
Describes retribution for animals and the disbeliever's wish to be dust.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that retribution extends to animals on Judgment Day, and that the disbeliever will come to envy their fate of becoming dust.

Core Idea
Even animals receive justice on Judgment Day, after which they become dust—a fate the disbeliever will desperately wish for.

This passage extends the concept of qisas beyond humans to animals, reporting that Allah will exact retribution for the hornless sheep from the horned one, then command them to become dust. At that moment, the disbeliever will exclaim, "O would that I were dust!"—a profound indication of the regret and despair of the wicked.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage aloud
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how succinctly the idea is presented: retribution for animals, then dust, then the disbeliever's cry.
The passage transitions from human qisas to animal qisas.
2
Identify the key elements
There are three parts: (1) retribution for animals, (2) they become dust after that, (3) the disbeliever's wish to be dust. Consider the connection between them.
3
Reflect on the disbeliever's reaction
Why does the disbeliever say 'O would that I were dust'? This shows the severity of the situation for wrongdoers, as they see that even animals find peace in non-existence after justice is served.
This is a powerful eschatological scene.
4
Connect to the broader lesson
This passage shows that Allah's justice is absolute, extending even to animals. It also highlights the regret of those who rejected faith and oppressed others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقصاص فيما بين الخصوم يوم القيامة حق، فإن لم يكن لهم الحسنات طرح السيئات عليهم جائز وحق على الجمع بينهما كما أشرنا إليها، وإما للتنويع، فبعضهم يعطى بشماله وهو القريب من الإسلام وبعضهم يعطى من وراء ظهره وهو المدبر بالكلية عن قبول الأحكام، وهي كتب كتبها الحفظة أيام حياتهم إلى حين مماتهم، كما قال الله تعالى: أَمْ يَحْسَبُونَ أَنَّا لَا نَسْمَعُ سِرَّهُمْ وَنَجُوابِهِم أَي ما يخفونه من الغير وما يتكلمون به فيما بينهم على أي نسمعها وَرُسُلُنَا أي الحفظة لَدَيْهِمْ يَكْتُبُونَ ﴾ [الزخرف: 80]، أي جميع أفعالهم وأحوالهم، وفيه ردّ على من زعم أنّ الملائكة ليس لهم اطلاع على بواطن الخلق. والقصاص أي المعاقبة بالمماثلة فيما بين الخصوم أي من نوع الإنسان والعباد يوم القيامة أي بالحسنات كما في نسخة حق أي ثابت يعنى بأخذ حسنات الظالم وإعطائها للخصوم في مقابلة المظالم، إذ ليس هناك الدنانير والدراهم، فإن لم يكن لهم أي للظلمة الحسنات أي بأن لم يوجد لهم الطاعات أو فنيت لكثرة السيئات طرح وفي نسخة: فطرح السيئات أى وضع سيئات المظلومين عليهم أي على رقبة الظالمين جائز وحق وفي نسخة: حق جائز وكلاهما للتأكيد، ومعناهما ثابت وجائز عقلا ووارد نقلا، فيجب الاعتماد على هذا الاعتقاد لما ورد من أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: من كانت له مظلمة لأخيه فليتحلله اليوم قبل أن لا يكون دينار ولا درهم إن كان له عمل صالح أخذ منه بقدر مظلمته وإن لم يكن له حسنات أخذ سيئات صاحبه فحمل عليه . وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام لأصحابه الكرام أتدرون من المفلس؟ قالوا: المفلس فينا من لا درهم له ولا متاع فقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: إن المفلس من يأتي يوم القيامة بصلاة وصيام وصدقة وقد شتم هذا وقذف هذا وأكل مال هذا وسفك دم هذا وضرب هذا، فيعطى هذا من حسناته وهذا من حسناته فإن فنيت حسناته قبل أن يقضى ما عليه أخذ من خطاياهم فطرحت عليه ثم طرح في النار. ثم هذا في حق العباد، وقد ورد في خصومة الحيوانات أنه سبحانه يقتص للشاة الجماء من القرناء ثم يقول لها: كوني ترابا وحينئذ يقول الكافر الظالم الفاجر : لَيْتَنِي كُنتُ تُرَابًا [النبأ: 40].
The retribution between the opponents on the Day of Judgment is true. If they (the oppressors) do not have good deeds, the evil deeds (of the oppressed) are thrown upon them; it is permissible and true. The combination of the two (has been indicated) as we have referred to, or it (the giving) is for diversification: some are given with their left hand—they are those close to Islam; and some are given from behind their back—they are those who have completely turned away from accepting the rulings. They are books that the recording angels wrote during their (the people's) lives until their deaths, as Allah Almighty said: 'Or do they think that We hear not their secrets and their private conversation? Yes, [We do], and Our messengers (angels) are with them recording.' (Az-Zukhruf 43:80) — i.e., all their actions and states. And in this is a refutation of those who claim that the angels have no knowledge of the inner states of creation. And 'al-qisas' means punishment by equivalence between the opponents i.e., among humans and servants on the Day of Judgment — i.e., by (exchange of) good deeds, as in one version — 'haqq' means established: it means taking the good deeds of the oppressor and giving them to the opponents in exchange for the wrongs, since there are no dinars and dirhams there. If they (the oppressors) do not have good deeds — i.e., if they have no acts of obedience or they have been exhausted due to many evil deeds — then the evil deeds (of the oppressed) are thrown — and in one version: 'then thrown' — i.e., the evil deeds of the wronged are placed upon them, i.e., upon the neck of the oppressors; 'ja'iz wa haqq' (permissible and true) — and in one version: 'haqq ja'iz' — both are for emphasis, meaning established and permissible rationally and transmitted textually, so it is obligatory to rely on this belief because of what has been reported: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever has a wrong against his brother, let him seek his pardon today before there is no dinar and no dirham; if he has righteous deeds, some of them will be taken in proportion to his wrong; if he has no good deeds, then evil deeds of his companion will be taken and loaded upon him.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to his noble companions: 'Do you know who the bankrupt is?' They said: 'The bankrupt among us is one who has no dirham and no property.' He said: 'The bankrupt is one who comes on the Day of Judgment with prayer, fasting, and charity, but he insulted this one, slandered that one, consumed the wealth of this one, shed the blood of that one, and beat this one. Then this one will be given from his good deeds, and that one from his good deeds. If his good deeds are exhausted before he settles what is due, then some of their sins will be taken and thrown upon him, and then he will be thrown into the Fire.' Then this (retribution) is concerning the servants. And it has been reported concerning the dispute of animals that He (Glory be to Him) exacts retribution for the hornless sheep from the horned one, then He says to it: 'Be dust!' And at that time the disbelieving, oppressive, immoral person says: 'O would that I were dust!' (An-Naba' 78:40).
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the concept of al-qisas (retribution) on the Day of Judgment as an established truth in Islamic theology. It begins by affirming that retribution between opponents (al-khusum) is true (haqq). The commentator explains the mechanism: if the oppressor has no good deeds to give in compensation, the evil deeds of the wronged are placed upon the oppressor. This is both permissible (ja'iz) and true (haqq), rationally and textually. The passage then clarifies two possible ways of giving on that Day: some receive their book in their left hand (those close to Islam but rebellious), and some receive it from behind (those completely averse). Then it cites Qur'an 43:80 about angels recording deeds, refuting those who deny angels' knowledge of inner states. The commentator then unpacks the term 'qisas' as punishment by equivalence using good deeds instead of money, citing a hadith urging reconciliation before Judgment Day. He also relates the famous hadith about the true bankrupt (muflis) who will have his good deeds distributed to those he wronged; if none remain, their sins are placed on him. The passage concludes by extending this retribution to animals, where the aweless sheep gets retribution from the horned one, after which they become dust—a cause for the disbeliever to wish the same. The overall argument follows the source's order: definition, textual proof from Qur'an and hadith, and an eschatological illustration.

القرناء
تراب
الكافر

Key Takeaway
The justice of Allah extends to all creatures, and even animals will be given retribution, leaving the disbeliever longing for non-existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The disbeliever's wish is not for Paradise but for complete annihilation. What does that tell you about the terror of standing before Allah without faith? How can you ensure your own heart trembles at His warning and not just at the sight of others' punishment?
?
You have heard that even a hornless sheep will have its right taken from a horned one. Does this reality change how you treat those you consider 'lesser'—servants, animals, the weak? Will you act on that change today?

The Reality of the Prophet's Pool
Affirmation of the Pool and its Quranic proof, interpretation of Kawthar, and scholary views on location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the existence of the Prophet's Pool is a confirmed reality based on the Quran and scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Pool is a literal reality, not a metaphor.

This lesson establishes the foundational belief in the Prophet's Pool (al-Hawd) as a true eschatological feature. We examine the Quranic verse on al-Kawthar and how scholars interpret it as referring to the Pool or a River, reconciling the two. We also learn about its location relative to the Bridge (Sirat) and the Balance (Mizan).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. It begins with the affirmation of the Pool and cites the Quranic verse. Then it explains the interpretation of Kawthar.
Notice the use of 'حق' to assert reality.
2
Understand the Quranic basis
The author cites Surah al-Kawthar as proof. Reflect on how the majority interpret it as the Pool or River.
3
Examine the scholarly discussion on location
The passage mentions a difference of opinion whether the Pool is before or after the Sirat. The author favors before. Al-Qurtubi's view of two pools is also mentioned.
This shows the scholarly depth on this topic.
4
Synthesize key points
Summarize: The Pool is real, based on Quran, interpreted as Kawthar, located at the standing-place, with some details about before/after Sirat.
This aligns with the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحوض النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حق لقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا أَعْطَيْنَاكَ الْكَوْثَرَ﴾ [الكوثر: 1] وفسره الجمهور بحوضه أو نهره ولا تنافي بينهما؛ لأن نهره في الجنة وحوضه في موقف القيامة على خلاف في أنه قبل الصراط أو بعده وهو الأقرب والأنسب. وقال القرطبي: وهما حوضان أحدهما قبل الصراط وقبل الميزان على الأصح، فإن الناس يخرجون عطاشاً من قبورهم فيردونه قبل الميزان والصراط. والثاني في الجنة وكلاهما يسمى كوثرا. انتهى. وروى الترمذي وحسنه أنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم قال: ((إن لكل نبي حوضا وإنهم يتباهون أيهم أكثر واردة وإني أرجو أن أكون أكثرهم واردة)). هذا، ونقل القرطبي أن من خالف جماعة المسلمين كالخوارج والروافض والمعتزلة وكذا الظلمة والفسقة الملعونة يطردون عن الحوض لما وقع منهم من الخوض وحديث الحوض رواه بضع وثلاثون من الصحابة، وكاد أن يكون متواترا. وقد ورد حديث: حوضي في الجنة مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيض من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، طعمه ألذ وأحلى من العسل وأبرد من الثلج وألين من الزبد، وحافتاه من الزبرجد، وأوانيه من الفضة وكيزانه كنجوم السماء، من شرب منه شربة لا يظمأ بعدها أبداً. وعن أكثر السلف هو الخير الكثير. وفي الأحاديث الصحاح: ((هو نهر في الجنة عليه خير كثير ترد عليه أمتي يوم القيامة)). وقيل: هو النبوة والقرآن.
The Pool (Hawd) of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is true, because of the saying of the Exalted: 'Indeed, We have given you al-Kawthar' [Kawthar: 1]. The majority interpreted it as his Pool or his River, and there is no contradiction between them, because his River is in Paradise and his Pool is at the standing-place of the Resurrection, with a difference of opinion as to whether it is before the Bridge (Sirat) or after it, and the former is the more likely and more appropriate. Al-Qurtubi said: There are two pools: one before the Bridge and before the Balance (Mizan) according to the soundest view, for people will come out thirsty from their graves and will go to it before the Balance and the Bridge. The second is in Paradise, and both are called Kawthar. End. Al-Tirmidhi narrated and authenticated that he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Every prophet has a pool, and they boast about which of them has more visitors, and I hope to have the most visitors.' This, and al-Qurtubi reported that those who oppose the community of Muslims, such as the Kharijites, the Rafidites, the Mu'tazilites, and likewise the oppressors and the cursed sinners, are driven away from the Pool because of their involvement (in innovation). The hadith about the Pool was narrated by thirty-odd Companions and is nearly mass-transmitted. A hadith has come: 'My Pool is in Paradise, a distance of one month, and its corners are equal; its water is whiter than milk, its scent more fragrant than musk, its taste more delicious and sweeter than honey, colder than snow, softer than butter; its rim is of chrysolite, its vessels of silver, its pitchers like the stars of the sky; whoever drinks a drink from it will never thirst after it forever.' According to most of the Salaf, it is abundant good. In the authentic hadiths: 'It is a river in Paradise upon which there is abundant good; my community will come to it on the Day of Resurrection.' And it was said: It is prophethood and the Qur'an.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage affirms and describes the reality of the Prophet Muhammad's Pool (al-Hawd), an eschatological feature. The author begins by stating that the Pool is true (ḥaqq), citing the Quranic verse 'Indeed, We have given you al-Kawthar' (108:1). He notes that the majority of scholars interpret 'al-Kawthar' as either the Pool or the River in Paradise, and that there is no contradiction: the River is in Paradise, while the Pool is at the standing-place of the Day of Resurrection. There is a scholarly difference over whether the Pool is before or after the Sirat (Bridge); the author favors it being before the Sirat. He then quotes al-Qurtubi, who mentions two pools: one before the Sirat and the Balance (al-Mizan), where people come out thirsty from their graves and drink, and another in Paradise; both are called Kawthar. The author then cites a hadith from al-Tirmidhi: every prophet has a pool, and they boast about the number of visitors; the Prophet hopes to have the most visitors. Next, he reports al-Qurtubi's view that those who oppose the Muslim community—like the Kharijites, Rafidites, Mu'tazilites, oppressors, and cursed sinners—are driven away from the Pool. The hadith about the Pool is narrated by over thirty Companions and is nearly mass-transmitted (mutawatir). The author then provides a detailed description of the Pool from another hadith: its size, water, scent, taste, temperature, rim, vessels, and that drinking from it quenches thirst forever. He mentions that most Salaf interpret 'Kawthar' as abundant good, and authentic hadiths say it is a river in Paradise. Finally, he notes an alternative interpretation: it signifies prophethood and the Qur'an. The passage thus establishes the Pool as a real, blessed feature of the afterlife, supported by revelation and tradition.

Key Terms
حوض
كوثر
الصراط
الميزان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Pool is merely a metaphor or has no basis in Quran.
Correction: The author affirms it as true (ḥaqq) and cites the Quran directly.

Checkpoint
What does the author use as primary evidence for the reality of the Prophet's Pool?
A) A hadith from al-Tirmidhi
B) The Quranic verse 'Indeed, We have given you al-Kawthar'
C) The consensus of the Salaf
D) The opinion of al-Qurtubi

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's Pool is a real, eschatological feature confirmed by the Quran and interpreted by scholars as part of al-Kawthar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You will leave your grave thirsty and desperate. Are you building a relationship with the Prophet (ﷺ) today so that he will recognize you and invite you to his Pool? What specific act of love for him can you do before this day ends?
?
The Prophet's Pool is a gift from Allah, but it is only for those who follow him sincerely. Which of your habits or beliefs would you need to change if you truly believed you will stand before that Pool tomorrow?
?
Knowing that the Pool is real and located before the terrifying Bridge, does that change how you view your deeds today? Will you face the Bridge having drunk from the Pool or still burning with thirst? Make a commitment right now to one action that prepares you for that moment.

The Prophet's Pool: Hadith Proofs and Those Excluded
Hadith evidence for the Pool and exclusion of opposing groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophetic hadiths affirm the Pool and that certain groups are excluded from it.

Core Idea
The Pool is attested by nearly mass-transmitted hadiths, and those who oppose the community are driven away.

This lesson examines the hadith evidence for the Prophet's Pool, including the statement that every prophet has a pool. It also addresses the sobering truth that those who oppose mainstream Islam—such as the Kharijites, Rafidites, Mu'tazilites, and oppressors—will be driven away from the Pool. The authenticity of these hadiths is emphasized by their being narrated by many Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage from 'وروى الترمذي' to 'متواترا'. It contains two main parts: a hadith about every prophet's pool and a report about exclusion.
2
Analyze the first hadith
The Prophet says every prophet has a pool and they boast about visitors. He hopes to have the most. Reflect on the implications.
This shows the honor of the Prophet and his community.
3
Understand the exclusion
Al-Qurtubi reports that those who oppose the community (Kharijites, etc.) and oppressors are driven away. Note the reason: 'because of their involvement in innovation'.
4
Note the transmission strength
The hadith is narrated by over thirty Companions and is nearly mutawatir. This strengthens its authority.

The Pool (Hawd) of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, is true, because of the saying of the Exalted: 'Indeed, We have given you al-Kawthar' [Kawthar: 1]. The majority interpreted it as his Pool or his River, and there is no contradiction between them, because his River is in Paradise and his Pool is at the standing-place of the Resurrection, with a difference of opinion as to whether it is before the Bridge (Sirat) or after it, and the former is the more likely and more appropriate. Al-Qurtubi said: There are two pools: one before the Bridge and before the Balance (Mizan) according to the soundest view, for people will come out thirsty from their graves and will go to it before the Balance and the Bridge. The second is in Paradise, and both are called Kawthar. End. Al-Tirmidhi narrated and authenticated that he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Every prophet has a pool, and they boast about which of them has more visitors, and I hope to have the most visitors.' This, and al-Qurtubi reported that those who oppose the community of Muslims, such as the Kharijites, the Rafidites, the Mu'tazilites, and likewise the oppressors and the cursed sinners, are driven away from the Pool because of their involvement (in innovation). The hadith about the Pool was narrated by thirty-odd Companions and is nearly mass-transmitted. A hadith has come: 'My Pool is in Paradise, a distance of one month, and its corners are equal; its water is whiter than milk, its scent more fragrant than musk, its taste more delicious and sweeter than honey, colder than snow, softer than butter; its rim is of chrysolite, its vessels of silver, its pitchers like the stars of the sky; whoever drinks a drink from it will never thirst after it forever.' According to most of the Salaf, it is abundant good. In the authentic hadiths: 'It is a river in Paradise upon which there is abundant good; my community will come to it on the Day of Resurrection.' And it was said: It is prophethood and the Qur'an.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage affirms and describes the reality of the Prophet Muhammad's Pool (al-Hawd), an eschatological feature. The author begins by stating that the Pool is true (ḥaqq), citing the Quranic verse 'Indeed, We have given you al-Kawthar' (108:1). He notes that the majority of scholars interpret 'al-Kawthar' as either the Pool or the River in Paradise, and that there is no contradiction: the River is in Paradise, while the Pool is at the standing-place of the Day of Resurrection. There is a scholarly difference over whether the Pool is before or after the Sirat (Bridge); the author favors it being before the Sirat. He then quotes al-Qurtubi, who mentions two pools: one before the Sirat and the Balance (al-Mizan), where people come out thirsty from their graves and drink, and another in Paradise; both are called Kawthar. The author then cites a hadith from al-Tirmidhi: every prophet has a pool, and they boast about the number of visitors; the Prophet hopes to have the most visitors. Next, he reports al-Qurtubi's view that those who oppose the Muslim community—like the Kharijites, Rafidites, Mu'tazilites, oppressors, and cursed sinners—are driven away from the Pool. The hadith about the Pool is narrated by over thirty Companions and is nearly mass-transmitted (mutawatir). The author then provides a detailed description of the Pool from another hadith: its size, water, scent, taste, temperature, rim, vessels, and that drinking from it quenches thirst forever. He mentions that most Salaf interpret 'Kawthar' as abundant good, and authentic hadiths say it is a river in Paradise. Finally, he notes an alternative interpretation: it signifies prophethood and the Qur'an. The passage thus establishes the Pool as a real, blessed feature of the afterlife, supported by revelation and tradition.

Description of the Prophet's Pool and Its Meanings
Physical description of the Pool and interpretation of Kawthar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed description of the Prophet's Pool and its various symbolic interpretations.

Core Idea
The Pool is described in vivid physical terms, symbolizing abundant good and spiritual sustenance.

This lesson presents a rich hadith describing the Prophet's Pool in sensory terms: its size, water quality, scent, taste, and vessels. It also explores how scholars have interpreted the meaning of 'Kawthar' as abundant good, a river in Paradise, or even prophethood and the Quran. The description reinforces the Pool's tangible reality and its spiritual blessings.

Paradise and Hell Are Created and Eternal
The author proves that Paradise and Hell are created now and will never perish, using Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that Paradise and Hell are already created and will never perish, supported by Quranic verses and hadith.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now and will never end.

This lesson presents the Sunni belief that Paradise and Hell are already created and eternal. The author provides evidence from the Quran and hadith, particularly the use of the past tense 'prepared' to indicate present existence. He also notes the Mu'tazila opposition. Let's examine the proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and then the English translation. Notice how the author states his claims and then provides evidence.
The passage is concise but packed with proof.
2
Identify the three proofs
Find the three pieces of evidence: the Quranic verses, the sacred hadith, and the hadith of the Night Journey. Note that all use the past tense.
3
Understand the linguistic argument
The author argues that the past tense is literal (haqiqa) and should not be shifted to metaphor without strong evidence. This is a key point in Sunni methodology.
This argument counters metaphorical interpretations.
4
Note the sectarian difference
The Mu'tazila opposed this view. Reflect on why this matters for theological consistency.
Knowing the opposing view helps solidify the Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجنة والنار لا تفنيان. والجنة والنار مخلوقتان اليوم أي موجودتان الآن قبل يوم القيامة، لقوله تعالى في نعت الجنة: ﴿أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ﴾ [آل عمران: 133]، وفي وصف النار: ﴿أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَافِرِينَ﴾ [البقرة: 24]، وللحديث القدسي: ((أعددت لعبادي الصالحين ما لا عين رأت ولا أذن سمعت ولا خطر على قلب بشر)). ولحديث الإسراء: ((أدخلت الجنة)) و ((أُريتُ النار)). وهذه الصيغة موضوعة للمضي حقيقة فلا وجه للعدول عنها إلى المجاز إلا بصريح آية أو صحيح دلالة، وفي المسألة خلاف للمعتزلة.
And Paradise and Hell do not perish. And Paradise and Hell are created today, i.e., they exist now before the Day of Resurrection, because of the saying of the Exalted in describing Paradise: 'Prepared for the righteous' [Al 'Imran: 133], and in describing Hell: 'Prepared for the disbelievers' [Baqarah: 24], and due to the sacred hadith: 'I have prepared for My righteous servants what no eye has seen, no ear has heard, and has not occurred to the heart of man.' And due to the hadith of the Night Journey: 'I was admitted into Paradise' and 'I was shown the Fire.' And this verbal form is used for the past as a reality, so there is no justification for departing from it to metaphor except with a clear verse or sound indication. And on this issue there is opposition from the Mu'tazila.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage affirms two intertwined doctrines: that Paradise and Hell are already created and that they will never perish. The author begins with the statement 'Paradise and Hell do not perish' (lā tafnayān), then immediately adds that they are 'created today' (makhluqatān al-yawm), explaining 'today' as meaning 'now, before the Day of Resurrection.' He provides three proofs. First, Quranic verses: Paradise is described as 'prepared for the righteous' (Al 'Imran 3:133) and Hell as 'prepared for the disbelievers' (Baqarah 2:24)—the past tense 'prepared' (u'iddat) indicates present existence. Second, a sacred hadith (hadith qudsi) in which Allah says He has prepared for His righteous servants what no eye has seen, etc., again using the past tense. Third, hadiths from the Night Journey (al-Isra') where the Prophet says 'I was admitted into Paradise' and 'I was shown the Fire,' implying they already existed at that time. The author then makes a linguistic argument: these verbs are in the past tense (al-māḍī) as a reality (ḥaqīqa), so one should not depart from their literal meaning to metaphor (majāz) without a clear textual or logical indication. Finally, he notes that the Mu'tazila differ on this issue—they denied that Paradise and Hell are created now or that they are eternal, claiming they will be created only after the Resurrection. The passage thus firmly establishes the Sunni position against the Mu'tazila.

النار
لا تفنيان
مخلوقتان
المعتزلة
حديث القدسي
الإسراء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'created today' means Paradise and Hell are temporally created at the moment of speech, rather than existing now before the Day of Resurrection.
Correction: The phrase 'created today' (makhluqatan al-yawm) is explained as 'existing now before the Day of Resurrection,' meaning they already exist, not that they are created at the moment of utterance.

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell already exist and will never perish, as proven by the past tense in Quran and hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Paradise and Hell Are Created and Exist Now
The author proves Paradise and Hell are created and refutes metaphorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why classical Sunni doctrine holds that Paradise and Hell are already created and exist now, based on clear textual evidence from the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell already exist—prepared and witnessed by the Prophet.

This lesson examines a foundational belief about the afterlife: that Paradise and Hell are not merely future creations but already exist. The author presents scriptural evidence from the Quran and authentic hadith, arguing that the literal meaning of the past-tense verbs used must be accepted unless there is strong reason to interpret metaphorically.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the author's overall argument.
Pay attention to the key terms: الجنة, النار, مخلوقة, أعدت.
2
Identify the three pieces of evidence
The author gives three proofs: two Quranic verses using 'prepared' (أُعِدَّتْ), one sacred hadith about preparation, and the hadith of the Night Journey where the Prophet entered Paradise and saw Hell.
Notice that all evidence uses past tense verbs.
3
Understand the linguistic argument
The author argues that these past tense forms are literal, so there is no reason to interpret them metaphorically unless there is clear counter-evidence. This refutes the Mu'tazila position.

(والجنة والنار مخلوقتان (اليوم أي موجودتان الآن قبل يوم القيامة، لقوله تعالى في نعت الجنة: أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ [آل عمران:133]، وفي وصف النار: أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَافِرِينَ [البقرة:24]، وللحديث القدسي: أعددت لعبادي الصالحين ما لا عين رأت ولا أذن سمعت ولا خطر على قلب بشر). ولحديث الإسراء: ((أدخلت الجنة)) و (أُريتُ النار). وهذه الصيغة موضوعة للمضي حقيقة فلا وجه للعدول عنها إلى المجاز إلا بصريح آية أو صحيح دلالة، وفي المسألة خلاف للمعتزلة.

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the doctrine that Paradise and Hell are already created and exist now, before the Day of Resurrection. The author then argues that these past tense forms are used in their literal sense, so they cannot be interpreted metaphorically unless there is clear evidence to the contrary. He concludes by noting that the Mu'tazila disagree on this matter, implying that they deny that Paradise and Hell are created now, interpreting the verses metaphorically. Where is Paradise? The Preferred Opinion
The author states the most correct opinion on Paradise's location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the most correct opinion regarding the location of Paradise and the evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
Paradise is in heaven, evidence from Quran and hadith.

The location of Paradise is a matter of theological reflection. While some say it is on earth or unknown, the author presents the strongest view with scriptural support. Let's examine the evidence and the preferred opinion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage about Paradise, then its translation. Notice the structure: preferred opinion, evidence, other opinions.
2
Identify the evidence
Find the Quranic verse and the hadith. How do they support Paradise being in heaven?
The verse places the Garden near the Lote Tree in heaven.
3
Understand the other opinions
Note the two alternative views: Paradise on earth or that we should refrain from speculating. Why might some choose refraining?
The commentator of al-Maqasid chose refraining.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this matters for Muslim belief. Does it affect our understanding of the afterlife?
It affirms that Paradise is a real, created place in the heavens.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الأصح أن الجنة في السماء، ويدل عليه قوله تعالى: عِندَ سِدْرَةِ الْمُنتَهَى عِنْدَهَا جَنَّةُ الْمَأْوَى [النجم:14-15]، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: ((سقف الجنة عرش الرحمن)). وقيل: في الأرض، وقيل: بالوقف حيث لا يعلمه إلا الله تعالى، واختاره شارح المقاصد. وأما النار، فقيل: تحت الأرضين السبع وقيل فوقها وقيل بالتوقف أيضا في حقها.
Then the most correct is that Paradise is in heaven, and it is indicated by His statement, the Most High: 'At the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, near which is the Garden of Refuge' [An-Najm 53:14-15], and his statement, peace be upon him: 'The ceiling of Paradise is the Throne of the Merciful.' And it is said: on earth, and it is said: to refrain, for none knows it except Allah the Most High, and the commentator of al-Maqasid chose this. As for Hell, it is said: under the seven earths, and it is said: above them, and it is said: to refrain concerning it as well.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a classification of scholarly opinions regarding the physical location of Paradise and Hell. The author begins by stating the most correct opinion (الأصح) that Paradise is in heaven. He provides two pieces of evidence: first, the Quranic verse that places the Garden of Refuge near the Lote Tree of the Utmost Boundary, which is in the heavens; second, the prophetic hadith that the ceiling of Paradise is the Throne of the Merciful, implying it is under the Throne. He then mentions two other opinions: that Paradise is on earth, or that one should refrain from speculating (الوقف) as only Allah knows. He notes that the commentator of al-Maqasid chose the view of refraining. Then he turns to Hell, stating opinions: under the seven earths, above them, or likewise refraining. Thus, the passage refrains from definitively settling the location of Hell but gives the preferred view for Paradise. The reader should note that the author uses a hierarchy of opinions, indicating the strength of evidence.

The Reality and Description of the Bridge (As-Sirat)
Affirmation and description of the Sirat from Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Sirat is a real bridge over Hell that all people must cross, and its description from authentic hadith.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real bridge over Hell; all must cross it, and its experience varies by deeds.

This lesson affirms the reality of the Sirat (the Bridge) as a matter of Islamic creed. Drawing from Quran and Sunnah, it describes a physical bridge stretched over Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair. The passage explains that crossing depends on one's deeds, and even the Prophets will supplicate for safety.

Guided Path
1
Note the doctrinal affirmation
Recognize that the author asserts the Bridge is true (haqq) and that this is placed before discussing Paradise and Hell.
The commentator adds 'And the Bridge is true' even though it's not in the main texts.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read the verse from Surah Maryam 19:71 and Al-Nawawi's interpretation that 'coming to it' means passing over the Bridge.
This interpretation is from Ibn Abbas and the majority of exegetes.
3
Analyze the hadith descriptions
Look at the multiple hadith narrations that describe the Bridge: its sharpness, thinness, and the varying experiences of people crossing it.
The Bridge is sharper than a sword and finer than a hair, but for some it is like a wide valley.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووقع في أصل شارح هنا زيادة والصراط حق وليس في المتون وكأنه ملحق، ولكن محله قبل ذكر الجنة والنار أليق، وهو ثابت بالكتاب والسنة، فقال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ مِنْكُمْ إِلَّا وَارِدُهَا﴾ [مريم:71]، قال النووي في شرح مسلم: الصحيح أن المراد في الآية المرور على الصراط، انتهى. وهو المروي عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه وجمهور المفسرين، وقد روي مرفوعاً أيضاً. وورد في صحيح مسلم: ((إن الصراط جسر ممدود على ظهر جهنم، أدق من الشعر وأحدّ من السيف)) وورد أيضاً: أنه يكون على بعض أهل النار أدق من الشعر وعلى بعض مثل الوادي الواسع. وفي رواية: ((ويضرب الصراط بين ظهراني جهنّم، وأكون أول من يجوز من الرسل بأمته، ولا يتكلم يومئذ إلا الرسل، وكلام الرسل يومئذ: اللهم سلّم سلّم، وفي جهنم كلاليب مثل شوك السَّعدان لا يعلم قدر عظمها إلا الله، تخطف الناس بأعمالهم، فمنهم من يوبق بعمله، ومنهم من يخردل ثم ينجو)). وفي رواية: ((فيمرّ المؤمنون كطرفة العين
And there occurred in the original of the commentator here an addition: 'And the Bridge is true'—and it is not in the texts, and it seems appended, but its place before the mention of Paradise and Hell is more appropriate. And it is established by the Book and the Sunnah, for Allah the Most High said: 'And there is none of you but will come to it' [Maryam 19:71]. Al-Nawawi said in his commentary on Sahih Muslim: 'The correct view is that what is intended in the verse is the passage over the Bridge.' End. And it is reported from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, and the majority of exegetes, and it has also been reported as marfu. And it is reported in Sahih Muslim: 'The Bridge is a bridge stretched over the back of Hell, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword.' And it is also reported that it will be on some of the people of Hell finer than a hair, and on some like a wide valley. And in one narration: 'And the Bridge will be set across the middle of Hell, and I will be the first of the messengers to cross with his nation, and no one will speak that day except the messengers, and the speech of the messengers that day is: O Allah, grant safety, grant safety. And in Hell are hooks like the thorns of the sa'dan, the enormity of which none knows except Allah, snatching people by their deeds. Some are destroyed by their deeds, and some are cut to pieces then saved.' And in one narration: 'The believers will pass like the blink of an eye...'
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation and description of the Sirat (the Bridge). The author begins by noting an addition in the commentator's original: 'And the Bridge is true' (الصراط حق). He clarifies that this is not in the main texts but seems appended, though its place is before discussing Paradise and Hell. The Bridge is established by Quran and Sunnah. He cites the Quranic verse 'And there is none of you but will come to it' (Maryam 19:71) and explains that Al-Nawawi interprets 'coming to it' as passing over the Bridge. This is the view of Ibn Abbas and the majority of exegetes, and is also reported as a marfu hadith. Then he quotes from Sahih Muslim describing the Bridge: a bridge stretched over Hell, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. A variant mentions that for some it is finer, for others like a wide valley, indicating that the difficulty of crossing depends on one's deeds. Another hadith describes the Bridge being set across Hell, with the Prophet as the first to cross, the supplication 'O Allah, grant safety,' and hooks that snatch people based on their deeds; some are destroyed, others are cut to pieces and then saved. Finally, he mentions a narration that believers pass like the blink of an eye. The passage thus affirms the reality of the Sirat as a physical bridge over Hell, with different experiences for different people, and that all must cross it. This is a matter of the unseen (samiyyat) accepted by Ahl al-Sunnah.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The hooks snatch people by their deeds. What 'hooks'—habits or attachments—are currently snatching you away from the straight path in your daily life? Identify one hook and make a concrete plan to remove it.

Paradise and Hell: Created and Eternal
Imam Abu Hanifa affirms creation and eternity of Paradise and Hell with proofs, then refutes Jahmiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that Paradise and Hell are created, eternal realities with eternal inhabitants, and how this refutes the Jahmiyya doctrine of annihilation.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are created realities that never end, for their inhabitants never leave.

This lesson presents the foundational Sunni belief about the afterlife destinations. Imam Abu Hanifa affirms that Paradise and Hell are real, created by Allah, and will last forever, along with their inhabitants. This is supported by clear Qur'anic verses and stands in opposition to the Jahmiyya heresy, which claimed both would perish.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from al-Wasiyya
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Notice the two main affirmations: Paradise and Hell are created, and they (and their inhabitants) are eternal.
2
Identify the Qur'anic proofs
Find the Qur'anic verses cited: for Paradise (Al Imran 133) and Hell (al-Baqarah 24) for their creation; for eternity of inhabitants (al-Baqarah 82 for believers, 39 for disbelievers).
These verses use the word 'khālidūn' meaning eternal abiding.
3
Understand the refutation of Jahmiyya
The passage explicitly rejects the Jahmiyya view that Paradise and Hell will perish. Note that it calls this view baseless and contradictory to scripture, Sunnah, and consensus.
The Jahmiyya are identified here as 'pure Jabriyya'.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this doctrine matters: it affirms the seriousness of reward and punishment, and the eternal nature of Allah's justice. Ask yourself: what would be lost if Paradise and Hell were temporary?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله في كتابه "الوصية": والجنة والنار حق، وهما مخلوقتان، ولا فناء لهما ولا لأهلهما؛ لقوله تعالى في حق أهل الجنة : ﴿ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٣٣]، وفي حق أهل النار : ﴿ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَافِرِينَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤]، خلقهما الله تعالى للثواب والعقاب. وقال أيضا في "الوصية": وأهل الجنة في الجنة خالدون، وأهل النار في النار خالدون لقوله تعالى في حق المؤمنين : ﴿ أُولَئِكَ أَصْحَابُ الْجَنَّةِ هُمْ فِيهَا خَالِدُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٨٢]، وفي حق الكفار : ﴿ أُولَئِكَ أَصْحَابُ النَّارِ هُمْ فِيهَا خَالِدُونَ ﴾ [البقرة: ٣٩]، انتهى. وذهب الجهمية وهم الجبرية الخالصة إلى أنهما تفنيان ويفنى أهلهما، وهو قول باطل بلا شبهة؛ لأنه مخالف للكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة.
And Imam al-A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) said in his book al-Wasiyya: Paradise and Hell are true, and they are created, and there is no annihilation for them nor for their inhabitants, due to the saying of the Most High concerning the people of Paradise: 'Prepared for the righteous' [Al Imran 133], and concerning the people of Hell: 'Prepared for the disbelievers' [al-Baqarah 24]. Allah Most High created them for reward and punishment. And he also said in al-Wasiyya: And the people of Paradise are eternally abiding in Paradise, and the people of Hell are eternally abiding in Hell, due to the saying of the Most High concerning the believers: 'Those are the companions of Paradise; they will abide therein eternally' [al-Baqarah 82], and concerning the disbelievers: 'Those are the companions of the Fire; they will abide therein eternally' [al-Baqarah 39]. End. And the Jahmiyya – and they are the pure Jabriyya – held that they both will perish and their inhabitants will perish, and this is a false statement without any doubt, because it contradicts the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the community.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents the Sunni doctrine of the eternity of Paradise and Hell. It quotes Imam al-A'zam from his work al-Wasiyya, affirming that Paradise and Hell are true (haqq) and created (makhluqatan), and they will never perish, nor will their inhabitants. Proof is given from Qur'anic verses: for Paradise, 'Prepared for the righteous' (Al Imran 133); for Hell, 'Prepared for the disbelievers' (al-Baqarah 24). The Imam then states that the inhabitants of Paradise are eternally abiding (khalidun) and likewise the inhabitants of Hell, citing verses from Surah al-Baqarah (82 for believers, 39 for disbelievers). The passage then condemns the Jahmiyya (identified as pure Jabriyya) who claim that both will perish and their inhabitants will perish, calling this view baseless and contradictory to scripture, prophetic tradition, and consensus of the Muslim community.

The Grave Questioning by Munkar and Nakir
Affirmation of grave questioning with evidence and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the questioning of the grave by Munkar and Nakir is a true doctrine supported by the Prophet's hadith and the Qur'an, and that prophets, children, and martyrs are excepted from this questioning.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is true but not universal—prophets, children, and martyrs are exempt.

This passage from Imam Abu Hanifa's Fiqh al-Akbar affirms the reality of the questioning in the grave by the angels Munkar and Nakir. It cites the Prophet's (ﷺ) observation of two graves being punished and a Qur'anic verse interpreted as referring to the grave. The text then notes exceptions to this general rule for prophets, children, and martyrs, based on a hadith in Sahih Muslim.

Guided Path

Read the passage carefully

The verse is understood to apply to the grave based on authentic hadith.

This exception is based on a hadith in Sahih Muslim.

The passage then lists exceptions to this general rule: prophets, children, and martyrs are not subject to the grave questioning. It references a hadith in Sahih Muslim where the Prophet (ﷺ) was asked about this, but the text cuts off at 'kafa' (sufficient).
