The Return of the Soul to the Grave
Affirms the return of the soul and discusses questioning of prophets and children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrine of the return of the soul to the grave and the initial opinions regarding the questioning of prophets and children.

Core Idea
The soul returns to the body in the grave before questioning.

The passage begins by affirming a core Sunni belief: the soul is returned to the servant in his grave. This sets the stage for discussing the questioning that follows. The author also presents various scholarly views on whether prophets and children are questioned, highlighting the depth of theological reflection on this matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on return of soul
Focus on the opening statement affirming that the return of the soul is true. Notice the hadith fragment 'with the flashing of swords as a witness' which hints at martyrs.
The term 'ببارقة السيوف' refers to martyrs.
2
Examine the scholarly opinions on questioning
Identify the different views: no questioning for prophets, questioning for children, and Imam Abu Hanifa's suspension of judgment on children of disbelievers.
This shows diversity of opinion within Sunni Islam.
3
Reflect on the core doctrine
Understand that the return of the soul is a matter of faith ('haqq'). The passage emphasizes that this happens before questioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإعادة الروح إلى العبد في قبره حق ببارقة السيوف شاهدا)) ففي الكفاية أنه لا سؤال للأنبياء عليهم السلام. وقال السيد أبو شجاع علماء الحنفية: إن للصبيان سؤالاً، وكذا للأنبياء عند البعض، وقال بعضهم: صبيان المسلمين مغفور لهم قطعاً، والسؤال لحكمة لم يطلع عليها. وتوقف الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله في سؤال أطفال الكفرة ودخولهم الجنة، وغيره حكم بذلك فيكونون خدم أهل الجنة. (وإعادة الروح) أي ردّها أو تعلّقها إلى العبد أي جسده بجميع أجزائه أو ببعضها مجتمعة أو متفرقة في قبره حق والواو لمجرد الجمعية فلا ينافي أن السؤال بعد إعادة الروح وكمال الحال، فيقول المؤمن: ربي الله وديني الإسلام ونبيي محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم، ويقول الكافر: هاه هاه لا أدري)) رواه أبو داود، وأصله في الصحيحين. وفي المسألة خلاف المعتزلة وبعض الرافضة. وقد وردت الأحاديث المتظاهرةُ في المبنى المتواترة في المعنى في تحقيق أحوال البرزخ والعقبى، قد استوفاها شيخ مشايخنا الجلال السيوطي في كتابه المسمى بـ"شرح الصدور في أحوال القبور" وفي كتابه الآخر المسمى بـ"البدور السافرة في أحوال الآخرة"، فعليك بهما إن كنت تريد الاطلاع وارتفاع النزاع عن الطباع.
And the return of the soul to the servant in his grave is true. 'With the flashing of swords as a witness.' In al-Kifaya, there is no questioning for the prophets, peace be upon them. And al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' said: The Hanafi scholars hold that children are questioned, and likewise the prophets according to some. And some said: The children of Muslims are certainly forgiven, and the questioning is for a wisdom not disclosed. And Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa), may Allah have mercy on him, halted in the matter of the questioning of the children of disbelievers and their entry into Paradise, while others judged that, so they become servants of the people of Paradise. (And the return of the soul) meaning its return or its attachment to the servant, i.e., his body, either all its parts or some of them, gathered or scattered, in his grave, is true. And the waw is merely for conjunction, so it does not negate that the questioning is after the return of the soul and the completion of the state. So the believer says: 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and my Prophet is Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.' And the disbeliever says: 'Hah, hah, I do not know.' Narrated by Abu Dawud, and its origin is in the two Sahihs. On this issue, there is disagreement with the Mu'tazila and some of the Rafidah. Indeed, numerous hadiths, manifest in chain and recurrent in meaning, have come concerning the realities of the Barzakh and the Hereafter. Our shaykh's shaykh, al-Jalal al-Suyuti, has gathered them in his book entitled 'Sharh al-Sudur fi Ahwal al-Qubur' and in his other book entitled 'al-Budur al-Safira fi Ahwal al-Akhira'. So you must refer to them if you desire investigation and the removal of discord from natures.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the return of the soul and the questioning in the grave. It begins by stating as a matter of doctrine that the return of the soul to the servant in his grave is true. It then cites a hadith fragment implying that martyrs are not questioned, and notes that according to al-Kifaya, prophets are not questioned either. The passage then presents various scholarly opinions: Abu Shuja' reports that Hanafis hold that children are questioned, and some extend this to prophets. Some hold that Muslim children are forgiven regardless. Imam Abu Hanifa (al-A'zam) suspended judgment on the fate of children of disbelievers, while others rule that they become servants of Paradise. The passage then provides a detailed explanation of the return of the soul: it means the soul is returned or attached to the body (all or some parts). The conjunction waw simply connects statements, so it does not contradict that the questioning occurs after the return of the soul and the completion of the state. It then quotes the answers of the believer and disbeliever during the questioning, based on a hadith in Abu Dawud and the two Sahihs. The passage notes that the Mu'tazila and some Rafidah oppose this doctrine. Finally, it recommends consulting the collections of al-Suyuti for a thorough treatment of the intermedate state (barzakh) and the afterlife.

Key Terms
إعادة الروح
سؤال القبر
البرزخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the soul does not return to the body until the Day of Resurrection.
Correction: The passage affirms that the soul returns to the grave immediately, before the questioning.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is Imam Abu Hanifa's position on the questioning of children of disbelievers?
A) They are definitely questioned.
B) They are not questioned.
C) He suspended judgment.
D) They become servants of Paradise.

Key Takeaway
The return of the soul to the grave is a fundamental belief, while the questioning of prophets and children involves varied scholarly opinions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that your soul will return to your grave immediately after death and be questioned, would you change anything about how you live today? What specifically would you do differently tonight before you sleep?
?
The passage mentions that some scholars say children of disbelievers become servants of Paradise. Does this align with your conception of Allah’s justice? How does it affect your view of those who have not yet accepted Islam?
?
Imam Abu Hanifa suspended judgment on the fate of children of disbelievers. Are there matters in your faith that you are willing to leave unresolved, trusting that Allah’s wisdom is beyond your understanding?

The Questioning in the Grave and the Answer of the Believer
Describes the questioning process and the answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed process of the questioning in the grave, the response of the believer and disbeliever, and the opposition of the Mu'tazila and Rafidah.

Core Idea
The believer answers correctly, while the disbeliever fails the test.

This passage delves into the specifics of the grave questioning. It explains that the soul is returned to the body after death, and then the angels ask about one's Lord, religion, and prophet. The believer responds with faith, while the disbeliever is confused. The author cites hadith evidence and notes that the Mu'tazila and some Rafidah reject this doctrine, recommending further study in al-Suyuti's works.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage on the questioning
Notice the explanation of the return of the soul (إعادة الروح) and the conjunction waw. Then read the answers of the believer and disbeliever.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and the two Sahihs.
2
Identify the opposition
The passage mentions that the Mu'tazila and some Rafidah disagree with this doctrine. Consider why they might reject it.
This highlights the importance of this belief in Sunni orthodoxy.
3
Recognize the scholarly sources
The author recommends al-Suyuti's books for further study. This shows the depth of the tradition.

The Squeeze of the Grave: Its Reality and Nature
Affirms the squeeze of the grave and its reality for all, with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the squeeze of the grave (ḍaghṭat al-qabr) is a true reality that even the perfect believer experiences, followed by divine expansion, and is not a punishment for believers.

Core Idea
The grave squeezes even the best believers, but for them it is like a mother's embrace.

This lesson examines the doctrine of the grave's squeeze (ḍaghṭa). While many assume it is only for sinners, the classical Sunni position affirms it for all, including the most righteous. We will read the evidence from the Quran and hadith, and explore how the squeeze transforms into expansion for the believer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage affirming the squeeze
The passage begins by stating that both the punishment and squeeze of the grave are true. Notice the clarification that the greater punishment is of the Hereafter.
This sets the context for the squeeze.
2
Understand the evidence and the squeeze for believers
The Quranic verse from Taha is presented as evidence. Then the squeeze is defined and emphasized as true even for the perfect believer, using the hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh.
3
Reflect on the process and simile
The passage explains that the grave constricts first, then Allah expands it. The simile of a mother's embrace shows that for believers, the squeeze is not painful but a form of closeness.
Compare with punishment discussed in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عذاب القبر وضغطة القبر حق، وعذابه حق كائن للكُفَّار كلّهم ولبعض المسلمين، دون العذاب الأكبر أي عذاب الآخرة، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ أَعْرَضَ عَنْ ذِكْرِى أي عن اتباع القرآن فلم يؤمن به، فَإِنَّ لَهُ مَعِيشَةً ضَنكًا، أي ضيقة في الدنيا أو في الآخرة، وَنَحْشُرُهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ أَعْمَى﴾ [طه:١٢٤]، وكأنها أيضاً مأخذ قول الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله. وضغطة القبر أي تضييقه حق حتى للمؤمن الكامل للحديث: ((لو كان أحد نجا منها لنجا سعد بن معاذ) الذي اهتز عرش الرحمن لموته. وهي أخذ أرض القبر وضيقه أولاً عليه ثم الله سبحانه يفسح ويوسع المكان مد نظره إليه. قيل : وضغطته بالنسبة إلى المؤمن على هيئة معانقة الأم الشفيقة إذا قدم عليها ولدها من السفرة العميقة. وعذابه أي إيلامه حق كائن للكفار كلهم أجمعين ولبعض المسلمين أي عصاة المسلمين كما في نسخة، وكذا تنعيم بعض المؤمنين حق، فقد ورد: ((إن القبر روضة من رياض الجنة أو حفرة من حفر النيران)). رواه الترمذي والطبراني رحمهما الله . وفي الحديث : ((إن القبر أول منازل الآخرة فإن نجا منه فما بعده أيسر منه وإن لم ينج منه فما بعده أشد منه)). رواه الترمذي والنسائي والحاكم بسند صحيح عن عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه.
The punishment of the grave and the squeeze of the grave are true. And its punishment is true and occurs for all disbelievers and for some Muslims, except the greater punishment, i.e., the punishment of the Hereafter. And likewise His statement, Exalted is He: 'And whoever turns away from My remembrance, i.e., from following the Quran and does not believe in it, then indeed for him is a straitened livelihood, i.e., narrow in this world or in the Hereafter, and We will gather him on the Day of Resurrection blind.' [Taha:124] And it is also a basis for the statement of Imam al-A'zam, may Allah have mercy on him. And the squeeze of the grave, i.e., its narrowing, is true, even for the perfect believer, due to the hadith: 'If anyone were saved from it, it would be Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, for whom the Throne of the Most Merciful shook at his death.' And it is that the earth of the grave constricts and narrows upon him first, then Allah, glorified is He, expands and widens the place as far as his sight extends. It is said: Its squeeze for the believer is like the embrace of a compassionate mother when her child returns to her from a long journey. And its punishment, i.e., its infliction of pain, is true and occurs for all disbelievers, all of them, and for some Muslims, i.e., sinful Muslims, as in a copy. Likewise, the bliss of some believers is true. Indeed, it has been reported: 'Verily, the grave is either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi and al-Tabarani, may Allah have mercy on them. In the hadith: 'Verily, the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter. If one is saved from it, what comes after is easier than it; and if one is not saved from it, what comes after is more severe than it.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and al-Hakim with a sound chain from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation and explanation of two related realities: the punishment of the grave and its squeeze. It begins by stating that both are true (ḥaqq). The punishment applies to all disbelievers and some Muslims, with the note that the 'greater punishment' belongs to the Hereafter. It then cites Qur'an 20:124 as evidence, interpreting 'straitened livelihood' as referring to the grave or the afterlife, and considers this a basis for Imam Abu Hanifa's position. The passage then defines the squeeze of the grave (ḍaghṭa) as its narrowing, emphasizing that it is true even for a perfect believer, as illustrated by the hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh. It explains the process: first, the grave constricts, then Allah expands it for the believer. A simile compares the squeeze for a believer to a mother's embrace. It then reiterates that punishment is for all disbelievers and sinful Muslims, while some believers experience bliss in the grave, citing a hadith that the grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hell. The passage concludes by quoting a hadith that the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter: salvation from it makes the rest easier, while failure to be saved makes what follows more severe.

Key Terms
ضغطة القبر
سعد بن معاذ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The squeeze of the grave only happens to sinful or disbelieving people.
Correction: The squeeze occurs for every person, including the perfect believer, but for believers it is followed by expansion and is analogous to a mother's embrace.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the believer after the initial squeeze of the grave?
A) It remains constricted forever.
B) It is expanded by Allah.
C) It turns into punishment.
D) Nothing happens.

Key Takeaway
The squeeze of the grave is a universal experience, but for believers it becomes a moment of divine closeness and expansion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever considered that the grave’s squeeze is a reality even for the best of believers? What does that tell you about your own need for Allah’s mercy? How will you prepare for that moment tonight?
?
The squeeze for a believer is like a mother's embrace. Does your current relationship with Allah make you long for that embrace, or do you fear the grave? What one change can you make today to turn fear into hope?
?
If the grave squeezes even Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, what makes you think you will escape its tightening? How does this realization change your attitude towards sin and repentance right now?

The Punishment and Bliss of the Grave for Disbelievers and Believers
Specifies the recipients of grave punishment and bliss, and affirms the grave as the first stage of the Hereafter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that punishment in the grave is reserved for disbelievers and sinful Muslims, while some believers experience bliss, and that the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter.

Core Idea
The grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire.

In this lesson, we explore who experiences punishment in the grave and who experiences bliss. The passage makes clear that punishment is for all disbelievers and some sinful Muslims, while some believers enjoy bliss. Two key hadiths reinforce the grave's role as the first stage of the afterlife, where one's fate begins.

Guided Path
1
Identify who receives punishment
The passage states that punishment is for all disbelievers and for some Muslims. Note the phrase 'some Muslims' refers to sinful ones.
This corrects the misconception that only disbelievers are punished.
2
Note the bliss for some believers
The passage affirms that some believers experience bliss in the grave. This is based on the hadith that the grave is either a garden or a pit.
3
Understand the grave as the first stage
The hadith from 'Uthman states that the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter, and salvation there makes the rest easier.
This emphasizes the importance of one's state in the grave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The punishment of the grave and the squeeze of the grave are true. And its punishment is true and occurs for all disbelievers and for some Muslims, except the greater punishment, i.e., the punishment of the Hereafter. And likewise His statement, Exalted is He: 'And whoever turns away from My remembrance, i.e., from following the Quran and does not believe in it, then indeed for him is a straitened livelihood, i.e., narrow in this world or in the Hereafter, and We will gather him on the Day of Resurrection blind.' [Taha:124] And it is also a basis for the statement of Imam al-A'zam, may Allah have mercy on him. And the squeeze of the grave, i.e., its narrowing, is true, even for the perfect believer, due to the hadith: 'If anyone were saved from it, it would be Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, for whom the Throne of the Most Merciful shook at his death.' And it is that the earth of the grave constricts and narrows upon him first, then Allah, glorified is He, expands and widens the place as far as his sight extends. It is said: Its squeeze for the believer is like the embrace of a compassionate mother when her child returns to her from a long journey. And its punishment, i.e., its infliction of pain, is true and occurs for all disbelievers, all of them, and for some Muslims, i.e., sinful Muslims, as in a copy. Likewise, the bliss of some believers is true. Indeed, it has been reported: 'Verily, the grave is either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi and al-Tabarani, may Allah have mercy on them. In the hadith: 'Verily, the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter. If one is saved from it, what comes after is easier than it; and if one is not saved from it, what comes after is more severe than it.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and al-Hakim with a sound chain from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation and explanation of two related realities: the punishment of the grave and its squeeze. It begins by stating that both are true (ḥaqq). The punishment applies to all disbelievers and some Muslims, with the note that the 'greater punishment' belongs to the Hereafter. It then cites Qur'an 20:124 as evidence, interpreting 'straitened livelihood' as referring to the grave or the afterlife, and considers this a basis for Imam Abu Hanifa's position. The passage then defines the squeeze of the grave (ḍaghṭa) as its narrowing, emphasizing that it is true even for a perfect believer, as illustrated by the hadith of Sa'd ibn Mu'adh. It explains the process: first, the grave constricts, then Allah expands it for the believer. A simile compares the squeeze for a believer to a mother's embrace. It then reiterates that punishment is for all disbelievers and sinful Muslims, while some believers experience bliss in the grave, citing a hadith that the grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hell. The passage concludes by quoting a hadith that the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter: salvation from it makes the rest easier, while failure to be saved makes what follows more severe.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
تنعيم القبر
البرزخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only disbelievers are punished in the grave.
Correction: Punishment in the grave occurs for all disbelievers and for some sinful Muslims.

Checkpoint

A) All believers.
B) Some believers.
C) No one.
D) Only prophets.

Key Takeaway
The grave punishment is not exclusively for disbelievers; sinful Muslims may also experience it, while some believers enjoy bliss, and the grave is the decisive first stage of the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The hadith says the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter. Are you living as if your next destination is determined by what you do now? What sinful habit have you been neglecting that might bring punishment in the grave, and how will you abandon it starting this moment?
?
You know that even some Muslims experience grave punishment for their sins. Does that thought move you to sincerely repent from a specific sin you have been downplaying? What will you do right now to turn back to Allah before you face that first stage?

States agreement and disagreement on grave life and soul return.

Core Idea
The dead experience a special life for reward and punishment, but the soul's return is debated.

This passage addresses a key issue in Islamic eschatology: what happens to the deceased in the grave before the Resurrection. While all Sunni scholars agree that Allah grants a form of life sufficient for experiencing reward or punishment, they differed on whether this involves the return of the soul. Let's read the text and unpack its meaning.

The Reality of the Grave's Pressure and Punishment
Affirms the grave's pressure and punishment for disbelievers and some believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the grave's pressure and punishment are real, applying to all disbelievers and some sinful Muslims, while believers experience temporary pressure followed by comfort.

Core Idea
The grave's pressure and punishment are true, with details based on Quran and Hadith.

This passage from a classical creed work affirms the reality of the grave's pressure (ضغطة القبر) and punishment (عذاب القبر). These are among the samʿiyyāt—matters known through revelation. The author uses Quranic verses and prophetic hadith to establish that disbelievers and sinful Muslims face punishment, while even the righteous experience temporary pressure followed by expansion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
2
Identify the three key elements
Notice the three elements: the pressure of the grave (ضغطة), its punishment (عذاب), and the comfort (تنعيم) for some believers. Each is affirmed as true.
The author uses the word 'حق' (true) for each.
3
Examine the scriptural proofs
Look at the Quranic verses (Sajda 21, Ta-Ha 124) and the hadith about Sa'd ibn Mu'adh and the grave being a garden. See how they support the doctrine.
The verse about 'straitened life' is interpreted as punishment in the grave.
4
Understand the application to categories of people
Note that punishment is for all disbelievers and sinful Muslims, while pressure applies even to perfect believers. Comfort is for some believers.
This corrects the misconception that only disbelievers face grave punishment.
5
Reflect on the gravity of the grave as first stage
End with the hadith that the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter. Its outcome determines ease or difficulty in what follows.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عذاب القبر وضغطة القبر حق، وعذابه حق كائن للكُفَّار كلّهم ولبعض المسلمين، دُونَ الْعَذَابِ الْاَكْبَرِ﴾ [السجدة : ۲۱] ، أي عذاب الآخرة، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ أَعْرَضَ عَنْ ذِكْرِى أي عن اتباع القرآن فلم يؤمن به، فَإِنَّ لَنَمَعِيشَةً ضَنكًا، أي ضيقة في الدنيا أو في الآخرة، وَنَحْشُرُةَ يَوْمَ الْقِيمَةِ أَعْلى الآيات [طه:١٢٤]، وكأنها أيضاً مأخذ قول الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله. وضغطة القبر أي تضييقه (حق) حتى للمؤمن الكامل للحديث: ((لو كان أحد نجا منها لنجا سعد بن معاذ الذي اهتز عرش الرحمن لموته. وهي أخذ أرض القبر وضيقه أولاً عليه ثم الله سبحانه يفسح ويوسع المكان مد نظره إليه. قيل : وضغطته بالنسبة إلى المؤمن على هيئة معانقة الأم الشفيقة إذا قدم عليها ولدها من السفرة العميقة. وعذابه) أي إيلامه (حق كائن للكفار كلهم أجمعين ولبعض المسلمين أي عصاة المسلمين كما في نسخة، وكذا تنعيم بعض المؤمنين حق، فقد ورد: ((إن) القبر روضة رواه الترمذي والطبراني رحمهما الله . وفي الحديث : ((إن القبر أول منازل الآخرة فإن نجا منه فما بعده أيسر منه وإن لم ينج منه فما بعده أشد منه)). رواه الترمذي والنسائي والحاكم بسند صحيح عن عثمان بن عفان رضي الله عنه.
The punishment of the grave: the pressing of the grave is true, and its punishment is true, occurring for all disbelievers and some Muslims, except the greater punishment [Sajda:21] meaning the punishment of the Hereafter, and also His saying: 'And whoever turns away from My remembrance' i.e. from following the Quran and does not believe in it, 'then indeed for him is a straitened life' i.e. narrow in the world or in the Hereafter, 'and We will gather him on the Day of Resurrection blind' [Ta-Ha:124], and it is perhaps also the basis of the statement of the Great Imam, may Allah have mercy on him. And the pressing of the grave, meaning its constriction, is true even for the perfect believer, due to the hadith: 'If anyone were to be saved from it, it would be Sa'd ibn Mu'adh, for whom the Throne of the Merciful shook at his death.' And it is the taking of the earth of the grave and its constriction at first upon him, then Allah the Glorious expands and widens the place as far as his eyesight reaches. It is said: Its pressure for the believer is like the embrace of a compassionate mother when her child returns from a deep journey. And its punishment, i.e. its inflicting pain, is true and occurs for all disbelievers collectively and for some Muslims, i.e. sinful Muslims as in one copy, and likewise the comfort of some believers is true, for it has been reported: 'Indeed the grave is a garden of Paradise' reported by al-Tirmidhi and al-Tabarani, may Allah have mercy on them. And in the hadith: 'Indeed the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter; if one is saved from it, what comes after is easier than it, and if one is not saved from it, what comes after is harder than it.' Reported by al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and al-Hakim with a sound chain from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal affirmation of the reality of the grave's pressure (ضغطة القبر) and punishment (عذاب القبر). The author begins by stating unequivocally that both are true (حق). The punishment is for all disbelievers and for some Muslims (i.e., sinful Muslims), but it is not the greater punishment of the Hereafter. He supports this with Quranic verses: Surah al-Sajda 21 and Surah Ta-Ha 124, interpreting 'straitened life' as referring to punishment in the grave or in the Hereafter. He then clarifies that the pressing of the grave (ضغطة) is its constriction, and it occurs even for the perfect believer, citing the hadith about Sa'd ibn Mu'adh. However, for the believer, this pressure is temporary and then Allah expands the grave. The author also mentions a simile comparing the pressure to a mother's embrace. He reiterates that punishment is exclusive to disbelievers and sinful Muslims, while some believers experience comfort (تنعيم) in the grave, as in the hadith 'The grave is a garden of Paradise.' Finally, he cites the hadith that the grave is the first stage of the Hereafter, emphasizing its importance. The passage thus establishes the doctrine of the grave's reward and punishment as a matter of creed.

The Nature of Life in the Grave and the Return of the Soul
Explains the kind of life in the grave and the debate on the soul's return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus among Ahl al-Haqq on life in the grave and the debate regarding the return of the soul, including Abu Hanifa's position and the supporting evidence.

Core Idea
Life in the grave is real, and the soul's return is implied by voluntary acts like answering angels.

This lesson explores a key theological question: what kind of life do the deceased experience in the grave, and does the soul return to the body? The passage presents the agreed-upon view that Allah creates a life sufficient for pleasure or pain, but scholars differ on the soul's return. We will examine Abu Hanifa's stance and the reasoning from the angels' questioning and prophetic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the structure: consensus, disagreement, evidence.
2
Identify the consensus and disagreement
Find where the passage states agreement on life in the grave and the point of difference regarding the soul's return.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's position
Note that his transmitted view is suspension (tawaqquf), but his words in this context imply the soul's return because the angels' questioning is a voluntary act.
4
Consider the analogy of sleep
Reflect on how the sleeper's soul departs yet remains connected, allowing sensation. How does this support the return of the soul?
5
Study the prophetic hadith
Read the hadith about the pain of flesh in the grave without the soul, and the analogy of the toothache. How does this answer the objection?
This hadith shows that pain can occur without the soul being present, but the context is about the life created by Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن أهل الحق اتفقوا على أن الله تعالى يخلق في الميت نوع حياة في القبر قدر ما يتألم أو يتلذذ ولكن اختلفوا في أنه هل يعاد الروح إليه؟ والمنقول عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله التوقف إلا أن كلامه هنا يدل على إعادة الروح، إذ جواب الملكين فعل اختياري فلا يتصور بدون الروح. وقيل: قد يتصور ألا ترى أن النائم يخرج روحه ويكون روحه متصلا بجسده حتى يتألم في المنام ويتنعم؟ وقد روي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام: أنه سئل كيف يوجع اللحم في القبر ولم يكن فيه الروح؟ فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم: كما يوجع سنك وليس فيه الروح)) .
Know that the people of truth are agreed that Allah the Exalted creates in the deceased a type of life in the grave sufficient to experience pain or pleasure, but they differed on whether the soul is returned to him. The transmitted view from Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, is suspension (al-tawaqquf), except that his words here indicate the return of the soul, because the answering of the two angels is a voluntary act, and that cannot be imagined without the soul. And it was said: It may be imagined; do you not see that the sleeper's soul departs while his soul remains connected to his body so that he experiences pain in sleep and pleasure? And it has been narrated from him, peace and blessings be upon him, that he was asked: How is the flesh pained in the grave when there is no soul in it? He said, peace and blessings be upon him: Just as your tooth is pained while there is no soul in it.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage addresses the mechanism of life in the grave. It begins by stating the consensus of Ahl al-Haqq that Allah creates a type of life in the deceased sufficient for experiencing pain or pleasure. The point of disagreement is whether the soul (الروح) is returned to the body. The author reports that the transmitted position of Abu Hanifa is suspension (التوقف), but then notes that Abu Hanifa's own words in this context imply the return of the soul, because the angels' questioning is a voluntary action that requires a soul. The author then presents an analogy: the sleeper's soul leaves but remains connected, allowing sensation. He further supports this by citing a hadith where the Prophet was asked how the flesh feels pain without the soul; the Prophet replied with the example of a toothache, which occurs without a soul in the tooth. Thus, the passage leans towards affirming the return of the soul, using rational argument and prophetic tradition.

Correction: The passage explains that the voluntary act of answering the angels implies the soul's return, and the analogy of sleep and the prophetic hadith show that sensation can occur with a subtle connection of the soul.

Grave Punishment and Pressure: Critique and Clarification
Critiques temporary punishment lifting and describes believer's grave state.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that punishment is lifted on Fridays and Ramadan is rejected, and how the believer experiences only pressure (ضغطة) in the grave, not punishment.

Core Idea
The believer feels pressure but not punishment; disbelievers face constant terror yet no seasonal relief.

This passage tackles two interconnected issues about the grave. First, it critiques a speculative view that punishment is temporarily lifted for disbelievers on certain days, calling for evidence. Second, it clarifies the believer's experience, distinguishing pressure from punishment using prophetic teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the author's critical tone toward Abu al-Mu'in's claim and his shift to affirming the believer's state.
2
Identify the two main parts
The passage has two clear sections: the critique of temporary punishment relief, and the explanation of the believer's pressure vs punishment.
Look for where the author says 'fihi bahath' (this is questionable) as a turning point.
3
Examine the evidence for the believer's state
The author cites two hadiths to show that the believer undergoes pressure, not punishment. Compare the imagery: a mother's squeeze and kohl for inflamed eyes.
Notice the hadith to 'Umar is incomplete due to page break.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما قاله الشيخ أبو المعين في أصوله على ما نقله عنه القونوي من أن عذاب القبر حق سواء كان مؤمنا أم كافرا أم مطيعا أم فاسقا ولكن إذا كان كافرا فعذابه يدوم في القبر إلى يوم القيامة ويرفع عنه العذاب يوم الجمعة وشهر رمضان بحرمة النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم؛ لأنه ما دام في الأحياء لا يعذبهم الله تعالى بحرمته، فكذلك في القبر يرفع عنهم وكل رمضان بحرمته، ففيه بحث؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى نقل صحيح أو دليل صريح، فالصواب ما قاله القونوي من هول ذلك وخوفه، لما أنه كان يتنعم بنعم الله سبحانه ولم يشكر الإنعام حقه. أن المؤمن إن كان مطيعا لا يكون له عذاب القبر، ويكون له ضغطة فيجد رضي الله عنها: قال : ويدل عليه ما روي عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أنه قال لعائشة كيف حالكِ عند ضغطة القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير؟ ثم قال يا حميراء إن ضغطة القبر للمؤمن كغمز الأم رجل ولدها، وسؤال منكر ونكير للمؤمن كالإثمد للعين إذا رمدت)). وكذا روي عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أنه قال لعمر رضي الله عنه: ( فكيف حالك إذا أتاك فتانا
As for what Shaykh Abu al-Mu'in said in his Usul, as transmitted by al-Qunawi, that the punishment of the grave is true whether the person is a believer or disbeliever, obedient or disobedient, but if he is a disbeliever, his punishment continues in the grave until the Day of Resurrection, but it is lifted from him on Friday and the month of Ramadan by the sanctity of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; because as long as he was among the living, Allah did not punish them by his sanctity, so likewise in the grave it is lifted from them, and every Ramadan by his sanctity—this is questionable; because it requires a sound transmission or clear proof. The correct view is what al-Qunawi said about the terror and fear of that, because he was enjoying the blessings of Allah the Glorious and did not thank Him properly for His blessings. That the believer, if obedient, does not have punishment in the grave, but he has pressure. And it is said: and it is indicated by what was narrated from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said to 'A'ishah: 'How will you be at the pressure of the grave and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir?' Then he said: 'O Humayra', the pressure of the grave for the believer is like the squeezing of a mother's leg to her child, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir for the believer is like kohl to the eye when it is inflamed.' And likewise it was narrated from the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, that he said to 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him: 'How will you be when the two testers come to you...
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct but related discussions. First, the author critiques the view of Shaykh Abu al-Mu'in transmitted by al-Qunawi, which holds that the punishment of the grave is universal but is lifted from disbelievers on Fridays and during Ramadan due to the sanctity of the Prophet. The author finds this questionable because it lacks a sound transmission or clear proof. He accepts al-Qunawi's reported alternative that the disbeliever experiences terror and fear because he failed to thank Allah for blessings. Second, the author states that the obedient believer has no punishment but does experience pressure (ضغطة) in the grave. He supports this with two hadiths: one to 'A'ishah describing the pressure as like a mother's gentle squeeze and the questioning as soothing like kohl; and the beginning of a hadith to 'Umar about the two testers (فتانا القبر). The passage thus clarifies the difference between punishment and pressure, and critiques weak theological claims.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
ضغطة القبر
منكر ونكير
حرمة النبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that believers suffer punishment in the grave similar to disbelievers.
Correction: The passage clarifies that obedient believers do not suffer punishment (عذاب القبر), but only pressure (ضغطة القبر), which is mild and even beneficial like kohl.

Key Takeaway
Disbelievers suffer constant terror in the grave, while believers experience only a gentle pressure, not punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The disbeliever suffers constant terror for failing to thank Allah for blessings. List three blessings you enjoyed today without consciously thanking Allah. How will you answer for that ingratitude in the grave if you do not repent now?
?
The questioning of Munkar and Nakir is like kohl to an inflamed eye for the believer—soothing and healing. But that requires a faith that is alive and tested. If the angels came to you tonight, would that moment be relief or agony? What one change can you make before sleep to tip the scale toward relief?

The Soul's Return for the Questioning of the Grave
Argument that the soul must return for the angels' questioning, with analogy and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the soul must be present during the grave questioning, based on the rational argument from voluntary action and the supporting analogies from sleep and the hadith.

Core Idea
The soul must return because answering the angels is a voluntary act requiring the soul.

This lesson examines a critical theological argument for the soul's temporary reunion with the body during the grave's questioning. The author presents a rational proof based on voluntary action, then addresses an objection using the example of sleep and a prophetic hadith about tooth pain. By the end, you'll see how the scholars reconcile sensation without soul with voluntary action requiring the soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully and then its literal translation. Notice the structure: a main argument, an objection, and a response.
2
Identify the key argument
The passage states that answering the two angels is a voluntary action, which cannot be performed without the soul. This establishes the necessity of the soul's return.
Voluntary action (فعل اختياري) is central.
3
Consider the sleep analogy
The objection suggests that the soul might not need to be physically present because in sleep, the soul leaves but remains connected. Reflect on how this analogy supports rather than refutes the argument.
4
Analyze the hadith about tooth pain
The Prophet's analogy shows that pain can exist without a soul in the tooth, but this is sensation, not voluntary action. The hadith does not disprove the need for the soul in voluntary acts.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Combine the rational argument and the scriptural support to understand the doctrine that the soul returns for the grave questioning. Note how the author distinguishes between voluntary acts and mere sensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[صودي؟] التوقف إلا أن كلامه هنا يدل على إعادة الروح، إذ جواب الملكين فعل اختياري فلا يتصور بدون الروح. وقيل: قد يتصور ألا ترى أن النائم يخرج روحه ويكون روحه متصلا بجسده حتى يتألم في المنام ويتنعم؟ وقد روي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام: أنه سئل كيف يوجع اللحم في القبر ولم يكن فيه الروح؟ فقال صلى الله عليه وسلم: كما يوجع سنك وليس فيه الروح.
[?] The pause except that his speech here indicates the return of the soul, because the answer to the two angels is a voluntary action, so it cannot be imagined without the soul. And it was said: It can be imagined – do you not see that the sleeping person takes out his soul and his soul remains connected to his body until he feels pain in his dream and delight? And it was narrated from him (peace and blessings be upon him) that he was asked: How is the flesh pained in the grave when there is no soul in it? He said: Just as your tooth is pained while there is no soul in it.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage argues for the necessity of the soul being returned to the body during the grave's questioning. It begins by stating that the answer to the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) is a voluntary action, and a voluntary action cannot be performed without the soul. This is the main argument. Then it addresses a potential objection: one might think that the soul can be absent because in sleep the soul leaves the body yet the sleeper still experiences pain or pleasure. The passage counters this by explaining that in sleep the soul remains connected to the body. Finally, it cites a hadith where the Prophet was asked how the flesh can feel pain in the grave without the soul, and he answered with the analogy of a toothache: even though the tooth has no soul, it still feels pain. This hadith supports the possibility of sensation without the soul, but the author is using it to show that the soul is not necessary for physical pain, but the questioning is a different case because it involves voluntary response.

Key Terms
روح
جواب الملكين
اختياري
النائم
قبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about toothache proves that the soul is not needed for any experience in the grave, including the questioning.
Correction: The hadith only addresses physical pain (sensation), not voluntary actions like answering. The questioning is a voluntary act and thus requires the soul.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must the soul be present for the questioning in the grave?
A) Because the questioning is a voluntary action that requires the soul.
B) Because the hadith says so.
C) Because the soul feels pain.
D) Because the angels require it.

Key Takeaway
The soul must return to the body during the grave questioning because responding to the angels is a voluntary act that requires the soul, as supported by rational analogy and prophetic hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know you will be questioned in the grave. Are you now preparing answers that require the presence of your soul—meaning sincere and conscious responses? Or will your answers be absent, like a body without a soul?
?
The hadith says your tooth can ache without a soul. But the questioning demands your soul. Are you living as if your most important answers can be given without your heart's presence? What would change if you remembered that your soul must be fully present to give account?
?
You sleep every night, and your soul leaves yet remains connected. This is a reminder of the grave. When you die, will your soul be ready to return for that first test? What are you doing today to ensure you pass the questioning?

Abu al-Mu'in's View on Lifting Punishment for Disbelievers on Friday and Ramadan
Author reports and criticizes Abu al-Mu'in's claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific claim made by Abu al-Mu'in regarding the lifting of punishment for disbelievers on Friday and Ramadan, and the author's critique that it lacks sound proof.

Core Idea
A claim without proof is not accepted, even if it seems merciful.

This passage presents a specific theological opinion about the punishment of the grave. Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi proposed that while punishment is universal, it is lifted for disbelievers on Fridays and in Ramadan due to the Prophet's honor. The author examines this claim and finds it unsupported by evidence. Let's see how he evaluates it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: first the claim, then the author's critique.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ففيه بحث' which signals the criticism.
2
Identify the conditions of the claim
Abu al-Mu'in says punishment is universal but for disbelievers it continues until Judgment Day except it is lifted on Friday and in Ramadan by the honor of the Prophet.
The reasoning is that during the Prophet's life, disbelievers were not punished because of his honor, so similarly after death.
3
Understand the author's critique
The author states that this view requires a sound transmission (naql sahih) or explicit proof (dalil sarih), which is lacking. He affirms al-Qunawi's statement about the horror of punishment as the correct stance.
This shows the importance of evidence in theological claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما قاله الشيخ أبو المعين في أصوله على ما نقله عنه القونوي من أن عذاب القبر حق سواء كان مؤمنا أم كافرا أم مطيعا أم فاسقا ولكن إذا كان كافرا فعذابه يدوم في القبر إلى يوم القيامة ويرفع عنه العذاب يوم الجمعة وشهر رمضان بحرمة النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم؛ لأنه ما دام في الأحياء لا يعذبهم الله تعالى بحرمته، فكذلك في القبر يرفع عنهم وكل رمضان بحرمته، ففيه بحث؛ لأنه يحتاج إلى نقل صحيح أو دليل صريح، فالصواب ما قاله القونوي من هول ذلك وخوفه، لما أنه كان يتنعم بنعم الله سبحانه ولم يشكر الإنعام حقه.
As for what Sheikh Abu al-Mu'in said in his Usul, as transmitted by al-Qunawi, that the punishment of the grave is true whether the person is a believer or disbeliever, obedient or sinful; but if he is a disbeliever, his punishment continues in the grave until the Day of Resurrection, and the punishment is lifted from him on Friday and the month of Ramadan by the honor of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him); because as long as he is among the living, Allah does not punish them by his honor, so likewise in the grave it is lifted from them, and every Ramadan by his honor. This is open to discussion because it requires a sound transmission or explicit proof. The correct thing is what al-Qunawi said about the horror and fear of that, because he was enjoying the blessings of Allah but did not thank the favor as it deserved.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage presents the view of Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi as transmitted by al-Qunawi, which states that punishment in the grave is universal (for believer and disbeliever alike) but that for disbelievers the punishment continues until the Judgment Day except that it is lifted on Friday and during Ramadan due to the honor of the Prophet. The author then critiques this view, saying it requires a sound transmission or explicit textual proof, which is lacking. He then affirms that the correct position is what al-Qunawi himself said about the horror and fear of the punishment, presumably meaning that the disbeliever experiences the full horror as a result of his ingratitude. Note that the author does not fully endorse al-Qunawi's statement about the lifting but rather uses al-Qunawi's other statement about horror as the correct view.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر (punishment of the grave)
يرفع العذاب (punishment is lifted)
يوم الجمعة (Friday)
شهر رمضان (month of Ramadan)
بحرمة النبي (by the honor of the Prophet)
نقل صحيح (sound transmission)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the author agrees with the lifting of punishment because he partially quotes al-Qunawi.
Correction: The author explicitly states the view needs proof, and he affirms al-Qunawi's statement about horror, not the lifting.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider Abu al-Mu'in's view problematic?
A) Because it contradicts the Quran.
B) Because it requires a sound proof which is absent.
C) Because al-Qunawi himself rejected it.
D) Because the Prophet's honor does not apply to disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Even a seemingly merciful claim about disbelievers must be backed by sound evidence; otherwise it is not accepted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to accept a comforting belief about the afterlife without any evidence from the Quran or Sunnah? What does this say about your attachment to truth over comfort?
?
When you hear a claim that seems merciful, do you stop to check if it is supported by revelation, or do you embrace it because it feels good?
?
The passage highlights the horror of the grave for those who enjoyed blessings without gratitude. Are you grateful enough that you would not fear that horror?

The Obedient Believer's State in the Grave: No Punishment but Pressing
Author states that the obedient believer has no punishment but experiences a pressing, with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the obedient believer experiences no punishment in the grave but only a gentle pressing, as evidenced by hadiths comparing it to a mother's pinch and beneficial kohl.

Core Idea
Believers face a gentle squeeze, not punishment, in the grave.

This lesson explores the delicate balance between the believer's security from punishment and the reality of the grave's experience. The author presents two hadiths that illustrate how the pressing and questioning are mild and even beneficial, reassuring the believer. By the end, you will appreciate the nuance of Islamic teachings on the grave's trials.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the author's main claim about the obedient believer's state in the grave.
The claim is that the obedient believer has no punishment but experiences a pressing.
2
Examine the first hadith with 'Aisha
Focus on the hadith where the Prophet speaks to 'Aisha. What analogies does he use for the pressing and the questioning?
The pressing is like a mother pinching her child's leg; the questioning is like kohl for an inflamed eye.
3
Examine the second hadith with 'Umar
Read the hadith with 'Umar. What is 'Umar's concern, and how does the Prophet's response reassure him?
'Umar asks if he will have his intellect; when assured, he says he does not care.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن المؤمن إن كان مطيعا لا يكون له عذاب القبر، ويكون له ضغطة [فيجد رضي الله عنها؟] قال : ويدل عليه ما روي عن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أنه قال لعائشة: كيف حالكِ عند ضغطة القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير؟ ثم قال يا حميراء إن ضغطة القبر للمؤمن كغمز الأم رجل ولدها، وسؤال منكر ونكير للمؤمن كالإثمد للعين إذا رمدت. وكذا روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال لعمر رضي الله عنه: فكيف حالك إذا أتاك فتانا القبر؟ فقال عمر: أفأكون في مثل هذه الحالة ويكون عقلي معي؟ قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: نعم، قال عمر: إذاً لا أبالي.
That the believer, if he is obedient, has no punishment of the grave, but he has a pressing [she was pleased with her?] He said: and it is evidenced by what is narrated from the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) that he said to 'Aisha: 'How is your state regarding the pressing of the grave and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir?' Then he said: 'O Humayra', the pressing of the grave for the believer is like a mother's pinch on her child's leg, and the questioning of Munkar and Nakir for the believer is like kohl for the eye when it is inflamed.' And likewise it is narrated from the Prophet that he said to 'Umar: 'How is your state when the two testers of the grave come to you?' 'Umar said: 'Will I be in such a state and my intellect be with me?' He said: 'Yes.' 'Umar said: 'Then I do not care.'
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage clarifies the state of an obedient believer in the grave. It first states that such a believer will not experience punishment (عذاب) but will experience a pressing (ضغطة). The phrase 'فيجد رضي الله عنها' is unclear in the OCR, but likely it is part of the context. Then it provides two hadiths as evidence. In the first, the Prophet tells 'Aisha that the pressing for a believer is like a mother gently pinching her child's leg, and the questioning is like applying kohl to an inflamed eye — uncomfortable but beneficial. In the second hadith, 'Umar asks whether he will have his intellect during that situation, and when assured, he says he does not care, indicating that with full mental awareness, the believer will be reassured despite the pressing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think believers experience no discomfort in the grave at all.
Correction: The hadith shows that believers experience a gentle pressing, but it is not punishment and is bearable.

Checkpoint

A) Because he knows he will be punished.
B) Because his intellect will be with him.
C) Because the tests are easy.
D) Because he will not be questioned.

Key Takeaway
The obedient believer is spared punishment but faces a gentle pressing and questioning, with the comfort of retained intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet compared the grave's pressing to a mother's gentle pinch. Are you living in such a way that your greatest fear in the grave is a mild discomfort rather than severe punishment? What habits or sins must you abandon to ensure your grave is free of punishment?
?
When you imagine standing before Munkar and Nakir, do you feel the calm confidence of 'Umar who said, 'I do not care'? What one change can you make today to build that certainty, knowing your intellect will remain sharp?
?
If the pressing and questioning are like soothing kohl to the righteous, what does that reveal about your current spiritual vision? Are you walking in obedience that will turn even the trials of the grave into mercy, or are you ignoring the call to prepare?

Al-Qunawi's View on Friday Punishment Refuted
Al-Qunawi's claim and its refutation using certain proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author rejects al-Qunawi's specific claim about the punishment of the grave being permanently lifted on Friday for all disobedient believers.

Core Idea
Beliefs require certain proofs; unsupported claims about the unseen are definitely false.

Al-Qunawi proposed a detailed view about the punishment of the grave being suspended on Friday and its night. The author responds by first establishing the epistemological standard for belief—certain proofs—then examining the evidence. This passage is important because it shows how kalam scholars weigh proofs in matters of the unseen and reject baseless claims even if they seem plausible.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Qunawi's claim
Start by reading the first part of the passage where al-Qunawi's view is presented. Notice the specific details: punishment is cut off on Friday and Friday night and does not return, and if one dies on those times, punishment is only for an hour.
Al-Qunawi is a known scholar; this view is not mainstream.
2
Identify the author's refutation
Read the author's response. He begins with a methodological principle: beliefs require certain proofs. Then he discusses the nature of isolated hadiths and tawatur. Finally, he declares the specific claim baseless and definitely false.
Pay attention to the phrase 'bāṭil qaṭʿan' (definitely false) — a strong rejection.
3
Understand the epistemological standard
The author stresses that in matters of belief (ʿaqāʾid), only certain proofs (adilla yaqīniyya) are acceptable. Isolated hadiths (āḥād) are speculative unless they reach mutawātir in meaning.
This is a key principle in Sunni kalam methodology.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider why the author says 'I do not know any basis for this' and declares it definitely false. What does this teach about how scholars evaluate claims about the unseen?
The author is not denying that punishment may be lifted for some on Friday, but rejecting the absolute and permanent nature of al-Qunawi's claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال القونوي وإن كان عاصيا يكون له عذاب القبر وضغطة القبر لكن ينقطع عنه عذاب القبر يوم الجمعة وليلة الجمعة ولا يعود العذاب إلى يوم القيامة وإن مات يوم الجمعة أو ليلة الجمعة يكون له العذاب ساعة واحدة وضغطة القبر، ثم ينقطع عنه العذاب ولا يعود إلى يوم القيامة. انتهى. فلا يخفى أن المعتبر في العقائد هو الأدلة اليقينية وأحاديث الآحاد لو ثبتت إنما تكون ظنية، اللهم إلا إذا تعدد طرقه بحيث صار متواترا معنويا فحينئذ يكون قطعيا، نعم ثبت في الجملة أن من مات [العذاب عنه؟] إلا أنه لا الجمعة أو ليلة الجمعة يرفع العذاب عنه، يوم إلا أنه لا يعود إليه إلى يوم القيامة فلا أعرف له أصلا وكذا رفع العذاب يوم الجمعة وليلتها مطلقا عن كل عاص، ثم لا يعود إلى يوم القيامة فإنه باطل قطعيا.
And al-Qunawi said: If a believer is disobedient, he will have the punishment of the grave and the pressing of the grave, but the punishment of the grave is cut off from him on Friday and Friday night and does not return until the Day of Resurrection; if he dies on Friday or Friday night, he has punishment for one hour and the pressing, then the punishment is cut off and does not return until the Day of Resurrection. End. Then it is not hidden that what is considered in beliefs is certain proofs, and isolated hadiths, if established, are only speculative, unless their chains multiply so that it becomes mutawatir in meaning, then it is certain. Yes, it is established in general that whoever dies [the punishment from him?], except that on Friday or Friday night the punishment is lifted from him, but it does not return to him until the Day of Resurrection – I do not know any basis for this. And likewise, the lifting of punishment on Friday and its night absolutely from every disobedient person, then it does not return until the Day of Resurrection is definitely false.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents al-Qunawi's specific view regarding the disobedient believer: he undergoes punishment and pressing in the grave, but the punishment is cut off on Friday and Friday night and does not return until the Day of Resurrection. If he dies on those times, he only suffers for an hour. The author then refutes this claim. He begins by stating that beliefs require certain proofs (adilla yaqiniyya), and that isolated hadiths (ahad al-ahad) are speculative unless they reach the level of tawatur ma'nawi. He then asserts that while it is generally established that punishment may be lifted for some on Friday, the specific claim that it does not return is baseless and definitely false. The author's language is strong, calling the claim 'batil qat'an' (definitely false).

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
ينقطع العذاب
يوم الجمعة
أحاديث الآحاد
متواتر معنوي
باطل قطعيا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the author accepts al-Qunawi's view or that the claim has a basis in reliable hadith.
Correction: The author clearly rejects the specific claim as having no basis, calling it 'bāṭil qaṭʿan' (definitely false). He only concedes a general lifting for some, not the absolute and permanent lifting.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what type of evidence is required for beliefs in matters of the grave?
A) Isolated hadiths only.
B) Certain proofs (adilla yaqiniyya).
C) Speculative proofs.
D) Consensus of scholars.

Key Takeaway
Claims about the unseen must be supported by certain proofs; absent that, they are rejected, even if proposed by a scholar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a belief you hold about the afterlife that you have not verified from certain sources (like the Quran or mutawatir hadith). Are you willing to question it? What would it take for you to accept it as true?
?
The author dismisses al-Qunawi's view as baseless. Is there any belief you hold that, if subjected to the same standard of certain proof, would be found lacking? How would you respond?
?
Consider the weight of the author's statement: 'The lifting of punishment on Friday for every disobedient person is definitely false.' Do you ever embrace comforting narratives about the grave without certain proof? What does that reveal about your heart?

Quranic Proofs for Barzakh Reward and Punishment
Imam Abu Hanifa cites two Quranic verses as evidence for immediate reward/punishment in the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two Quranic proofs for reward and punishment in the intermediate state (barzakh) and the sound view that it involves both soul and body.

Core Idea
The Quran proves that reward and punishment begin immediately after death in the barzakh.

One of the key beliefs of Ahl al-Sunna is that the soul experiences reward or punishment immediately after death, before the Resurrection. Imam Abu Hanifa presents two Quranic verses to support this. The first shows martyrs receiving provision from their Lord, and the second shows the people of Noah entering fire after drowning. He also notes the importance of the letter fa in the second verse, indicating immediate sequence. Let's read the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Read the two verses cited and note the states they describe: martyrs alive and receiving provision, and the drowned entering fire. Consider what they imply about the afterlife before resurrection.
The first verse addresses martyrs specifically, but the principle applies to all believers.
2
Understand the letter fa
Focus on the second verse: 'fa'udkhilu naran' (then made to enter a fire). The author explains that the letter fa indicates immediate sequence, meaning punishment followed drowning without delay.
This grammatical point is crucial for proving barzakh punishment.
3
Learn the scholarly disagreement
Note that scholars disagreed whether the experience involves the soul alone, body alone, or both. The author declares that the soundest view is both, but we affirm the reality without investigating the modality.
This shows the balance between evidence and tafwid (leaving the how to Allah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من الأدلة على إنعام أهل الطاعة وإيلام أهل المعصية قوله سبحانه: ﴿وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللهِ أَمْوَاتًا بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِنْدَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ فَرِحِينَ بِمَا آتَاهُمُ اللهُ مِنْ فَضْلِهِ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٦٩-١٧٠]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿مِمَّا خَطِيئَاتِهِمْ أُغْرِقُوا فَأُدْخِلُوا نَارًا﴾ [نوح: ٢٥]، فإن الأصل في وضع الفاء التعقيب، واختلف في أنه بالروح أو بالبدن أو بهما وهو الأصح منهما، إلا أنا نؤمن بصحته ولا نشتغل بكيفيته واختلف في حقيقة الروح، فقيل: إنه جسم لطيف شابك الجسد مشابكة الماء بالعود الأخضر، أجرى الله تعالى العادة بأن يخلق الحياة ما استمرت هي في الجسد، فإذا فارقته
Then among the proofs for the blessing of the obedient people and the punishing of the disobedient people are His words: 'And never think of those who have been killed in the cause of Allah as dead. Rather, they are alive with their Lord, receiving provision, rejoicing in what Allah has given them of His bounty' (Al 'Imran 169-170), and His words: 'Because of their sins they were drowned and made to enter a fire' (Nuh 25). For the principle of the positioning of the letter fa is immediate sequence. And there is disagreement whether this is with the soul or with the body or with both, and the latter is the sounder of the two. However, we believe in its truth and do not occupy ourselves with its modality. And there is disagreement about the reality of the soul. It is said: It is a subtle body interpenetrating the body like the penetration of water into green wood. Allah has made it His custom to create life as long as it remains in the body, and when it leaves it...
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage provides Quranic evidence for the reality of reward and punishment in the intermediate state (barzakh). The first verse (Al 'Imran 169-170) shows that martyrs are alive and receiving provision from their Lord, indicating a reward. The second verse (Nuh 25) shows that the people of Noah were drowned and then made to enter a fire, implying punishment after death. The author notes that the letter fa ('then') indicates immediate sequence, showing the punishment occurs right after death. Then he mentions the scholarly disagreement on whether these experiences are with the soul alone, the body alone, or both, affirming that the correct view is that they involve both. He then turns to the reality of the soul, presenting the view that it is a subtle body (jism latif) that interpenetrates the body like water in green wood, and that Allah's custom is to create life as long as the soul remains in the body. The passage ends mid-sentence, indicating that the discussion continues.

Key Terms
إنعام (blessing)
إيلام (punishing)
الذين قتلوا في سبيل الله (martyrs)
أحياء عند ربهم يرزقون (alive with their Lord, receiving provision)
خطيئات (sins)
الفاء التعقيب (fa indicating immediacy)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that reward and punishment in the grave are purely spiritual with no bodily involvement.
Correction: The author states the soundest view is that both soul and body are involved, as indicated by the Quranic verses and transmitted from the Salaf.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Quranic verse is used to show immediate punishment after death?
A) Al 'Imran 169-170
B) Nuh 25
C) Al-Fatiha 1-7
D) Al-Ikhlas 1-4

Key Takeaway
The Quran affirms that reward and punishment begin in the grave, and the sound view is that both soul and body experience it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The martyrs are already receiving provision right now. Are you living today as if death opens into immediate reward or punishment, or do you put that reality out of your mind? What can you do today to prepare for that moment?
?
The letter 'fa' in Nuh 25 shows that punishment followed sin without any delay. If you were to die right now, what sin would you fear most its immediate consequence? Will you sincerely repent from it today?
?
Imam Abu Hanifa says we affirm the reality of barzakh reward and punishment without asking 'how'. Is your faith strong enough to accept what Allah has told you even when you cannot fully understand it? How can you strengthen that trust starting today?

The Reality of the Soul as a Subtle Body
Imam Abu Hanifa discusses the reality of the soul as a subtle body interpenetrating the body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description of the soul as a subtle body that interpenetrates the body and the relationship between soul and life.

Core Idea
The soul is a subtle body that interpenetrates the physical body like water in green wood.

After discussing reward and punishment in the barzakh, the author turns to a deeper question: what is the soul itself? Muslim theologians have debated its nature. Imam Abu Hanifa presents one view: the soul is a subtle body that interpenetrates the physical body, giving it life. This analogy helps us understand the connection between soul and body.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the soul
Read the Arabic description of the soul as a subtle body (jism latif). Note the technical term 'mushabaka' (interpenetration).
2
Understand the analogy
The soul interpenetrates the body like water interpenetrates green wood. Water is not the wood but permeates it completely. Similarly, the soul is not the body but pervades it.
This analogy shows both distinction and intimate connection.
3
Learn the link between soul and life
Allah's custom (ada) is that life is created as long as the soul remains in the body. When the soul leaves, life ceases. This underscores the soul's role as the principle of life.
This is not a necessary causal connection but Allah's habitual way.

Source Text

The Nature of the Soul: Opinions and the Correct View
Author discusses opinions on the soul and defends the subtle body view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different opinions on the nature of the soul in Islamic theology, the author's defense of the soul as a subtle body, and the ultimate recommendation to entrust its knowledge to God.

Core Idea
The soul's true nature is beyond full human comprehension; we must entrust its knowledge to Allah.

In this passage, the author presents two views on the relationship between the soul and life, and explains why the soul is best described as a subtle body. He then reconciles this with the Quranic verse that states the spirit is from the command of the Lord, ultimately advising that the most correct position is to entrust the knowledge of the soul's essence to Allah. This lesson will guide you through these arguments and the final conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the first phrase appears corrupt; focus on the coherent parts.
2
Identify the two opinions on the soul
The passage presents two views: one comparing life to the sun's ray (favored by Sufis), and another describing the soul as an essence permeating the body like rosewater (held by some Ahl al-Sunnah). Note how the author differentiates them.
3
Understand the author's preferred view and its evidence
The author favors the view that the soul is a subtle body (jism latif) rather than an essence. He cites reports of the soul exiting, entering, ascending, and descending as evidence.
4
Examine the reconciliation with the Quranic verse
The author addresses the potential contradiction with 'The spirit is from the command of my Lord' (Al-Isra:85). He offers two explanations: either the command belongs entirely to God, or the spirit was created by an instant command. This shows that the discussion does not contradict the verse.
5
Reflect on the final conclusion
The author concludes that the strongest opinion is to entrust the knowledge of the soul's true nature to God, as held by the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah. Consider why this is a prudent theological stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
توفت الموت الحياة. وقالوا: الحياة للروح بمنزلة الشعاع للشمس، فإن الله تعالى أجرى العادة بأن يخلق النور والضياء في العالم ما دامت الشمس طالعة، كذلك يخلق الحياة للبدن ما دامت الروح فيه ثابتة، وإلى هذا القول مال المشايخ الصوفية. وقال جماعة من أهل السنة والجماعة: الروح جوهر سارية في البدن كسريان ماء الورد في الورد. انتهى. وهو لا يغاير القول الأول إلا في اختلافهم أنه جوهر أو جسم لطيف، والأخير هو الصحيح بدليل ما ورد من أن الروح إذا خرجت من الجسد وإذا دخلت وأمثال ذلك من العروج إلى عليين ومن النزول إلى سجين، وهذا الكلام في تحقيق المرام ما ينافي قوله سبحانه: ﴿ قُلِ الرُّوحُ مِنْ أَمْرِ رَبِّي وَمَا أُوتِيَتُمْ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ إِلَّا قَلِيلًا ﴾ [الإسراء: ٨٥]، فإن الأمر كله لله تعالى، أو لأن الروح خلق بالأمر التنجيزي كبعض المخلوقات، وأكثر الكائنات خلقوا بالوصف التدريجي، ولذا قال الله تعالى: ﴿أَلَا لَهُ الْخَلْقُ وَالْأَمْرُ﴾ [الأعراف: ٥٤]، مع أن الكلام في جنسه على طريق الإجمال هو من العلم القليل استثنى الله تعالى بقوله: ﴿وَمَا أُوتِيتُمْ مِنَ الْعِلْمِ إِلَّا قَلِيلًا﴾ [الإسراء: ٨٥] على أن أولى الأقاويل وأقواها أن يفوض علمه إلى الله تعالى، وهو قول جمهور أهل السنة والجماعة.
The death [؟] life. And they said: Life is to the spirit (ruh) like the ray of the sun, for God Almighty has made it customary (adah) to create light and brightness in the world as long as the sun is rising; likewise He creates life for the body as long as the spirit is established in it. And the Sufi masters inclined to this view. And a group of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah said: The spirit is an essence (jawhar) permeating the body like the permeation of rosewater in the rose. End. And it does not differ from the first view except in their disagreement whether it is an essence or a subtle body (jism latif), and the latter is correct based on what has been reported that the spirit when it exits the body and when it enters, and similar things, ascending to 'Illiyin and descending to Sijjin. And this speech in achieving the goal does not contradict His saying, exalted: 'Say: The spirit is from the command of my Lord, and you have not been given of knowledge except a little.' [Al-Isra: 85], for the command is entirely for God Almighty, or because the spirit was created by an existential command like some creatures, and most beings were created by gradual description. Therefore God said: 'Indeed, His is the creation and the command.' [Al-A'raf: 54]. And even though speech about its genus in summary is from the little knowledge which God exempted by His saying: 'And you have not been given of knowledge except a little.' [Al-Isra:85]. Moreover, the most appropriate and strongest of opinions is to entrust its knowledge to God Almighty, and that is the saying of the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage discusses the nature of the soul (ruh) and life. It presents three views: first, that life is to the spirit as the sun's ray is to the sun—God creates life as long as the spirit is present; this view is favored by Sufi masters. Second, that the spirit is an essence (jawhar) permeating the body like rosewater in a rose, held by some Ahl al-Sunnah. The author notes that the second view differs from the first only whether the spirit is an essence or a subtle body (jism latif). He declares the latter (subtle body) correct, citing reports of the spirit exiting and entering the body and ascending to 'Illiyin or descending to Sijjin. Then he addresses the Quranic verse 'Say: The spirit is from the command of my Lord' (Al-Isra:85), explaining that this does not contradict the discussion because either the command belongs entirely to God, or the spirit was created by an instant command while most creatures were created gradually. He also references Al-A'raf:54. Finally, he concludes that the best and strongest view is to entrust the knowledge of the soul's true nature to God, which is the position of the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Key Terms
الروح (ruh)
الجوهر (jawhar)
الجسم اللطيف (jism latif)
العادة (adah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul's nature can be fully comprehended by human reason.
Correction: The passage teaches that the soul's essence is known only to Allah, and the most correct position is to entrust its knowledge to Him.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the most appropriate position regarding the nature of the soul?
A) It is a ray of life derived from the sun.
B) It is an essence permeating the body like rosewater.
C) It is a subtle body (jism latif).
D) To entrust its knowledge to God Almighty.

Key Takeaway
The soul's essence is known only to Allah, and the most prudent position is to entrust its knowledge to Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the author says the strongest opinion is to entrust knowledge of the soul to Allah, is there a deep question about your own existence that you have been trying to answer on your own? How does it feel to release that need to know and trust that Allah knows best?

Think of a moment when you were frustrated by not understanding something about your faith or yourself. Does this passage challenge your impulse to demand full clarity before submitting? What would it look like to say 'I entrust this to Allah' and move forward in trust?
?
The spirit is from the command of your Lord—a reality so profound that your knowledge of it is but a little. Does your heart rest in that mystery, or does it resist? What would change in your life if you fully accepted that some truths are not for you to grasp?
