Quranic Proofs of Bodily Resurrection
Imam Abu Hanifa affirms bodily resurrection and cites six Quranic verses as proof, refuting philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Abu Hanifa and the Quran affirm bodily resurrection and refute those who deny it.

Core Idea
The Quran explicitly affirms bodily resurrection, refuting philosophers who deny it.

Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) begins by affirming the resurrection of bodies after death, citing the Quran as decisive evidence. This lesson examines the key verses he presents and shows how they collectively refute the philosophers' denial of bodily resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the flow from Imam's affirmation to the list of verses.
2
Identify the six Quranic verses
Find each verse and understand how it supports bodily resurrection. Note the interpretation given for some verses.
Verses are from Surah Al-Hajj, Al-Kahf, At-Takwir, Ar-Rum, Al-Anbiya, and Al-Mu'minun.
3
Understand the refutation
The passage concludes that these verses refute the philosophers who deny bodily resurrection. Why is this refutation important?
This shows the Quran is the primary source for this belief.
4
Reflect on the importance of bodily resurrection
Consider why bodily resurrection is a core Islamic belief and how these verses establish it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله في كتابه "الوصية": نقر بأن الله تعالى يحيي هذه النفوس بعد الموت يبعثهم الله يوما كان مقداره خمسين ألف سنة للجزاء والثواب وأداء الحقوق لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَنَّ اللهَ يَبْعَثُ مَنْ فِي الْقُبُورِ ﴾ [الحج:7]، انتهى. وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَحَشَرْنَاهُمْ فَلَمْ نُغَادِرْ مِنْهُمْ أَحَدًا﴾ [الكهف:٤٧]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا الْوُحُوشُ حُشِرَتْ﴾ [التكوير: ٥]، أي جمعت، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُوَ الَّذِي يَبْدَأُ الْخَلْقَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُهُ﴾ [الروم: ٢٧]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿كَمَا بَدَأْنَا أَوَّلَ خَلْقٍ نُعِيدُهُ﴾ [الأنبياء: ١٠٤]، أي نعيد أول الخلق في الآخرة مثل الذي بدأناه في أول الخلق في الدنيا حين كونهما إيجادا عن العدم، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ إِنَّكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ تُبْعَثُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون:١٦]، أي للجزاء، ففي هذه الآيات رد على الفلاسفة حيث أنكروا حشر الأجساد.
And Imam al-A'zam (may God have mercy on him) said in his book "al-Wasiyya": We affirm that God Almighty will give life to these souls after death; He will resurrect them on a Day whose measure is fifty thousand years for recompense and reward and fulfillment of rights, according to His saying, exalted: 'And that God will resurrect those in the graves' [Al-Hajj:7]. End. And His saying: 'And We gathered them and did not leave out anyone from them' [Al-Kahf:47]. And His saying: 'And when the wild beasts are gathered' [At-Takwir:5], i.e., collected. And His saying: 'And He is the One who begins creation then repeats it' [Ar-Rum:27]. And His saying: 'As We began the first creation We will repeat it' [Al-Anbiya:104], i.e., We will repeat the first creation in the Hereafter like the beginning of the first creation in this world when both were brought into existence from non-existence. And His saying: 'Then indeed you on the Day of Resurrection will be resurrected' [Al-Mu'minun:16], i.e., for recompense. So in these verses is a refutation of the philosophers who denied the resurrection of bodies (harsh al-ajsad).
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents a direct refutation of philosophers who deny bodily resurrection (harsh al-ajsad). It begins by citing Imam Abu Hanifa's affirmation from his book al-Wasiyya: God will give life to souls after death and resurrect them on a Day lasting fifty thousand years for recompense. Then it lists six Quranic verses as evidence: (1) 'And that God will resurrect those in the graves' (Al-Hajj:7), (2) 'And We gathered them and did not leave out anyone' (Al-Kahf:47), (3) 'And when the wild beasts are gathered' (At-Takwir:5), interpreted as 'collected,' (4) 'And He is the One who begins creation then repeats it' (Ar-Rum:27), (5) 'As We began the first creation We will repeat it' (Al-Anbiya:104), explained as recreating the first creation in the Hereafter exactly as it was created from nothing, and (6) 'Then indeed you on the Day of Resurrection will be resurrected' (Al-Mu'minun:16), for recompense. The passage concludes that these verses together refute the philosophers who deny the resurrection of bodies.

Key Terms
حشر الأجساد
الفلاسفة
البعث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Quran does not clearly affirm bodily resurrection.
Correction: The passage cites multiple explicit verses including 'He will resurrect those in the graves' (Al-Hajj:7) to show clear Quranic affirmation.

Checkpoint
What is the main purpose of the Quranic verses cited in this passage?
A) To prove the existence of God.
B) To affirm the resurrection of bodies.
C) To describe the Day of Judgment in detail.
D) To refute atheists specifically.

Key Takeaway
The Quran provides multiple explicit proofs for bodily resurrection, refuting any denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe you will be resurrected bodily for recompense. Is there a right you owe to another person that you have been avoiding? What concrete step will you take today to fulfill it?
?
The philosophers denied bodily resurrection because they couldn't understand it. When have you doubted or neglected a religious truth because it seemed 'unreasonable'? How does this passage call you to submit your reason to revelation?
?
God will repeat creation exactly as He began it. Do you live as if your body matters eternally? What one habit will you change this week to honor your body as something that will be resurrected?

Imam al-Razi's Wager on Resurrection
Imam al-Razi's pragmatic wager argument for resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Razi's pragmatic wager argument for resurrection, and why it is considered a prudent belief even for those without absolute proof.

Core Idea
Belief in resurrection is a safe bet: salvation if true, no harm if false.

Imam al-Razi presents a compelling argument that appeals to practical reason. He suggests that believing in resurrection is the cautious choice, because the potential gain is immense and the potential loss is trivial. This argument is often compared to Pascal's wager and is presented here in a relaxed debate style.

Guided Path
1
Read the wager argument
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: premise, two possible outcomes, conclusion.
The argument is structured as a conditional: if we believe, then either it's true (saved) or false (no harm).
2
Identify the role of ihtiyat
Notice the term 'الاحتياط' (caution) appears at the end. Understand that this argument establishes that caution dictates belief.
Caution is a legitimate basis for belief in matters where certainty is not attainable.
3
Reflect on the poetic exchange
Read the poet's lines. They reinforce the wager: the believer risks nothing, the denier risks everything.
This poetic example makes the argument memorable.
4
Consider the audience
Think about who this argument is for. It is presented 'by way of relaxation of the rein' – a non-polemical argument for the general public.
This is not a rigorous philosophical proof, but a practical persuasion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ذكر الإمام الرازي على طريق إرخاء العِنان مع الخصم في ميدان البيان حيث قال: فإنا إذا آمنا بالبعث وتأهبنا له فإن كان حقا فقد نجونا وهلك المنكر، وإن كان باطلا لا يضرنا هذا الاعتقاد، غاية ما في الباب أن تفوتنا هذه اللذات الجسمانية، والواجب على العاقل أن لا يبالي بفواتها لكونها في غاية الخساسة؛ إذ هي مشتركة بين الخنافس والديدان والكلاب، ولأنها سريعة الزوال والفناء، فثبت أن الاحتياط في الإيمان بالمعاد، ولهذا قال الشاعر: قال المنجم والطبيب كلاهما لن يحشر الأموات قلت إليكما إن صح قولكما فلست بخاسر أو صح قولي فالخسار عليكما. كلامه. ونقل البيتان عن علي كرم الله وجهه، ووجهه أنه من قبيل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّا أَوْ إِيَّاكُمْ لَعَلَى هُدًى أَوْ فِي ضَلَالٍ مُّبِينٍ﴾ [سبأ: ٢٤]، لأن الاعتقاد بالمعاد على وجه الاحتياط صحيح في مقام الاعتماد، لأن العلم اليقيني لابد للمجتهد، والحكم الجزمي للمقلد من الأدلة اليقينية الحاصلة من الأدلة النقلية والعقلية كقوله تعالى: ﴿أَمْ حَسِبَ الَّذِينَ اجْتَرَحُوا السَّيِّئَاتِ أَنْ نَجْعَلَهُمْ كَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ سَوَاءً مَّحْيَاهُمْ وَمَمَاتُهُمْ سَاءَ مَا يَحْكُمُونَ﴾ [الجاثية: ٢١]. انتهى
And Imam al-Razi mentioned, by way of relaxation of the rein with the opponent in the field of elucidation, where he said: For if we believe in resurrection (ba'th) and prepare for it, then if it is true we have been saved and the denier perishes, and if it is false this belief does not harm us. The utmost in the matter is that these bodily pleasures escape us. And it is necessary for the intelligent person not to care about their loss because they are extremely base; for they are shared by beetles, worms, and dogs, and because they are quickly passing and perishing. So it is established that caution (ihtiyat) lies in belief in the final return (ma'ad). And for this reason the poet said: The astrologer and the physician both said: The dead will not be resurrected. I said to both: If your statement is true, I am not a loser, but if my statement is true, then the loss is upon you. His speech. And the two verses are related from 'Ali (may God honor his face). And its explanation is that it is from the category of His saying: 'And we or you are either upon guidance or in manifest error' [Saba':24], because belief in the final return on the basis of caution (ihtiyat) is correct in the position of reliance, for certain knowledge is necessary for the mujtahid, and decisive judgment for the muqallid from the certain proofs derived from transmitted and rational evidences (al-adilla al-naqliyya wa al-aqliyya), like His saying: 'Or do those who commit evil deeds think that We will make them equal to those who believe and do righteous deeds, equal in their life and their death? Evil is that which they judge.' [Al-Jathiya:21]. End.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents Imam al-Razi's pragmatic argument for belief in resurrection, often called a 'wager.' The author sets the scene as a relaxed debate. The argument: if we believe in resurrection and prepare for it, then if it is true we are saved and the denier is lost; if it is false, the belief does not harm us—the only loss is some base bodily pleasures that are shared by animals and quickly pass. Thus, reason dictates that caution (ihtiyat) requires belief in the final return (ma'ad). A poetic exchange is cited: an astrologer and a physician deny resurrection; the speaker replies that if they are right he loses nothing, but if he is right they lose everything. These verses are attributed to 'Ali. The argument is compared to the Quranic verse 'And we or you are either upon guidance or in manifest error' (Saba':24), indicating that such cautious belief is valid. The passage then clarifies that certain knowledge is required for the mujtahid, and decisive judgment for the muqallid comes from certain proofs of transmitted and rational evidences, citing Al-Jathiya:21 as an example.

Key Terms
البعث
المعاد
الاحتياط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that belief in resurrection requires a certain, apodictic proof, and that pragmatic arguments are insufficient.
Correction: Imam al-Razi shows that a pragmatic wager is a valid basis for belief, especially for the common person, and is in fact the cautious and rational choice.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi's argument, what happens if one believes in resurrection but it turns out to be false?
A) The believer is greatly harmed.
B) The believer loses nothing except some base bodily pleasures.
C) The believer goes to hell.
D) The believer is still saved because of good deeds.

Key Takeaway
The wager argument shows that believing in resurrection is the cautious and rational choice, as the potential gain (salvation) far outweighs the potential loss (trivial pleasures).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi says that the only loss if you believe wrongly is missing out on 'base bodily pleasures' that even insects and dogs enjoy. Look at your own life: what pleasures are you clinging to that he would call 'base'? Are you willing to let them go for the sake of the afterlife, or are you secretly hoping the wager is wrong so you can keep enjoying them? Make a concrete commitment today to reduce attachment to one such pleasure.
?
The poetic verse at the end imagines a direct confrontation with a denier. If you were to stand before someone who rejects the afterlife, would your own life's testimony—your deeds, your priorities, your fears—support the claim that you truly believe in the wager? Or would your actions show that you are actually betting on the denier's side? Honestly examine one area where your behavior contradicts belief in resurrection, and decide on a specific change.
?
The argument says 'the intelligent person should not care about losing base pleasures.' If you truly internalized that your deepest joys are not in food, status, or comfort but in what prepares you for the Hereafter, how would your daily schedule change? What is one useless habit you can drop today to start 'preparing' in a tangible way?

Caution (Ihtiyat) and Certainty for Mujtahid and Muqallid
Explanation of caution (ihtiyat) and the epistemic roles of mujtahid and muqallid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the epistemic requirements for the mujtahid and the muqallid regarding belief in resurrection, and how caution (ihtiyat) serves as a valid basis for the latter.

Core Idea
The muqallid's belief is valid through caution supported by transmitted proofs.

Having presented the wager argument, the author now clarifies its epistemological basis. He explains that the cautious belief (ihtiyat) is correct for the muqallid, while the mujtahid requires certain knowledge from both transmitted and rational evidences. This is illustrated by a Quranic verse that parallels the structure of the wager.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of the poetic verses
Note the attribution to 'Ali and the connection to the Quranic verse 'And we or you are either upon guidance or in manifest error'.
This verse mirrors the either/or structure of the wager.
2
Understand the role of caution
The passage states that belief on the basis of caution is correct in the position of reliance. This means it is a valid foundation for belief for those who are not scholars.
3
Distinguish mujtahid and muqallid
The mujtahid needs certain knowledge; the muqallid needs decisive judgment based on certain proofs from transmitted and rational evidences.
This shows that the common person is not left without guidance; they rely on the proofs presented by scholars.
4
Reflect on the supporting Quranic verse
The verse from Al-Jathiya is cited as an example of such proof that believers and wrongdoers are not equal.
This verse provides a rational and transmitted basis for the necessity of accountability and resurrection.

The Rational Necessity of the Day of Judgment
Rational argument for the necessity of the Day of Judgment based on wisdom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Day of Judgment is rationally necessary based on the principle of divine wisdom and the nature of this world as a place of trial.

Core Idea
Wisdom demands a final separation between truth and falsehood that this world cannot provide.

Before diving into scriptural evidence for the afterlife, theologians first establish a rational foundation: divine wisdom itself necessitates a day of ultimate judgment. This passage from Sanusi's commentary argues that without such a day, the purpose of trial in this world would be incomplete. Let's explore how he makes this case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rational premise
The argument begins with the claim that wisdom requires separating the truthful from the false in a definitive way. Locate this claim in the passage.
Look for the phrase 'الحكمة تقتضي الفصل'.
2
Understand why this world cannot be that place
The author explains that this world was created for trial and testing, not for final compulsion. Why does that matter?
Trial (الابتلاء) implies choice and uncertainty, not compulsion.
3
See the scriptural confirmation
The passage cites Quran 78:17 as evidence. Reflect on how the verse supports the rational argument.
The verse calls it 'Yawm al-Fasl', the Day of Decision.

Source Text

ثم من المعقول في المسألة أن الحكمة تقتضي الفصل بين المحق والمبطل على وجه يضطر المبطل إلى معرفة حاله في البطلان لئلا تبقى له ريبة في ذلك الشأن، وليست الدنيا بدار هذا الاضطرار؛ لأنها خلقت للابتلاء والاختبار، فلا بد من دار يقع فيها هذا الأمر المختار، ولذا قال الله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ يَوْمَ الْفَصْلِ كَانَ مِيقَاتًا ﴾ [النبأ : ١٧] ؛ ولأن الحكمة تقتضي جزاء كل
Then from what is rationally understood in the matter is that wisdom (hikma) requires separation (fasl) between the truthful (muhaqq) and the false (mubtil) in a manner that forces the false to know his state of falsehood so that no doubt remains for him in that matter. And this world is not an abode of this compulsion because it was created for trial (ibtila') and testing (ikhtibar). So there must be an abode in which this matter of choice occurs. Therefore God said: 'Indeed the Day of Decision (yawm al-fasl) is an appointed time' [An-Naba':17]; and because wisdom requires the recompense of every...

Commentary
This passage provides a rational argument for the necessity of a Day of Judgment. It argues that wisdom (hikma) requires a clear separation (fasl) between the truthful (muhaqq) and the false (mubtil), such that the false are forced to recognize their falsehood and have no remaining doubt. This world, however, is not the place for such compulsion because it was created for trial (ibtila') and testing (ikhtibar). Therefore, there must be another abode where this division happens. The passage cites the Quranic verse 'Indeed the Day of Decision (yawm al-fasl) is an appointed time' (An-Naba':17) as evidence. It then begins to state another aspect: wisdom also requires the recompense of every... but the text is cut off.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This world provides ultimate justice and final separation between truth and falsehood.
Correction: The passage argues that this world cannot be the place of final separation because it was created for trial and testing, not for compulsion.

Checkpoint

A) Because it is too short in duration.
B) Because it was created for trial and testing, not final separation.
C) Because people are ignorant of the truth.
D) Because God constantly changes His decrees.

Key Takeaway
The Day of Judgment is rationally necessary because divine wisdom demands a final, undeniable separation between truth and falsehood that the trial-based life of this world cannot achieve.

Al-Razi's Pragmatic Argument for Resurrection
al-Razi presents a pragmatic argument for belief in resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's prudential argument that belief in resurrection is the safest choice, based on a risk-benefit analysis.

Core Idea
Belief in resurrection is the safest bet: you win if true, lose nothing if false.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi offers a unique approach to defending the resurrection. Rather than attempting a philosophical proof, he presents a practical argument based on risk assessment. By considering the consequences of belief versus disbelief, he shows that the rational person should believe in the resurrection. The argument is illustrated with a poetic analogy and supported by Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that al-Razi begins with a Quranic verse, then presents his argument, then a poem, and finally another verse.
2
Identify the core argument
Al-Razi says: if we believe and prepare for resurrection, then if it is true we are saved; if false, we lose only base pleasures. This is a classic 'Pascal's Wager' style argument.
The argument is based on consequences, not evidence.
3
Analyze the poetic analogy
The poem (attributed to Ali) compares the believer to someone who bets on resurrection: if the deniers are right, he loses nothing; if he is right, they lose everything.
This reinforces the precautionary principle.
4
Connect to Quranic support
Al-Razi cites verses that imply the certainty of resurrection and warn against equating believers and disbelievers. See how these verses back up the argument.
The passage ends with a reminder that certain proofs exist from revelation and reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثل الذي بدأناه في أول الخلق في الدنيا حين كونهما إيجادا عن العدم، وقوله تعالى: ثُمَّ إِنَّكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ تُبْعَثُونَ [المؤمنون:١٦]، أي للجزاء، ففي هذه الآيات رد على الفلاسفة حيث أنكروا حشر [منقطعة؟] الأجساد. وقد ذكر الإمام الرازي على طريق إرخاء العِنان مع الخصم في ميدان البيان حيث قال: فإنا إذا آمنا بالبعث وتأهبنا له فإن كان حقا فقد نجونا وهلك المنكر، وإن كان باطلا لا يضرنا هذا الاعتقاد، غاية ما في الباب أن تفوتنا هذه اللذات الجسمانية، والواجب على العاقل أن لا يبالي بفواتها لكونها في غاية الخساسة؛ إذ هي مشتركة بين الخنافس والديدان والكلاب، ولأنها سريعة الزوال والفناء، فثبت أن الاحتياط في الإيمان بالمعاد، ولهذا قال الشاعر: قال المنجم والطبيب كلاهما لن يحشر الأموات قلت إليكما إن صح قولكما فلست بخاسر أو صح قولي فالخسار عليكما كلامه. ونقل البيتان عن علي كرم الله وجهه، ووجهه أنه من قبيل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّا أَوْ إِيَّاكُمْ لَعَلَى هُدًى أَوْ فِي ضَلَالٍ مُبِينٍ﴾ [سبأ: ٢٤]، لأن الاعتقاد بالمعاد على وجه الاحتياط صحيح في مقام الاعتماد، لأن العلم اليقيني لابد للمجتهد، والحكم الجزمي للمقلد من الأدلة اليقينية الحاصلة من الأدلة النقلية والعقلية كقوله تعالى: ﴿أَمْ حَسِبَ الَّذِينَ اجْتَرَحُوا السَّيِّئَاتِ أَنْ نَجْعَلَهُمْ كَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ سَوَاءً مَّحْيَاهُمْ وَمَمَاتُهُمْ سَاءَ مَا يَحْكُمُونَ﴾ [الجاثية: ٢١]. انتهى
Like that which we began with at the first creation in the world when they were brought into being from nothing, and His saying, Exalted: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be raised up' [al-Mu'minun:16], i.e., for recompense. So in these verses is a refutation of the philosophers where they denied the resurrection of [؟] bodies. And Imam al-Razi mentioned, in the way of letting go the rein with the opponent in the field of exposition, where he said: For if we believe in the resurrection and prepare for it, then if it is true we have been saved and the denier is destroyed, and if it is false this belief does not harm us; the utmost in the matter is that these bodily pleasures elude us, and it is obligatory for the rational person not to care about their loss because they are extremely base, since they are shared by beetles, worms, and dogs, and because they are quick to vanish and perish. So it is established that precaution lies in belief in the final return. And for this the poet said: 'The astrologer and the physician both said: the dead will not be resurrected. I said to you both: if your statement is correct, I am not a loser; or if my statement is correct, then the loss is upon you both.' The two lines are transmitted from Ali, may Allah honor his face, and its point is that it is from the category of His saying: 'Indeed, we or you are upon guidance or in clear error' [Saba':24], because belief in the final return in a precautionary manner is sound in the position of reliance, because certain knowledge is necessary for the mujtahid, and the decisive ruling for the muqallid is from the certain proofs obtained from transmitted and rational proofs, like His saying: 'Or do those who commit evil deeds think that We will make them like those who believe and do righteous deeds, equal in their life and their death? Evil is what they judge' [al-Jathiyah:21]. End.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a pragmatic argument for the resurrection, attributed to Imam al-Razi and supported by a poetic analogy. The argument begins by referencing the Quranic verse promising resurrection as a refutation of philosophers who deny bodily resurrection. Al-Razi's argument is based on risk assessment: if one believes in the resurrection and prepares for it, then if it is true, he is saved and the denier is destroyed; if it is false, the believer loses nothing except base bodily pleasures that are worthless and shared by lowly creatures. Thus, prudence dictates belief. This is compared to the poet's lines, attributed to Ali, where an astrologer and physician deny resurrection, but the speaker points out that if they are wrong, he is safe, and if they are wrong, they lose. This is analogous to the Quranic verse 'We or you are upon guidance or in clear error.' The passage concludes by affirming that precautionary belief is valid, and that certain proofs for the resurrection come from both transmitted and rational sources, citing another verse warning against equating evil-doers with believers.

Key Terms
البعث
المعاد
الفلاسفة
الاحتياط
اللذات الجسمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument gives a certain proof that the resurrection will happen.
Correction: Al-Razi's argument does not aim to prove resurrection with certainty; rather, it shows that belief is the rational choice based on risk assessment. The passage itself acknowledges that certain knowledge comes from other proofs (transmitted and rational).

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi's argument cited in the passage, what would happen if belief in the resurrection is false?
A) The believer would be punished.
B) The believer would lose only base bodily pleasures.
C) The believer would suffer eternally.
D) The believer would prove the philosophers correct.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's pragmatic argument shows that belief in resurrection is the safest and most rational choice, regardless of whether it can be proven with certainty.

?
The poem says: 'If your statement is correct, I am not a loser.' Can you honestly say that your daily actions reflect that same confidence? When you sin in private, are you acting as if there is no resurrection, even though you claim to believe?
?
Al-Razi says bodily pleasures are shared by beetles and dogs. What does that say about the things you chase? Are you living for pleasures that even insects enjoy, or are you investing in what only a believer can gain—eternal reward?

Rational Proofs for the Day of Judgment
The author gives multiple rational arguments for the necessity of a final judgment day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational arguments that necessitate the Day of Judgment as derived from divine wisdom and justice.

Core Idea
Wisdom and justice demand a perfect recompense that this world cannot provide.

The author presents a series of rational arguments grounded in the attributes of divine wisdom and justice. These proofs demonstrate that the existence of a final judgment day is not merely a revealed truth but a logical necessity. This passage lays out four interconnected lines of reasoning that compel the rational mind to affirm the hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from one argument to the next.
Each argument begins with a phrase like 'because wisdom necessitates' or 'and because'.
2
Identify the four proofs
The passage contains four distinct rational proofs. Mark where each begins and ends. Note how each is supported by a Quranic verse.
The proofs are: (1) separation of truth/falsehood, (2) recompense according to deeds, (3) pure recompense, (4) death before justice.
3
Understand the logic of each proof
For each proof, ask: What premise does it start from? Why does it lead to the necessity of a judgment day? How does the Quranic citation reinforce the argument?
4
Reflect on the overall conclusion
Combine all four reasons. Why is this world insufficient for perfect justice? How do these arguments show that the hereafter is a rational necessity, not just a dogma?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من المعقول في المسألة أن الحكمة تقتضي الفصل بين المحق والمبطل على وجه يضطر المبطل إلى معرفة حاله في البطلان لئلا تبقى له ريبة في ذلك الشأن، وليست الدنيا بدار هذا الاضطرار؛ لأنها خلقت للابتلاء والاختبار، فلا بد من دار يقع فيها هذا الأمر المختار، ولذا قال الله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ يَوْمَ الْفَصْلِ كَانَ مِيقَاتًا﴾ [النبأ: ١٧]؛ ولأن الحكمة تقتضي جزاء كل عامل على حسب عمله وقد ينعم على العاصي ويبتلي المطيع في دار الدنيا للابتلاء، فلا بد من دار الجزاء؛ ولأن جزاء العمل الصالح نعمة لا يشوبها نقمة، وجزاء العمل السيء نقمة لا يشوبها نعمة، ونعم الدنيا مشوبة بالنقم، ونقمها بالنعم، فلا بد من دار يحصل فيها كمال الجزاء؛ ولأنه قد يموت المحسن والمسيء قبل أن يصل إليهما ثواب أو عقاب فلولا حشر ونشر يصل بهما الثواب إلى المحسن والعقاب إلى المسيء لكانت هذه الحياة عبثا، وقد قال الله سبحانه: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْنَا السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا لَاعِبِينَ مَا خَلَقْنَاهُمَا إِلَّا بِالْحَقِّ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَهُمْ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ إِنَّ يَوْمَ الْفَصْلِ مِيقَاتُهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ﴾ [الدخان: ٣٨-٤٠]
Then from what is rationally understood in the matter is that wisdom necessitates separation between the truthful and the false in a way that compels the false to know his state of falsehood so that no doubt remains for him in that regard, and the world is not a house of this compulsion because it was created for trial and testing; so there must be a house where this determined matter occurs, and therefore Allah said: 'Indeed, the Day of Judgment is an appointed time' [al-Naba':17]; and because wisdom necessitates recompense for every doer according to his deed, and He may bestow favor on the disobedient and afflict the obedient in the worldly abode for testing, so there must be an abode of recompense; and because the recompense for righteous work is a blessing untainted by affliction, and the recompense for evil work is affliction untainted by blessing, but worldly blessings are mixed with afflictions and its afflictions with blessings, so there must be an abode where complete recompense occurs; and because the good-doer and the evil-doer may die before reward or punishment reaches them, so were it not for a resurrection and spreading that would bring reward to the good-doer and punishment to the evil-doer, this life would be in vain, and Allah said: 'And We did not create the heavens and the earth and what is between them in play. We did not create them except in truth, but most of them do not know. Indeed, the Day of Judgment is the appointed time for them all' [al-Dukhan:38-40].
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a sequence of rational proofs for the necessity of a Day of Judgment. The first argument is from wisdom (hikmah): it requires a clear separation between truth and falsehood so that the false have no doubt. This separation cannot be fully realized in this world, which is a place of test and trial; therefore, another abode is needed. This is supported by the Quranic verse 'Indeed, the Day of Judgment is an appointed time.' The second argument: wisdom requires that every person be recompensed according to his deeds. In this world, the disobedient may receive blessings and the obedient may suffer trials, so a separate abode for perfect recompense is necessary. The third argument: the recompense for good should be pure blessing and for evil pure affliction. In this world, all blessings and afflictions are mixed; therefore, an abode of complete justice is required. The fourth argument: since many die without receiving their due reward or punishment, the resurrection and gathering are necessary to bring full recompense; otherwise, life would be meaningless. This is corroborated by the Quranic statement that the creation of heavens and earth is not in play but in truth, and the Day of Judgment is the appointed time for all.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Justice is absent in this world.
Correction: The argument does not claim that justice is absent in this world, but that it is incomplete and must be perfected in the hereafter.

B) This world's blessings and afflictions are mixed, so perfect recompense requires another abode.
C) God is unjust if He does not punish immediately.
D) The Quran explicitly denies justice in this world.

Key Takeaway
Rational reflection on divine wisdom and justice necessitates a final Day of Judgment for perfect and complete recompense.

?

The Necessity of the Hereafter: Proof from Divine Justice
Arguments from divine justice and wisdom proving the necessity of an afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural proofs for the necessity of the Hereafter (Dar al-Jaza') based on divine justice and wisdom.

Core Idea
Without an afterlife, divine justice would be incomplete.

This passage presents the core rational arguments that necessitate a final abode of recompense. It shows that this world cannot fulfill perfect justice because its rewards and punishments are mixed, and many people die without receiving their due. The author then cites a Quranic verse to seal the argument. By the end, you'll see why the Hereafter is not just a matter of faith but a logical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Read and understand the first rational proof
The author argues that worldly rewards are mixed with afflictions, so pure recompense requires another realm. Identify the key phrases: 'nعمة لا يشوبها نقمة' and 'نقمها بالنعم'.
This argument is based on the nature of perfect justice.
2
Read and understand the second rational proof
The author argues that many righteous and wicked die before receiving reward or punishment, so without resurrection, life would be futile. Note the term 'عبث' (futility).
This argument relies on the fact of death.
3
Reflect on the Quranic confirmation
The author cites Quran 44:38-40 to show that creation is not in play but with truth, and the Day of Decision is the appointed time for all. See how the verse supports the rational arguments.
The Quranic verse provides scriptural authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من عامل على حسب عمله وقد ينعم على العاصي ويبتلي المطيع في دار الدنيا للابتلاء، فلا بد دار الجزاء؛ ولأن جزاء العمل الصالح نعمة لا يشوبها نقمة، وجزاء العمل السيء نقمة لا يشوبها نعمة، ونعم الدنيا مشوبة بالنقم، ونقمها بالنعم، فلا بد من دار يحصل فيها كمال الجزاء؛ ولأنه قد يموت المحسن والمسيء قبل أن يصل إليهما ثواب أو عقاب فلولا حشر ونشر يصل بهما الثواب إلى المحسن والعقاب إلى المسيء لكانت هذه الحياة عبثا، وقد قال الله سبحانه: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْنَا السَّمَوَاتِ وَالأَرْضَ وَمَا بَيْنَهُمَا العِبِينَ مَا خَلَقْتُهُمَا إِلَّا بِالْحَقِّ وَلَكِنَّ أَكْثَرَهُمْ لَا يَعْلَمُونَ إِنَّ يَوْمَ الْفَصْلِ مِيقَاتُهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ ﴾ [الدخان: ٣٨-٤٠] .
He acts according to his deed, and He may bestow favor upon the disobedient and test the obedient in the worldly abode for trial; so the abode of recompense (dar al-jaza') is necessary. And because the reward of the righteous deed is a blessing that no affliction mixes with, and the recompense of the evil deed is an affliction that no blessing mixes with, while the blessings of this world are mixed with afflictions and its afflictions with blessings, so there must be an abode in which complete recompense occurs. And because the good-doer and the evil-doer may die before reward or punishment reaches them; so if there were no resurrection and gathering (hashr wa nashr) through which reward reaches the good-doer and punishment the evil-doer, this life would be futile. And Allah the Exalted has said: 'And We did not create the heavens and the earth and what is between them in play. We did not create them except with truth, but most of them do not know. Indeed, the Day of Decision is their appointed time all together.' [Surah al-Dukhan, 38-40].
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessity of the Hereafter, known as Dar al-Jaza' (the Abode of Recompense). It presents two main arguments. First, God deals with people in this world according to their deeds but often gives favors to sinners and trials to the obedient as tests; therefore, a pure and complete recompense cannot be realized here. The reward for good deeds should be an unalloyed blessing, and the punishment for evil deeds an unalloyed affliction, but in this world, blessings are always mixed with afflictions and vice versa. Hence, a separate abode is necessary for perfect justice. Second, many righteous and wicked people die before receiving any reward or punishment; without a resurrection and gathering (hashr wa nashr) where the good receive their due and the wicked theirs, the entire life would be pointless (عبث). The passage concludes by citing Quran 44:38-40, which states that creation is not in play but with truth, and the Day of Decision is the appointed time for all.

On the Superiority of Quranic Verses: Two Kinds of Virtue
Classification of Quranic verses into two types of virtue.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why all Quranic verses are equal in virtue as divine speech, yet some have an additional virtue due to their content, and be able to distinguish between virtue of mention (fadilat al-dhikr) and virtue of the mentioned (fadilat al-madhkur).

Core Idea
All Quranic verses are equal as speech; their content adds extra merit.

In this lesson, we explore a nuanced theological point: while every verse of the Quran is the speech of Allah and therefore equally virtuous in its essence, some verses carry an extra distinction because of what they describe. The author explains that the virtue of a verse can be twofold: the virtue of its wording (dhikr) and the virtue of its subject matter (madhkur). This distinction helps reconcile reports that seem to give certain verses, like Ayat al-Kursi, special status without undermining the equality of all Quranic words.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle of equality
First, read the opening statement that all Quranic verses are equal in virtue and greatness in the meaning of speech. Note the general rule before the exception.
The word 'ma'na al-kalam' refers to their being divine speech.
2
Identify the two kinds of virtue
Look for the terms 'fadilat al-dhikr' and 'fadilat al-madhkur'. Understand that the first relates to the wording itself, the second to what is being talked about.
The passage gives examples: Ayat al-Kursi has both; verses about disbelievers have only virtue of mention.
3
Apply the distinction to examples
Consider why Ayat al-Kursi and Surah al-Ikhlas have double virtue, while other verses do not. Reflect on how this reconciles different hadiths about Quranic excellence.
This shows how kalam uses conceptual distinctions to harmonize revealed texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القول في تفاضل آيات القرآن

والقرآن منزل على رسول الله، وهو في المصحف مكتوب، وآيات القرآن كلها في معنى الكلام مستوية في الفضيلة والعظمة إلا أن لبعضها فضيلة الذكر وفضيلة المذكور، مثل آية الكرسي؛ لأن المذكور فيها جلال الله تعالى وعظمته وصفته، فاجتمعت فيها فضيلتان فضيلة الذكر وفضيلة المذكور، وفي صفة الكفار فضيلة الذكر فحسب، وليس في المذكور وهم الكفار فضيلة.

والقرآن) منزّل بالتشديد أي نزل منجما على رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أي عاما في ثلاثة وعشرين، وهو في المصحف أي في جنسه، وفي نسخة "في المصاحف" مكتوب أي مزبور ومسطور، وفيه إيماء إلى أن ما بين الدفتين كلام الله تعالى على ما هو المشهور. وآيات القرآن كلها أي جميعها في معنى الكلام أي في مقام المرام سواء يكون في رحمة الله ومدح أوليائه أو في غضب الله وذم أعدائه وسائر الأحكام المتعلقة بحكم ابتلائه مستوية الفضيلة أي اللفظية والعظمة أي المعنوية، إلا أن لبعضها فضيلة الذكر أي باعتبار مبناها وفضيلة المذكور أي باعتبار معناها، مثل آية الكرسي؛ لأن المذكور فيها جلال الله تعالى أي هيبته وعظمته وصفته أي نعته الخاص بذاته فاجتمعت فيها فضيلتان فضيلة الذكر وفضيلة المذكور، ومثلها سورة الإخلاص فإنها مختصة بنعوت الاختصاص. وفي صفة الكفار أي كسورة تبت ونحوها من أحوال الفجار فضيلة الذكر فحسب بسكون السين أي فقط، وليس في المذكور وهم الكفار فضيلة تأكيد لما قبله وتصريح بما علم ضمنا من مفهومه بما ورد في فضائل القرآن وسور منه وآيات منه محمول على ما ذكرنا جمعا بين اختلاف الروايات.
Discussion on the superiority of the verses of the Quran.

And the Quran is revealed upon the Messenger of God, and it is written in the mus'haf, and all the verses of the Quran, in the meaning of speech, are equal in virtue and greatness except that some of them have a virtue of mention (fadilat al-dhikr) and a virtue of the mentioned (fadilat al-madhkur), like the Verse of the Throne (Ayat al-Kursi); because what is mentioned in it is the majesty, greatness, and attribute of God Almighty, so two virtues are combined in it: the virtue of mention and the virtue of the mentioned. And in the description of the disbelievers there is only the virtue of mention, and there is no virtue in the mentioned, who are the disbelievers.

And the Quran) is revealed with tashdid, i.e., revealed gradually upon the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, i.e., over a period of twenty-three years, and it is in the mus'haf, i.e., in its genus, and in a copy "in the mus'hafs" written, i.e., inscribed and written, and in it is an indication that what is between the two covers is the speech of God Almighty according to the well-known view. And the verses of the Quran all of them, i.e., all of them, in the meaning of speech, i.e., in the station of intent, whether in the mercy of God and praise of His friends or in the anger of God and blame of His enemies and the rest of rulings related to the judgment of His trial, are equal in virtue, i.e., verbal virtue, and greatness, i.e., meaning-based virtue, except that some of them have a virtue of mention, i.e., with respect to their wording, and a virtue of the mentioned, i.e., with respect to their meaning, like the Verse of the Throne; because what is mentioned in it is the majesty of God Almighty, i.e., His awe and greatness and attribute, i.e., His specific description of His essence, so two virtues are combined in it: the virtue of mention and the virtue of the mentioned, and similar to it is Surah al-Ikhlas, for it is specific to the attributes of exclusivity. And in the description of the disbelievers, i.e., like Surah al-Masad and similar accounts of the wicked, there is only the virtue of mention, with sukun of the sin, i.e., only, and there is no virtue in the mentioned, who are the disbelievers, an emphasis of what preceded and a clarification of what is known implicitly from its understanding, based on what has been reported concerning the virtues of the Quran and its surahs and its verses, carried upon what we have mentioned as a reconciliation between conflicting reports.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the superiority (tafadul) of the verses of the Quran. The author first states a general principle: all Quranic verses are equal in virtue and greatness inasmuch as they are divine speech (ma'na al-kalam), but some have a double virtue due to their content. The two types of virtue are: (1) virtue of mention (fadilat al-dhikr), which pertains to the wording itself, and (2) virtue of the mentioned (fadilat al-madhkur), which pertains to the object or subject mentioned. For example, Ayat al-Kursi (Q. 2:255) mentions the majesty, greatness, and attributes of God, so it combines both virtues: its wording is virtuous and its content is the greatest subject. Similarly, Surah al-Ikhlas (Q. 112) is specific to the attributes of God's exclusivity, so it also has both virtues. In contrast, verses describing the disbelievers (e.g., Surah al-Masad) have only the virtue of mention; their content (the disbelievers themselves) has no inherent virtue. The author then provides a detailed commentary on the matn, explaining that the Quran was revealed gradually over 23 years, is written in the mus'haf (or mus'hafs), and that what is between the covers is the speech of God. He reiterates that all verses are equal in verbal virtue (fadila lafziyya) and meaning-based greatness ('azama ma'nawiyya) as speech, but some have an additional virtue due to their meaning. He specifically mentions Ayat al-Kursi and Surah al-Ikhlas as examples of verses with double virtue, and affirms that the reports about the superiority of certain verses and surahs should be understood in this way to reconcile apparent discrepancies.

Key Terms
تفاضل
فضيلة الذكر
فضيلة المذكور
آية الكرسي
سورة الإخلاص
معنى الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Verses about punishment (e.g., Surah al-Masad) are less virtuous than verses about mercy.
Correction: All verses are equally virtuous as divine speech; the difference is only in the virtue of the mentioned, which does not affect their essential equality as kalam.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which of the following Quranic verses or surahs combines both the virtue of mention (fadilat al-dhikr) and the virtue of the mentioned (fadilat al-madhkur)?
A) Ayat al-Kursi and Surah al-Masad
B) Ayat al-Kursi and Surah al-Ikhlas
C) Surah al-Ikhlas and verses about the disbelievers
D) All verses equally have both virtues

Key Takeaway
All Quranic verses are equal in virtue as divine speech, but some gain added merit from the subject they discuss.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite a verse about the punishment of disbelievers, do you feel it is less valuable than a verse about mercy? How does this lesson correct your perception of every single verse as divine speech? What changes in your recitation starting today?
?
If every verse has virtue of mention because it is Allah's speech, do you treat each verse with equal reverence, or do you speed through verses you find less appealing? Which verses do you usually skip or rush? Commit to reciting Ayat al-Kursi and Surah al-Masad with the same awe tomorrow.
?
The disbelievers themselves have no virtue, yet the verses describing them are still virtuous as speech. This shows the Quran elevates even the mention of evil. Does this make you reflect on how you view the Quran's comprehensiveness? Will you now appreciate every word, even when it condemns? What will you do to change your approach to the Quran?

Eternal Fate of Those Never Reached by Da'wah
Ibn al-Humam states the fruit of disagreement for those never reached by da'wah and lists the opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different theological positions on the eternal fate of a person who never received the prophetic message.

Core Idea
The fate of the unreached divides theologians: some damn, others give hope.

Ibn al-Humam begins by showing the practical consequence (thamara) of the previously discussed disagreement about rational obligation. The key issue: what happens to someone who never heard the call of a prophet? Different schools of thought give opposing answers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ibn al-Humam uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the three groups and their positions
The passage presents two positions held by three groups: Mu'tazila and first group of Hanafis vs second group of Hanafis and Ash'aris. Find each and note their stance on eternal punishment.
3
Ask: why does this matter?
Ask yourself why these categories are the first thing a student of kalam must learn. The commentary will help you answer.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ابن الهمام وثمرة هذا الخلاف تظهر فيمن لم تبلغه دعوة رسول فلم يؤمن حتى فهو مخلد في النار عند المعتزلة والفريق الأول من الحنفية دون الفريق الثاني منهم والأشاعرة، وإذا لم يكن مخاطبا بالإسلام عند هؤلاء فأسلم أي وحد هل يصح إسلامه بمعنى أنه يثاب في الآخرة؟ عند الحنفية نعم كإسلام الصبي الذي يعقل معنى الإسلام والتكليف. وذكر بعض مشايخ الحنفية أنه أبا الخطاب من المشايخ الشافعية يقول: لا يصح عباداته من إيمان من لم تبلغه دعوة كإيمان الصبي عندهم، أي على القول المرجح من مذهبهم خلافا للأئمة الثلاثة؛ لأن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم دعا عليا إلى الإسلام فأجابه، مع الإجماع على أن صلاة وصوم ونحوهما صحيحة. وأما ما نقله البيهقي من أن الأحكام إنما علقت بالبلوغ بعد الهجرة عام الخندق وأما قبل ذلك فكانت منوطة بالتمييز، فيحتاج إلى بيان ذلك وكيفية وقوعه هنالك على أن أمور الإسلام في تكاليف الأحكام كانت تدريجية من الأهون إلى الأصعب لا بالعكس، ولذا كان التكليف أولا بالتوحيد، ثم زيد الصلاة والزكاة ونحوهما كما هو مقتضى حكمة الحكيم المجيد.
Ibn al-Humam said: The fruit of this disagreement appears concerning one whom the call of a messenger did not reach, so he did not believe. Thus he is eternally in the Fire according to the Mu'tazila and the first group of the Hanafis, unlike the second group of them and the Ash'aris. And if according to these he is not addressed by Islam, then if he becomes Muslim—i.e., declares tawhid—is his Islam valid in the sense that he will be rewarded in the afterlife? According to the Hanafis, yes, like the Islam of a discerning child (al-sabi) who understands the meaning of Islam and taklif. And some Hanafi masters mentioned that Abu al-Khattab from the Shafi'i masters says: His acts of worship are not valid from the faith of the one not reached by the call, like the faith of the child according to them—that is, according to the preponderant view of their school, contrary to the three Imams; because the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, called Ali to Islam and he responded, despite the consensus that prayer, fasting and the like are valid. As for what al-Bayhaqi reported—that rulings were attached to puberty after the hijra in the year of the Trench, but before that they were contingent on discernment—this requires explanation of that and how it occurred there, given that the matters of Islam in the obligations of rulings were gradual from easier to harder, not the opposite. Therefore, taklif was first with tawhid, then prayer, zakat, and the like were added, as necessitated by the wisdom of the Wise, the Glorious.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage discusses the practical consequence (thamara) of the earlier disagreement about the nature of obligation before revelation. The issue is the fate of a person who never received the prophetic message (da'wah). Ibn al-Humam outlines the positions: The Mu'tazila and one group of Hanafis hold that such a person is eternally in Hell, while another group of Hanafis and the Ash'aris disagree. Then he addresses whether, if such a person embraces Islam (tawhid), his Islam is valid and he will be rewarded. The Hanafis affirm that it is, likening it to the valid Islam of a discerning child (sabi) who understands the meaning of Islam and moral responsibility (taklif). Some Hanafi scholars mention that the Shafi'i master Abu al-Khattab denies the validity of such a person's worship, comparing it to a child's faith according to his school. The author notes that the Prophet called Ali to Islam and he responded, and there is consensus that a child's prayer and fasting are valid. Then he references al-Bayhaqi's report that legal rulings were tied to puberty after the Hijra, but before that to discernment. He calls for an explanation of this gradualism in Islamic obligations, which started with tawhid and gradually added more duties. This gradualism reflects divine wisdom.

Key Terms
من لم تبلغه الدعوة
الفريق الأول
الفريق الثاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All scholars agree that those who never heard the message are punished.
Correction: Ibn al-Humam shows that there is disagreement: some schools (Mu'tazila and some Hanafis) hold eternal punishment, while others (other Hanafis and Ash'aris) disagree.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two groups hold that the unreached person is eternally in Hell?
A) Mu'tazila and Ash'aris.
B) Mu'tazila and first group of Hanafis.
C) First and second group of Hanafis.
D) Only Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
The eternal fate of those unreached by da'wah is a point of disagreement, with some schools asserting punishment and others not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that some people are eternally punished without hearing the message, how does that change the urgency with which you share Islam with your non-Muslim friends and neighbors?
?
When you encounter someone who has never heard a proper presentation of Islam, do you assume they are excused? Or do you feel a weight of responsibility to convey the truth? What does your answer reveal about your understanding of Allah's justice?

Validity of Islam for the Unreached and Child
Ibn al-Humam discusses the validity of Islam for the unreached, the parallel with a child's faith, and the gradual nature of obligations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether a person never reached by da'wah can have valid faith and worship.

Core Idea
Even without a prophet's call, embracing tawhid may bring reward, like a child's faith.

After stating the disagreement about eternal fate, Ibn al-Humam turns to a related question: if such a person declares tawhid (Islam), is it valid and rewarded? The Hanafis affirm, comparing it to the Islam of a discerning child. He also discusses the Shafi'i opposition and the case of Ali's early acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the flow: question, Hanafi answer, objection, counterargument, and a final note on gradualism.
This passage is more argumentative than the first.
2
Identify the Hanafi position and its analogy
The Hanafis answer 'yes, like the Islam of a discerning child.' Understand why they use this analogy.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
Abu al-Khattab says such a person's worship is invalid, like a child's faith according to his school. Note the response with Ali's example.
4
Reflect on the gradualism of obligations
The passage ends with a note that obligations were gradual, starting with tawhid. See how this supports the main point.

?

?

Are you willing to extend that same mercy to others in your heart, and to yourself when you feel your own faith is weak? What will you do the next time you think someone's faith is invalid?

The Major Signs of the Hour
Lists major signs of the Hour with Quranic proof texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the major signs of the Hour that are mentioned in the Quran, along with their corresponding verses.

Core Idea
The Quran explicitly describes major signs of the Hour.

This lesson presents the major signs of the Hour as listed by the author, supported by direct Quranic evidence. The signs include the emergence of Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the sun rising from the west, and the descent of Jesus. These are not merely hadith reports but are firmly rooted in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Focus on the signs and the verses cited.
The passage is continuous and focuses on three signs.
2
Identify each sign and its verse
Make a list: sign 1 (Dajjal/Gog-Magog) with 21:96, sign 2 (sun rising west) with 6:158, sign 3 (Jesus descent) with 43:61 and 4:159.
3
Understand the explanation for the sun sign
Notice that after the sun rises from the west, faith will not benefit those who had not believed before. This is a key theological point.
This explains the verse's meaning.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why these signs are important in Islamic eschatology and how they are drawn from the Quran itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخروج الدجّال ويأجوج ومأجوج وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ونزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء. وقد أفردت في هذه المسألة المصوّرة رسالة مختصرة وسميتها بـ"المنهاج العلوي في المعراج النبوي". وقد أغرب شارح "العقائد" في تأويل قول عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها: «ما فقد جسد محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ليلة المعراج.» حيث قال : معناه ما فقد جسده عن الروح، بل كان معه روحه. انتهى. وغرابته لا تخفى والتأويل الصحيح أن المعراج كان بمكة في أوائل البعثة حين لم الله تعالى عنها، أو يقال: القضية كانت متعددة، ولذا اختلف في الانتهاء، تولد عائشة رضي، فقيل: إلى الجنة، وقيل: إلى العرش، وقيل: إلى ما فوقه وهو مقام: ﴿ دَنَا فَتَدَلَّى فَكَانَ قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى ﴾ [النجم: ۸-۹] ، ولا يلزم من تعدد الواقعة فرض الصلاة كل مرة كما توهم ابن القيم معترضا. وخروج الدجّال ويأجوج ومأجوج كما قال الله تعالى: حَتَّى إِذَا فُتِحَتْ يَأْجُوجُ وَمَأْجُوجُ وَهُمْ مِنْ كُلِ حَدَبٍ يَنْسِلُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٩٦]، أي يسرعون، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها) كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ ايتِ رَيكَ لَا يَنْفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيْمَانَهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ مِنْ قَبْلُ أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيْمَانِهَا خَيْرًا [الأنعام: ١٥٨]، أي لا ينفع الكافر إيمانه في ذلك الحين، أي طلوع الشمس من المغرب، ولا الفاسق الذي ما كسب خيرا في إيمانه أو توبته يعني لا ينفع نفسا إيمانها ولا كسبها الإيمان إن لم تكن آمنت من قبل أو كسبت خيرا. ونزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّهُ أي عيسى لِلسَّاعَةِ [الزخرف: ٦١]، أي علامة القيامة، وقال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتُبِ إِلَّا لَيُؤْ مِنَنَّ بِهِ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ ﴾ [النساء: ١٥٩]، أي قبل موت عيسى عليه السلام بعد نزوله عند قيام الساعة فتصير
And the emergence of the Dajjal, and Gog and Magog, and the rising of the sun from its west, and the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, from heaven. And I have written a short treatise on this illustrated issue and named it 'al-Minhaj al-'Alawi fi al-Mi'raj al-Nabawi'. And the commentator of 'al-Aqa'id' has made a strange interpretation... (this repeats from earlier lesson) ... And the emergence of the Dajjal and Gog and Magog, as Allah said: 'Until when Gog and Magog are let loose, and they hasten from every elevated place' (21:96), i.e., they hurry. And the rising of the sun from its west, as Allah said: 'The day when some signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before or earned good through its faith' (6:158), i.e., the faith of the disbeliever will not benefit him at that time, i.e., at the rising of the sun from the west, nor the sinner who had not earned good in his faith or repentance, meaning no soul's faith or earning of faith will benefit if it had not believed before or earned good. And the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, from heaven, as Allah said: 'And indeed he (i.e., Jesus) is for the Hour' (43:61), i.e., a sign of the Hour, and Allah said: 'And there is none from the People of the Book except that he will surely believe in him before his death' (4:159), i.e., before the death of Jesus, peace be upon him, after his descent at the establishment of the Hour, so it becomes...
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains many of the major signs of the Hour (ashrat al-sa'ah). The author lists: the emergence of al-Dajjal (the false messiah), the release of Gog and Magog (Ya'juj and Ma'juj), the sun rising from the west, and the descent of Jesus from heaven. For each, he provides Quranic evidence. For Gog and Magog, he cites Surah al-Anbiya 21:96. For the sun rising from the west, he cites Surah al-An'am 6:158, explaining that at that time, faith will no longer benefit those who had not believed before. For the descent of Jesus, he cites Surah al-Zukhruf 43:61 and Surah al-Nisa 4:159, explaining that Jesus is a sign of the Hour, and that all People of the Book will believe in him before his death after his descent. The passage ends mid-sentence ('fasir' — 'so it becomes') indicating the continuation of the explanation.

يأجوج ومأجوج
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
نزول عيسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think major signs of the Hour are only found in hadith.
Correction: This passage shows they are also explicitly mentioned in the Quran.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The Quran explicitly mentions several major signs of the Hour, including the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, the sun rising from the west, and the descent of Jesus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the sun were to rise from the west tomorrow, would any of your current excuses for delaying repentance hold up? What are you waiting for to turn back to Allah wholeheartedly?
?
The descent of Jesus will convince every Jew and Christian of the truth. But you already know this truth from the Quran. Are you living as if you truly believe these signs will come, or are you letting the world distract you from preparing for that Day?

Critique of a Commentator on the Mi'raj
Critiques a commentator's interpretation of Aisha's hadith on the Mi'raj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's critique of a commentator's interpretation of Aisha's statement about the Prophet's body during the Mi'raj.

Core Idea
The author corrects a strange interpretation regarding the Mi'raj.

This passage contains the author's criticism of a commentator's explanation of Aisha's statement that the Prophet's body was not absent during the Mi'raj. The author provides his own interpretation and discusses the issue of the multiple occurrences of the Mi'raj.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Identify the commentator's interpretation being criticized.
2
Understand the critique
The commentator said the Prophet's body was not separate from his spirit. The author calls this strange and offers a different interpretation.
The author suggests the Mi'raj occurred early in Mecca or multiple times.
3
Note the different endpoints
The author lists different opinions about where the Mi'raj ended: Paradise, Throne, or above that. He cites 53:8-9.
4
Recognize the response to Ibn Qayyim
The author refutes Ibn Qayyim's objection that multiple Mi'raj events would require multiple prayer prescriptions.
He says that does not follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخروج الدجّال ويأجوج ومأجوج وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ونزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء. وقد أفردت في هذه المسألة المصوّرة رسالة مختصرة وسميتها بـ"المنهاج العلوي في المعراج النبوي". وقد أغرب شارح "العقائد" في تأويل قول عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها: «ما فقد جسد محمد صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ليلة المعراج.» حيث قال : معناه ما فقد جسده عن الروح، بل كان معه روحه. انتهى. وغرابته لا تخفى والتأويل الصحيح أن المعراج كان بمكة في أوائل البعثة حين لم الله تعالى عنها، أو يقال: القضية كانت متعددة، ولذا اختلف في الانتهاء، تولد عائشة رضي، فقيل: إلى الجنة، وقيل: إلى العرش، وقيل: إلى ما فوقه وهو مقام: ﴿ دَنَا فَتَدَلَّى فَكَانَ قَابَ قَوْسَيْنِ أَوْ أَدْنَى ﴾ [النجم: ۸-۹] ، ولا يلزم من تعدد الواقعة فرض الصلاة كل مرة كما توهم ابن القيم معترضا. وخروج الدجّال ويأجوج ومأجوج كما قال الله تعالى: حَتَّى إِذَا فُتِحَتْ يَأْجُوجُ وَمَأْجُوجُ وَهُمْ مِنْ كُلِ حَدَبٍ يَنْسِلُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٩٦]، أي يسرعون، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها) كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ ايتِ رَيكَ لَا يَنْفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيْمَانَهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ مِنْ قَبْلُ أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيْمَانِهَا خَيْرًا [الأنعام: ١٥٨]، أي لا ينفع الكافر إيمانه في ذلك الحين، أي طلوع الشمس من المغرب، ولا الفاسق الذي ما كسب خيرا في إيمانه أو توبته يعني لا ينفع نفسا إيمانها ولا كسبها الإيمان إن لم تكن آمنت من قبل أو كسبت خيرا. ونزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّهُ أي عيسى لِلسَّاعَةِ [الزخرف: ٦١]، أي علامة القيامة، وقال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتُبِ إِلَّا لَيُؤْ مِنَنَّ بِهِ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ ﴾ [النساء: ١٥٩]، أي قبل موت عيسى عليه السلام بعد نزوله عند قيام الساعة فتصير
And the emergence of the Dajjal, and Gog and Magog, and the rising of the sun from its west, and the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, from heaven. And I have written a short treatise on this illustrated issue and named it 'al-Minhaj al-'Alawi fi al-Mi'raj al-Nabawi'. And the commentator of 'al-Aqa'id' has made a strange interpretation... (this repeats from earlier lesson) ... And the emergence of the Dajjal and Gog and Magog, as Allah said: 'Until when Gog and Magog are let loose, and they hasten from every elevated place' (21:96), i.e., they hurry. And the rising of the sun from its west, as Allah said: 'The day when some signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before or earned good through its faith' (6:158), i.e., the faith of the disbeliever will not benefit him at that time, i.e., at the rising of the sun from the west, nor the sinner who had not earned good in his faith or repentance, meaning no soul's faith or earning of faith will benefit if it had not believed before or earned good. And the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, from heaven, as Allah said: 'And indeed he (i.e., Jesus) is for the Hour' (43:61), i.e., a sign of the Hour, and Allah said: 'And there is none from the People of the Book except that he will surely believe in him before his death' (4:159), i.e., before the death of Jesus, peace be upon him, after his descent at the establishment of the Hour, so it becomes...
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains many of the major signs of the Hour (ashrat al-sa'ah). The author lists: the emergence of al-Dajjal (the false messiah), the release of Gog and Magog (Ya'juj and Ma'juj), the sun rising from the west, and the descent of Jesus from heaven. For each, he provides Quranic evidence. For Gog and Magog, he cites Surah al-Anbiya 21:96. For the sun rising from the west, he cites Surah al-An'am 6:158, explaining that at that time, faith will no longer benefit those who had not believed before. For the descent of Jesus, he cites Surah al-Zukhruf 43:61 and Surah al-Nisa 4:159, explaining that Jesus is a sign of the Hour, and that all People of the Book will believe in him before his death after his descent. The passage ends mid-sentence ('fasir' — 'so it becomes') indicating the continuation of the explanation.

Key Terms
المعراج
عائشة
ابن القيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mi'raj was a single event with a fixed endpoint.
Correction: The author suggests it might have been multiple events, leading to different reported endpoints.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the problem with the commentator's interpretation of Aisha's hadith?
A) The commentator thought the body was separate from the spirit.
B) The commentator's interpretation is strange and incorrect.
C) The commentator denied the Mi'raj happened.
D) The commentator said the Mi'raj was in Medina.

Key Takeaway
The author rejects a literal interpretation of Aisha's statement and proposes that the Mi'raj may have occurred multiple times.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the commentator's interpretation that the Prophet's body never separated from his spirit during the Mi'raj, do you feel a temptation to accept it because it seems to preserve the literal meaning of Aisha's words? Or do you, like the author, consider that the unseen may involve realities beyond our usual categories? Pause and ask yourself: where else in your faith do you insist on a literal reading that might actually limit your understanding of Allah's power?
?
The author rejects Ibn Qayyim's objection by saying that multiple Mi'raj events do not entail multiple prescriptions of prayer. Are there objections you hold against certain beliefs in Islam that actually rely on false assumptions about necessary consequences? Write down one such objection you have heard or held, and then ask: must that consequence really follow?
?
This passage shows a scholar critiquing another's interpretation and offering a nuanced view. When you disagree with a scholar or a fellow Muslim, do you dismiss their view as 'strange' without seeking to understand the deeper reason? Or do you strive to find a reconciliation, even if it means accepting multiple possibilities? Commit today to approaching disagreements in religious matters with humility and a willingness to consider that the truth may be more multifaceted than you assumed.

The Major Signs of the Hour with Quranic Evidence
Enumerates four major eschatological signs and cites Quranic verses for each, with a note on conjunction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four major eschatological signs mentioned by the author, their Quranic proofs, and the significance of the conjunction 'waw' in their listing.

Core Idea
The four signs of the Hour are scripturally established and listed but not necessarily in chronological order.

The author now turns to the major signs that will precede the Day of Judgment. He lists four well-known portents and, crucially, provides a direct Quranic verse for each one. This lesson will guide you through each sign and its evidence, and clarify a common confusion about the order in which they are mentioned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four signs
Read the Arabic passage and list the four signs mentioned. Notice that the author presents them in a single sentence before giving the proofs.
The signs are: the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, sunrise from the west, and the descent of Jesus.
2
Examine the Quranic proof for each sign
For each sign, the author cites a specific Quranic verse. Read the verses and the brief explanations provided.
The verses are: 21:96 for Gog and Magog, 6:158 for sunrise from the west, 43:61 and 4:159 for Jesus. Note that no verse is given for the Dajjal in this passage.
3
Understand the clarification about 'waw'
The author notes a variant order and then explains that the conjunction 'waw' (and) indicates mere conjunction, not chronological sequence. Reflect on why this clarification is important.
The common misunderstanding is that listing order equals time order. The author explicitly refutes this.
4
Connect to broader eschatology
Consider how these signs function in Islamic theology: they are certain but their exact order and timing are known only to Allah.
This lesson focuses on the textual evidence; deeper theological implications are for later study.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخروج الدجال ويأجوج ومأجوج وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ونزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء. كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿حَتَّى إِذَا فُتِحَتْ يَأْجُوجُ وَمَأْجُوجُ وَهُمْ مِنْ كُلِّ حَدَبٍ يَنْسِلُونَ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٩٦]، أي يسرعون، وطلوع الشمس من مغربها كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ آيَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنْفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانَهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ مِنْ قَبْلُ أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْرًا﴾ [الأنعام: ١٥٨]، أي لا ينفع الكافر إيمانه في ذلك الحين، أي طلوع الشمس من المغرب، ولا الفاسق الذي ما كسب خيرا في إيمانه أو توبته يعني لا ينفع نفسا إيمانها ولا كسبها الإيمان إن لم تكن آمنت من قبل أو كسبت خيرا. ونزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّهُ أي عيسى لِلسَّاعَةِ﴾ [الزخرف: ٦١]، أي علامة القيامة، وقال الله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ إِلَّا لَيُؤْمِنَنَّ بِهِ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ﴾ [النساء: ١٥٩]، أي قبل موت عيسى عليه السلام بعد نزوله عند قيام الساعة فتصير الملل واحدة وهي ملة الإسلام الحقيقة. وفي نسخة قدّم طلوع الشمس على البقية، وعلى كل تقدير فالواو لمطلق الجمعية.
And the emergence of the Dajjal, and Gog and Magog, and the sunrise from its west, and the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, from heaven. As Allah Almighty said: 'Until when Gog and Magog are let loose and they hasten from every mound' [Quran 21:96], meaning they hurry. And the sunrise from its west, as Allah Almighty said: 'The day when some signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before or earned good in its faith' [Quran 6:158], meaning the faith of the disbeliever will not benefit him at that time, i.e., at sunrise from the west, nor the sinner who did not earn good in his faith or repentance, meaning no soul's faith or its earning of faith will benefit if it had not believed before or earned good. And the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, from heaven, as Allah Almighty said: 'And indeed he, meaning Jesus, is for the Hour' [Quran 43:61], meaning a sign of the Resurrection, and Allah Almighty said: 'And there is none of the People of the Book but will surely believe in him before his death' [Quran 4:159], meaning before the death of Jesus, peace be upon him, after his descent at the establishment of the Hour, so the religions become one, which is the true religion of Islam. And in one copy, sunrise was placed before the rest, but in any case the 'waw' is for absolute conjunction.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage enumerates four major signs of the Hour: the Dajjal, Gog and Magog, sunrise from the west, and the descent of Jesus. The author provides a Quranic proof for each: for Gog and Magog, Surah al-Anbiya 96; for sunrise from the west, Surah al-An'am 158, explaining that faith at that time will not benefit; for Jesus, Surah al-Zukhruf 61 and Surah al-Nisa 159, noting that all People of the Book will believe in him before his death. The author then notes a variant in the order (sunrise placed first) and clarifies that the conjunction 'waw' does not imply chronological order but merely joins the items mentioned. Thus, the passage is a classification of signs with scriptural evidence, emphasizing that the listing order is not necessarily the order of occurrence.

Key Terms
أشراط الساعة
الدجال
يأجوج ومأجوج
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
نزول عيسى
الواو لمطلق الجمعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that the order in which the signs are listed reflects their chronological order of occurrence.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the conjunction 'waw' is for mere conjunction (مطلق الجمعية) and does not indicate sequence. The order in the list is not necessarily the order of their appearance.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does the author cite for the sign of the sunrise from the west?
A) Surah al-Anbiya 96
B) Surah al-An'am 158
C) Surah al-Zukhruf 61
D) Surah al-Nisa 159

Key Takeaway
The major signs of the Hour are attested in the Quran, and their listing order does not imply a chronological sequence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The sunrise from the west will shut the door of acceptance. If you were to die tonight, would your faith and deeds be enough to secure you, or are you procrastinating in turning to Allah?
?
The descent of Jesus will bring unity of belief. Is your heart truly attached to the truth about Jesus as taught in the Quran, or do you hold onto doubts or ideas from other sources that contradict it?
?
The Dajjal is a trial that will deceive many. What are you doing today to arm yourself with knowledge of his fitnah so that you are not among those who follow him?
