The Mahdi, the Dajjal, and Jesus' Descent
Author describes the Mahdi's appearance, Dajjal's siege, and Jesus' descent and victory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of events involving the Mahdi's appearance, the Dajjal's siege, and Jesus' descent to kill the Dajjal.

Core Idea
The Mahdi appears first, then the Dajjal, then Jesus descends to defeat him.

This lesson focuses on the beginning of the eschatological narrative: the Mahdi's emergence, the Dajjal's siege, and the dramatic descent of Jesus to kill the Dajjal. Understanding this sequence is crucial for grasping the overall timeline of the end times.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the Mahdi and Dajjal
Read the Arabic passage describing the Mahdi's appearance in the two sanctuaries, his journey to Jerusalem, and the Dajjal's siege.
Notice the specific locations mentioned: 'الحرمين الشريفين' (Mecca and Medina) and 'بيت المقدس' (Jerusalem).
2
Identify details of Jesus' descent
Find where Jesus descends (the eastern minaret in Damascus) and how he kills the Dajjal (with a single blow).
3
Reflect on the Dajjal's destruction
Consider the comparison of the Dajjal melting like salt in water, emphasizing the swift and complete victory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا فترتيب القضية أن المهدي عليه السلام يظهر أولاً في الحرمين الشريفين، ثم يأتي بيت المقدس فيأتي الدجال ويحصره في ذلك الحال فينزل عيسى عليه السلام المنارة الشرقية في دمشق الشام، ويجيء إلى قتال الدجال فيقتله بضربة في الحال، فإنه يذوب كالملح في الماء عند نزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء، فيجتمع عيسى عليه السلام بالمهدي رضي الله عنه وقد أقيمت الصلاة، فيشير المهدي لعيسى عليه السلام بالتقدم فيمتنع متعللا بأن هذه الصلاة أقيمت لك فأنت أولى بأن تكون الأمام في هذا المقام، ويقتدي به ليظهر متابعته لنبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم كما أشار إلى هذا المعنى صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: ((لو كان موسى حيا لما وسعه إلا اتباعي)) . وقد بينت وجه ذلك عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ مِيثَاقَ النَّبِيِّنَ﴾ إشارة إلى أن تقدّم المهدي خاص بهذه الصلاة. لَمَا آتَيْتُكُمْ مِنْ كِتَابٍ وَحِكْمَةٍ ثُمَّ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولُ الآية [آل عمران : ۸۱]، في "شرح الشفا" وغيره. وقد ورد ((أنه يبقى في الأرض أربعين سنة، ثم يموت ويصلي عليه المسلمون ويدفنونه)). على ما رواه الطيالسي في مسنده، وروى غيره أنه يدفن بين النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والصديق رضي الله عنه . وروي أنه يدفن بين الشيخين، فهنيئا للشيخين حيث اكتنفا بالنبيين.
Otherwise, the order of the matter is that the Mahdi, peace be upon him, appears first in the two noble sanctuaries, then he comes to Jerusalem, then the Dajjal comes and besieges him in that situation, then Jesus, peace be upon him, descends at the eastern minaret in Damascus of Syria, and he comes to fight the Dajjal and kills him with a blow instantly, for he melts like salt in water at the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, from heaven. Then Jesus meets the Mahdi, may Allah be pleased with him, while the prayer has been established. The Mahdi signals to Jesus to go forward, but he refuses, excusing himself by saying: 'This prayer has been established for you, so you are more entitled to be the imam in this situation.' And he follows him to show his following of our Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, as the Prophet referred to this meaning in his saying: 'If Moses were alive, he would have no choice but to follow me.' And I have explained the aspect of that at His saying: 'And when Allah took the covenant of the prophets' [Quran 3:81], indicating that the precedence of the Mahdi is specific to this prayer. And it has been reported that he remains on earth for forty years, then he dies, the Muslims pray over him and bury him, according to what al-Tayalisi narrated in his Musnad, and others narrated that he is buried between the Prophet and al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him. And it is narrated that he is buried between the two shaykhs. So blessed are the two shaykhs, for they are flanked by the two prophets.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage describes the chronological sequence of eschatological events. It begins by stating that the Mahdi appears first in Mecca and Medina, then goes to Jerusalem. The Dajjal then appears and besieges him. At that moment, Jesus descends on a minaret in Damascus, comes to fight the Dajjal, and kills him instantly (the Dajjal melts like salt). Jesus then meets the Mahdi, who prepares to lead the prayer. The Mahdi invites Jesus to lead, but Jesus declines, saying the prayer was established for the Mahdi, so he is more entitled. Jesus follows the Mahdi to demonstrate his adherence to the Sharia of the Prophet Muhammad, citing a hadith about Moses. The author then references his explanation of Quran 3:81 regarding the covenant of the prophets, indicating that the Mahdi's precedence is only for this prayer. Finally, he mentions that Jesus will live for forty years, then die, and be buried in a grave between the Prophet and Abu Bakr, or between the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar), bringing together two prophets and two caliphs.

عيسى
المنارة الشرقية
بيت المقدس

Key Takeaway
Jesus descends in Damascus, kills the Dajjal instantly, ending the siege of the Mahdi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Dajjal's power melts like salt at Jesus' descent. What 'powerful' sin or doubt in your life have you been tolerating that you know would dissolve if you truly turned to Allah? What specific step will you take today to confront it?
?
The sequence shows that calamity (the Dajjal's siege) precedes divine rescue (Jesus' descent). How does this reshape your patience during your current trials? Name one trial you are facing that you need to trust will be followed by relief.
?
The Mahdi appears first in the holy places. If you seek guidance to face the trials ahead, are you turning to the sources of guidance (the Quran and Sunnah) as the Mahdi turned to the sanctuaries? What habit will you change this week to seek guidance more earnestly?

The Meeting of Jesus and the Mahdi: Prayer Leadership
Author describes Jesus' meeting with the Mahdi and the issue of prayer leadership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the interaction between Jesus and the Mahdi regarding who should lead the prayer, and the significance of Jesus deferring to the Mahdi.

Core Idea
Jesus defers to the Mahdi to lead the prayer, showing his adherence to Muhammad's Sharia.

After the Dajjal is defeated, Jesus meets the Mahdi. A prayer is about to begin, and the Mahdi invites Jesus to lead. However, Jesus refuses, citing that the prayer was established for the Mahdi. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this interaction and the hadith cited.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing the meeting
Read the Arabic text from 'فيجتمع عيسى' through the end of the Quranic reference. Pay attention to the dialogue.
2
Understand Jesus' refusal
Notice that Jesus says 'هذه الصلاة أقيمت لك فأنت أولى' meaning the prayer was established for the Mahdi, so he is more entitled to lead.
This shows Jesus' humility and respect for the earthly caliph.
3
Reflect on the hadith and Quranic interpretation
Consider the hadith about Moses and the Quranic verse (3:81) that the author cites to explain that the Mahdi's precedence is specific to this prayer.
The author references his own work 'Sharh al-Shifa' for further explanation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا فترتيب القضية أن المهدي عليه السلام يظهر أولاً في الحرمين الشريفين، ثم يأتي بيت المقدس فيأتي الدجال ويحصره في ذلك الحال فينزل عيسى عليه السلام المنارة الشرقية في دمشق الشام، ويجيء إلى قتال الدجال فيقتله بضربة في الحال، فإنه يذوب كالملح في الماء عند نزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء، فيجتمع عيسى عليه السلام بالمهدي رضي الله عنه وقد أقيمت الصلاة، فيشير المهدي لعيسى عليه السلام بالتقدم فيمتنع متعللا بأن هذه الصلاة أقيمت لك فأنت أولى بأن تكون الأمام في هذا المقام، ويقتدي به ليظهر متابعته لنبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم كما أشار إلى هذا المعنى صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: ((لو كان موسى حيا لما وسعه إلا اتباعي)) . وقد بينت وجه ذلك عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ مِيثَاقَ النَّبِيِّنَ﴾ إشارة إلى أن تقدّم المهدي خاص بهذه الصلاة. لَمَا آتَيْتُكُمْ مِنْ كِتَابٍ وَحِكْمَةٍ ثُمَّ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولُ الآية [آل عمران : ۸۱]، في "شرح الشفا" وغيره. وقد ورد ((أنه يبقى في الأرض أربعين سنة، ثم يموت ويصلي عليه المسلمون ويدفنونه)). على ما رواه الطيالسي في مسنده، وروى غيره أنه يدفن بين النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والصديق رضي الله عنه . وروي أنه يدفن بين الشيخين، فهنيئا للشيخين حيث اكتنفا بالنبيين.
Otherwise, the order of the matter is that the Mahdi, peace be upon him, appears first in the two noble sanctuaries, then he comes to Jerusalem, then the Dajjal comes and besieges him in that situation, then Jesus, peace be upon him, descends at the eastern minaret in Damascus of Syria, and he comes to fight the Dajjal and kills him with a blow instantly, for he melts like salt in water at the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, from heaven. Then Jesus meets the Mahdi, may Allah be pleased with him, while the prayer has been established. The Mahdi signals to Jesus to go forward, but he refuses, excusing himself by saying: 'This prayer has been established for you, so you are more entitled to be the imam in this situation.' And he follows him to show his following of our Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, as the Prophet referred to this meaning in his saying: 'If Moses were alive, he would have no choice but to follow me.' And I have explained the aspect of that at His saying: 'And when Allah took the covenant of the prophets' [Quran 3:81], indicating that the precedence of the Mahdi is specific to this prayer. And it has been reported that he remains on earth for forty years, then he dies, the Muslims pray over him and bury him, according to what al-Tayalisi narrated in his Musnad, and others narrated that he is buried between the Prophet and al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him. And it is narrated that he is buried between the two shaykhs. So blessed are the two shaykhs, for they are flanked by the two prophets.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage describes the chronological sequence of eschatological events. It begins by stating that the Mahdi appears first in Mecca and Medina, then goes to Jerusalem. The Dajjal then appears and besieges him. At that moment, Jesus descends on a minaret in Damascus, comes to fight the Dajjal, and kills him instantly (the Dajjal melts like salt). Jesus then meets the Mahdi, who prepares to lead the prayer. The Mahdi invites Jesus to lead, but Jesus declines, saying the prayer was established for the Mahdi, so he is more entitled. Jesus follows the Mahdi to demonstrate his adherence to the Sharia of the Prophet Muhammad, citing a hadith about Moses. The author then references his explanation of Quran 3:81 regarding the covenant of the prophets, indicating that the Mahdi's precedence is only for this prayer. Finally, he mentions that Jesus will live for forty years, then die, and be buried in a grave between the Prophet and Abu Bakr, or between the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar), bringing together two prophets and two caliphs.

الصلاة
أمتكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jesus will lead the prayer after his descent.
Correction: The text shows Jesus defers to the Mahdi, saying 'This prayer was established for you, so you are more entitled.'

Checkpoint

A) He is not yet ready to pray.
B) The prayer was established for the Mahdi, so he is more entitled.
C) Jesus cannot lead prayer after killing the Dajjal.
D) The Mahdi does not want Jesus to lead.

Key Takeaway
Jesus defers to the Mahdi in prayer to demonstrate his complete adherence to the Sharia of Prophet Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself in a situation where someone else is more entitled to lead, do you step back gracefully, or does your ego resist? Jesus, a prophet of Allah, deferred to the Mahdi. Where is your pride hurting your ability to follow proper Islamic etiquette?
?
Jesus followed the Mahdi to demonstrate his commitment to Muhammad's Sharia. Is there any practice or belief you hold onto that contradicts the Sunnah? What would it take for you to abandon it completely and follow the Prophet without reservation?
?
The Prophet said that if Moses were alive, he would have to follow Muhammad. Do you truly internalize that Muhammad is the final messenger with the complete and abrogating Sharia? Or do you still secretly elevate other traditions or figures above his Sunnah? Examine your heart honestly.

Jesus' Life After Victory and His Burial
Author quotes reports about Jesus' lifespan, death, and burial location.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Jesus lives forty years after his descent, dies a natural death, and is buried between Muhammad and Abu Bakr.

This lesson covers the concluding part of the narrative: Jesus' long life on earth after defeating the Dajjal, his natural death, and the honor of being buried in a grave that lies between the Prophet Muhammad and Abu Bakr as-Siddiq.

Sequence of Mahdi, Dajjal, and Jesus's Descent
Sequence of eschatological events: Mahdi, Dajjal, Jesus, and the prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct order of eschatological events involving the Mahdi, Dajjal, and Jesus, and the significance of Jesus following the Mahdi in prayer.

Core Idea
Jesus descends to follow, not lead — the Mahdi is the imam.

This passage from the commentary on Fiqh al-Akbar clarifies the sequence of major events before the end of time. It corrects common assumptions about who leads the prayer, and uses the incident to demonstrate Jesus's reverence for the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the manuscript variant mentioned at the beginning.
2
Identify the sequence of events
Trace the order: Mahdi appears, then Dajjal, then Jesus descends, then the meeting and prayer. Notice the specific locations.
The 'waw' (and) does not imply order; the actual order is explained.
3
Understand the prayer incident
Focus on the dialogue: Mahdi gestures for Jesus to lead, Jesus declines, then follows. Understand why Jesus declines and what this shows about his relationship to the Prophet Muhammad.
This is the key point that counters the common misconception.
4
Note the burial details
The passage includes narrations about Jesus's lifespan and burial place. Observe the variant opinions and the honor to the two Shaykhs.
This part is supplementary but enriches understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي نسخة قدّم طلوع الشمس على البقية، وعلى كل تقدير فالواو لمطلق الجمعية، وإلا فترتيب القضية أن المهدي عليه السلام يظهر أولاً في الحرمين الشريفين، ثم يأتي بيت المقدس فيأتي الدجال ويحصره في ذلك الحال فينزل عيسى عليه السلام المنارة الشرقية في دمشق الشام، ويجيء إلى قتال الدجال فيقتله بضربة في الحال، فإنه يذوب كالملح في الماء عند نزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء، فيجتمع عيسى عليه السلام بالمهدي رضي الله عنه وقد أقيمت الصلاة، فيشير المهدي لعيسى عليه السلام بالتقدم فيمتنع متعللا بأن هذه الصلاة أقيمت لك فأنت أولى بأن تكون الأمام في هذا المقام، ويقتدي به ليظهر متابعته لنبينا صلى الله عليه وسلم كما أشار إلى هذا المعنى صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: ((لو كان موسى حيا لما وسعه إلا اتباعي)). وقد بينت وجه ذلك عند قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ مِيثَاقَ النَّبِيِّنَ﴾ إشارة إلى أن تقدّم المهدي خاص بهذه الصلاة. لَمَا أَتَيْتُكُمْ مِنْ كِتَابٍ وَحِكْمَةٍ ثُمَّ جَاءَكُمْ رَسُولُ الآية [آل عمران : ۸۱]، في "شرح الشفا" وغيره. وقد ورد ((أنه يبقى في الأرض أربعين سنة، ثم يموت ويصلي عليه المسلمون ويدفنونه)). على ما رواه الطيالسي في مسنده، وروى غيره أنه يدفن بين النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والصديق رضي الله عنه. وروي أنه يدفن بين الشيخين، فهنيئا للشيخين حيث اكتنفا بالنبيين. وفي رواية: ((أنه يمكث سبع سنين)). قيل: وهي الأصح.
And in a copy, he presented the rising of the sun before the rest. And in any case, the 'waw' is for absolute conjunction. Otherwise, the arrangement of the matter is that the Mahdi, peace be upon him, appears first in the two noble sanctuaries, then he comes to Bayt al-Maqdis. Then the Dajjal comes and besieges him in that situation. Then Jesus, peace be upon him, descends at the eastern minaret in Damascus of Syria, and he comes to fight the Dajjal and kills him with a single blow instantly. For he melts like salt in water when Jesus, peace be upon him, descends from heaven. Then Jesus, peace be upon him, meets the Mahdi, may Allah be pleased with him, while the prayer has been established. The Mahdi gestures to Jesus, peace be upon him, to go forward, but he declines, using as an excuse that this prayer was established for you, so you are more worthy to be the imam in this situation. And he (Jesus) follows him (the Mahdi) to show his following of our Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, as he, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, indicated this meaning by his saying: 'If Moses were alive, he would have no choice but to follow me.' And I have explained the aspect of that at the saying of Allah Almighty: 'And when Allah took the covenant of the prophets,' indicating that the precedence of the Mahdi is specific to this prayer. 'When I gave you a Book and Wisdom, then a messenger comes to you' [Al Imran: 81], in 'Sharh al-Shifa' and elsewhere. And it has been narrated that he (Jesus) will remain on earth for forty years, then he will die, and the Muslims will pray over him and bury him. According to what al-Tayalisi narrated in his Musnad, and others narrated that he will be buried between the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him. And it is narrated that he will be buried between the two Shaykhs. So congratulations to the two Shaykhs for being flanked by the two prophets. And in a narration: 'He will stay for seven years.' It is said that this is the more correct.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage describes the sequence of major eschatological events involving the Mahdi, the Dajjal, and Jesus (peace be upon him). It begins by noting a manuscript variant that places the rising of the sun (from the west) earlier, but the commentator emphasizes that the conjunction 'waw' simply indicates conjunction, not order. The actual order is: the Mahdi appears first in Mecca and Medina, then heads to Jerusalem. The Dajjal comes and besieges him. Then Jesus descends at the eastern minaret in Damascus, goes to fight the Dajjal, and kills him instantly; the Dajjal melts like salt in water. After that, Jesus meets the Mahdi while the prayer is being established. The Mahdi gestures for Jesus to lead the prayer, but Jesus declines, saying the prayer was established for the Mahdi, so he is more worthy to be imam. Jesus then follows the Mahdi to demonstrate his obedience to the Prophet Muhammad (PBUH), citing the hadith about Moses also having to follow the Prophet. The commentator adds that he explained this point earlier at the verse about the covenant of the prophets (Quran 3:81) and references 'Sharh al-Shifa'. The passage then includes the hadith that Jesus will remain on earth for forty years, die, and be buried by Muslims, with some narrations specifying burial between the Prophet and Abu Bakr, or between the two Shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar). A variant says seven years, which is considered more authentic. The passage concludes by celebrating the honor of the two Shaykhs being flanked by two prophets (Muhammad and Jesus).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jesus will lead the prayer when he descends.
Correction: Jesus declines leadership in prayer and follows the Mahdi, demonstrating his followership to Prophet Muhammad.

?

?

Jesus's Forty-Year Stay and His Leadership in Prayer
Clarifies the forty-year hadith and Jesus's imamate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct interpretation of the forty-year stay of Jesus and his role as imam in prayer, including the relationship with the Mahdi.

Core Idea
Jesus's forty years cover both his first and second coming, and he leads prayer as the superior imam.

This passage from the commentary clarifies a key ambiguous point about the hadith that Jesus will stay for forty years. It also resolves the apparent tension between Jesus and the Mahdi regarding who leads the prayer. The scholar explains that Jesus is the primary imam, and the Mahdi follows him, without contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get the flow. Then read the English translation to grasp the meaning.
Pay attention to the phrase 'المراد بالأربعين' which signals the intended meaning.
2
Understand the 'forty years' interpretation
The commentator clarifies that the forty years mentioned in the hadith includes both the time before Jesus's ascension and after his return. He notes Jesus was raised at age 33, so the remaining years are after his return.
This resolves a common confusion that the forty years refer only to the second coming.
3
Learn about Jesus's imamate
The passage cites Sharh al-Aqa'id to state that Jesus is the imam who leads prayer, and the Mahdi follows him because Jesus is superior (afdal).
Note that this does not contradict earlier statements where the Mahdi initially gestures to Jesus, because that gesture was out of respect for Islamic law, not because the Mahdi is the actual imam.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal significance
This lesson reinforces the high status of Jesus in Islamic eschatology and clarifies the relationship between Jesus and the Mahdi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمراد بالأربعين في الرواية الأولى مدة مكثه قبل الرفع وبعده، فإنه رفع وله ثلاث وثلاثون سنة. وفي شرح العقائد : الأصح أن عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام يصلي بالناس ويؤمهم ويقتدي به المهدي؛ لأنه أفضل وإمامته أولى. انتهى. ولا ينافي ما قدمناه كما لا يخفى.
And what is meant by 'forty' in the first narration is the duration of his stay before the raising and after it, for he will be raised at thirty-three years of age. And in Sharh al-Aqa'id: The correct opinion is that Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, will pray with the people and lead them, and the Mahdi will follow him, because he is superior and his imamate is more appropriate. End. And it does not contradict what we presented, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage provides an interpretation of the hadith that Jesus will remain on earth for forty years. The commentator clarifies that the 'forty years' refers to the total period of his stay on earth both before his ascension and after his second coming, since he was raised (ascended) at the age of thirty-three. Then the commentator cites from 'Sharh al-Aqa'id' the correct position: that Jesus will lead the prayer and the Mahdi will follow him, because Jesus is superior (afdal) and his imamate takes precedence. The commentator concludes that this does not contradict what was previously mentioned (that the Mahdi initially gestures to Jesus and then Jesus follows the Mahdi), because the initial deference was to show Jesus's subordination to Islamic law, while in absolute terms Jesus is the imam.

الرفع
عيسى عليه السلام
الإمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The forty years refer only to Jesus's second coming.
Correction: The forty years encompass his entire stay on earth, both before ascension and after return, totaling forty years (33 before ascension + 7 after return).

Checkpoint

A) The Mahdi

D) An angel

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mahdi, a great leader, humbly follows Jesus. Is there someone in your life whom you resist following because of pride? What would it cost you to step back and let that person lead?
?
Jesus's imamate is based on his superiority in virtue and knowledge. In what areas of your life are you trying to lead without being truly qualified? How can you humbly seek to follow those who are more knowledgeable and pious?
?
If you knew that your time on earth was limited to a specific number of years, as Jesus's was forty, what would you change about how you spend your days? Would you prioritize prayer, learning, or serving others differently?

Gog and Magog and the Death of the Believers
Describes three eschatological signs after Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of events after Jesus: the appearance and destruction of Gog and Magog, the death of all believers, and the sun rising from the west.

Core Idea
After Jesus, Gog and Magog are destroyed, then believers die and the sun rises from the west.

This lesson focuses on the first three events in the eschatological sequence described in the commentary. After the death of Jesus, Gog and Magog emerge, but Allah destroys them through the blessing of Jesus' supplication. Then all remaining believers die, and the sun rises from the west—a major sign of the Hour.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the three distinct events.
2
Identify the events
List the three events in order: appearance of Gog and Magog, their destruction, death of believers and sunrise.
The destruction is through Jesus' prayer.
3
Reflect on the sequence
Consider why these events are placed after Jesus' death in Islamic eschatology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يظهر يأجوج ومأجوج فيهلكهم الله أجمعين ببركة دعائه عليهم. ثم يموت المؤمنون وتطلع الشمس من مغربها ويرفع القرآن كما روى ابن ماجه من حديث حذيفة: ((يدرس الإسلام كما يدرس وشي الثوب أي أطرافه حتى لا يدرى صيام ولا صلاة ولا نسك ولا صدقة، ويسرى على كتاب الله في ليلة فلا يبقى في الأرض منه آية)). وروى البيهقي في "شعب الإيمان" عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه قال: ((اقرؤوا القرآن قبل أن يرفع فإنه لا تقوم الساعة حتى يرفع قالوا: هذه المصاحف ترفع فكيف ما في الصدور ؟ قال : يغدى عليهم ليلا فيرفع من صدورهم فيصبحون يقولون لكنا نعلم شيئا ثم يقعون في الشعر)). قال القرطبي: وهذا إنما يكون بعد موت عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام وبعد هدم الحبشة الكعبة.
Then Gog and Magog appear, and Allah destroys them all by the blessing of his (Jesus's) supplication against them. Then the believers die, and the sun rises from its west, and the Quran is raised, as Ibn Majah narrated from the hadith of Hudhayfah: 'Islam wears out like the embroidery of a garment wears out, i.e., its edges, until it is not known what is fasting, prayer, ritual, or charity. And the Book of Allah will be taken away in a night, and not a single verse of it will remain on earth.' And al-Bayhaqi narrated in 'Shu'ab al-Iman' from Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'Read the Quran before it is raised, for the Hour will not rise until it is raised. They said: The mus-hafs are raised? What about what is in the hearts? He said: It will be taken from them at night, and it will be raised from their hearts. In the morning they will say: We used to know something, then they will fall into poetry.' Al-Qurtubi said: That will only be after the death of Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, and after the Abyssinians demolish the Ka'bah.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage outlines three more eschatological events after the death of Jesus. First, the emergence of Gog and Magog (Ya'juj and Ma'juj), whom Allah destroys through the blessing of Jesus's supplication. Second, after that, all believers die, and the sun rises from the west—a major sign of the Hour. Third, the Quran is raised (taken away) from the earth. The commentator supports this with a hadith from Ibn Majah via Hudhayfah: Islam will gradually wear out until even the basic rituals are unknown, and the Quran will be taken away in a single night, leaving no verse on earth. Another hadith from Ibn Mas'ud, narrated by al-Bayhaqi, warns people to read the Quran before it is raised, explaining that it will be removed not only from manuscripts but also from people's hearts, so they may wake up having forgotten it. Al-Qurtubi clarifies that this raising occurs after the death of Jesus and after the Abyssinians destroy the Ka'bah. The passage provides the scriptural basis for these signs.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
الشمس من مغربها
موت المؤمنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to Gog and Magog?
A) They conquer the world
B) They are destroyed by Allah through Jesus' supplication
C) They convert to Islam
D) They are sealed behind a wall

Key Takeaway
The first set of signs after Jesus includes the destruction of Gog and Magog, the death of all believers, and the sun rising from the west.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After Jesus, the believers die before the sun rises from the west. Are you living today as if every good deed could be your last, since you don't know when your life will end before that sign?
?
Gog and Magog are destroyed through Jesus' supplication, not his own power. Does your prayer life reflect a real dependence on Allah to protect you from evils you cannot overcome alone, or do you rely on your own strength?
?
The sun rising from the west closes the door of repentance. Which sin are you putting off repentance for, assuming you have time to change later? What will it take for you to turn back to Allah today?

The Raising of the Quran
Describes the raising of the Quran with two hadiths and timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran will be raised from the earth, including its removal from physical copies and human hearts.

Core Idea
The Quran will be taken away in a night, leaving no verse on earth or in hearts.

This lesson covers the final sign mentioned in the passage: the raising of the Quran. Two hadiths describe how Islam will fade and the Quranic text will be lifted from both manuscripts and memories. The commentator specifies that this occurs after the death of Jesus and the destruction of the Ka'bah by the Abyssinians.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith from Hudhayfah
Note the description of Islam wearing out and the Quran being taken away in a night.
2
Read the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud
Understand the clarification that the Quran is lifted from hearts as well.
3
Note the timing by al-Qurtubi
This event occurs after the death of Jesus and the Abyssinian destruction of the Ka'bah.

Correction: It is also lifted from people's hearts, as Ibn Mas'ud explained.

Summary Belief in All Signs of the Hour
States the principle of summary belief in signs of the Hour.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that summary belief in the signs of the Day of Judgment is sufficient, and that detailed knowledge of each sign is not required for correct faith.

Core Idea
Summary belief in all signs of the Hour suffices.

This passage concludes the discussion on eschatological signs by establishing a key methodological principle. The commentator explains that it is enough to affirm them in general, based on authentic reports and explicit verses, without needing to know every detail. This principle protects the believer from unnecessary speculation while maintaining firm faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the key phrase 'الإيمان الإجمالي' (summary belief).
2
Identify the key principle
The passage states that summary belief (iman ijmail) in what is in the Books and Sunnah is sufficient. Identify the phrase that specifies the sources (Quran and hadith).
The passage also mentions 'الأخبار الصحيحة' (authentic reports) and 'الآيات الصريحة' (explicit verses).
3
Reflect on the reason for brevity
Why does the commentator say 'تفاصيل هذه الأحوال ليس هذا المحل محل بيان بسطها'? Consider that the context does not require detailed exposition; the core obligation is affirmation.
This shows a pedagogical choice to focus on essentials.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتفاصيل هذه الأحوال ليس هذا المحل محل بيان بسطها، وكذا ما أبهمه الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله بقوله : (وسائر علامات يوم القيامة) إذ يكفي الإيمان الإجمالي بما في الكتب والسنة على ما وردت أي على وفق ما جاءت به الأخبار الصحيحة بل الآيات الصريحة بالنسبة إلى بعض شرائطها حق كائن أي ثابت وأمر قويم.
And the details of these conditions are not a place for their elaboration here, as well as what the Greatest Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, meant by his saying: 'And the rest of the signs of the Day of Judgment' — for summary belief in what is in the Books and the Sunnah as they have come, i.e., in accordance with what the authentic reports have brought, rather the explicit verses concerning some of their conditions, is sufficient — true and existent, i.e., established and a correct matter.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This concluding passage explains that the detailed discussion of all the specific events of the Day of Judgment is not appropriate for this context. The commentator refers to the statement of the Greatest Imam (Abu Hanifa) in the matn of al-Fiqh al-Akbar: 'And the rest of the signs of the Day of Judgment' — indicating that the author did not elaborate. The commentator argues that it is sufficient to have a general, summary belief (iman ijmail) in what is found in the Quran and authentic hadith regarding these signs. Some of these signs are mentioned in explicit Quranic verses. Such signs are 'true and existent' (haqq ka'in), meaning they are established and sound. Thus the lesson emphasizes that detailed knowledge is not required; the essential obligation is to affirm that all the signs reported in authentic sources will indeed come to pass.

Key Terms
الإيمان الإجمالي
علامات يوم القيامة
الأخبار الصحيحة
الآيات الصريحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That one must know every detail of eschatological signs to have correct faith.
Correction: The passage asserts that summary belief (iman ijmail) in the signs as reported in authentic sources is sufficient; detailed knowledge is not obligatory.

Checkpoint
What type of belief is considered sufficient for the signs of the Hour according to the passage?
A) Detailed belief with all evidences
B) Summary belief (ijmali)
C) Belief based on reason alone
D) Belief only in major signs

Key Takeaway
Summary belief (iman ijmail) in all signs of the Hour as reported in authentic sources is sufficient; detailed knowledge is not required.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself more concerned with knowing the timeline of the Hour than with preparing for its sudden arrival? How would your daily priorities shift if you truly lived with summary belief while letting the details rest with Allah?
?
When you hear debates about the specifics of the Dajjal or the Beast, does it stir anxiety or arrogance in your heart? Could you instead say, 'I believe in it as reported,' and trust that the authentic reports are enough to keep you on the straight path?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow and He asked why you didn't require every detail of the signs to believe, would your iman be enough? Or would you have to admit you demanded certainty beyond His revelation?

The Reality of Eschatological Signs and the Descent of Jesus
Author affirms signs of the Hour and details Jesus's descent and role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all signs of the Day of Resurrection reported in authentic narrations are true and certain, and you will learn about the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, including the duration of his stay and his leadership in prayer.

Core Idea
Eschatological signs are real; Jesus will return as a just leader.

The author begins by affirming the truth of all signs of the Hour as conveyed by authentic reports. He then clarifies a specific point regarding the 'forty' years mentioned in narrations about Jesus's descent, and he cites the preferred opinion that Jesus will lead the prayer, with the Mahdi following him. This lesson establishes the foundational belief in these prophetic announcements.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the affirmative language and the logical flow from general affirmation to specific detail about Jesus.
2
Identify the key statements
The passage affirms signs as true, explains the 'forty', and states Jesus's imamate. Underline each key point.
3
Understand the difference between opinions
Notice the mention of Sharh al-‘Aqa’id and the preference for Jesus leading over the Mahdi. Why would there be different opinions?
This shows scholarly debate over details, but core belief is fixed.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Why does the author start with these specifics? To ground belief in authentic reports and to clarify a common point of confusion about Jesus's role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسائر علامات يوم القيامة على ما وردت به الأخبار الصحيحة حق كائن والمراد بالأربعين في الرواية الأولى مدة مكثه قبل الرفع وبعده، فإنه رفع وله ثلاث وثلاثون سنة. وفي شرح العقائد : الأصح أن عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام يصلي بالناس ويؤمهم ويقتدي به المهدي؛ لأنه أفضل وإمامته أولى. انتهى. ولا ينافي ما قدمناه كما لا يخفى(۱). ثم يظهر يأجوج ومأجوج فيهلكهم الله أجمعين ببركة دعائه عليهم. ثم يموت المؤمنون وتطلع الشمس من مغربها ويرفع القرآن كما روى ابن ماجه من حديث حذيفة: ((يدرس الإسلام كما يدرس وشي الثوب أي أطرافه حتى لا يدرى صيام ولا صلاة ولا نسك ولا صدقة، ويسرى على كتاب الله في ليلة فلا يبقى في الأرض منه (آية)). (۲) وروى البيهقي في "شعب الإيمان" عن ابن مسعود رضي الله الله عنه قال: ((اقرؤوا القرآن قبل أن يرفع فإنه لا تقوم الساعة حتى يرفع قالوا: هذه المصاحف ترفع فكيف ما في الصدور ؟ قال : يغدى عليهم ليلا فيرفع من صدورهم فيصبحون يقولون لكنا نعلم شيئا ثم يقعون في الشعر)). (۳) قال القرطبي: وهذا إنما يكون بعد موت عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام وبعد هدم الحبشة الكعبة. وتفاصيل هذه الأحوال ليس هذا المحل محل بيان بسطها ، وكذا ما أبهمه الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله بقوله : (وسائر علامات يوم القيامة) إذ يكفي الإيمان الإجمالي بما في الكتب والسنة على ما وردت أي على وفق ما جاءت به الأخبار الصحيحة بل الآيات الصريحة بالنسبة إلى بعض شرائطها حق كائن أي ثابت وأمر قويم.
And the rest of the signs of the Day of Resurrection, as reported by authentic narrations, are true and certain. The intended meaning of 'forty' in the first narration is the duration of his stay before his raising and after it, for he was raised at the age of thirty-three years. In Sharh al-‘Aqa’id: The correct view is that Jesus, peace be upon him, will lead the people in prayer and they will follow him, and the Mahdi will follow him because he is superior and his leadership is more appropriate. End. And it does not contradict what we have presented, as is not hidden. Then Gog and Magog will appear, and Allah will destroy them all through the blessing of his supplication against them. Then the believers will die, and the sun will rise from its west, and the Quran will be raised, as reported by Ibn Majah from the hadith of Hudhayfah: 'Islam will wear out like the embroidery of a garment (i.e., its edges) worn out, so that one will not know fasting, prayer, ritual sacrifice, or charity, and the Book of Allah will be taken away at night, so that no verse will remain on earth.' And al-Bayhaqi narrated in Shu‘ab al-Iman from Ibn Mas‘ud, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'Recite the Quran before it is raised, for the Hour will not come until it is raised. They said: The copies will be raised, so what about what is in the hearts? He said: It will come upon them at night and be raised from their hearts, and they will wake up saying: We do not know anything, and then they will fall into poetry.' Al-Qurtubi said: This will only be after the death of Jesus, peace be upon him, and after the Abyssinians demolish the Ka'bah. The details of these states are not a place for explanation here; likewise what the Great Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, left ambiguous in his statement: 'and the rest of the signs of the Day of Resurrection'—for general belief in what is in the Books and Sunnah, as they came, i.e., in accordance with what the authentic narrations brought, indeed the clear verses regarding some of their conditions, suffices. They are true, i.e., established and correct.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the eschatological signs mentioned in the Fiqh al-Akbar. The author first affirms that all signs of the Day of Judgment, as reported in authentic narrations, are true and real. He then clarifies the phrase 'the rest of the signs' by focusing on specific events. He explains the reference to 'forty' regarding the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him—it is the duration of his stay on earth before and after his being raised to heaven, noting that he was raised at age thirty-three. He then cites the preferred opinion from Sharh al-‘Aqa’id that Jesus will lead the prayer and the Mahdi will follow him, because Jesus is superior, and this does not contradict earlier statements. Next, he details events: the appearance of Gog and Magog, their destruction by Allah through Jesus's supplication, the death of believers, the sun rising from the west, and the raising of the Quran. He supports these with hadiths, including one from Ibn Majah about Islam wearing out and the Quran being taken up from the earth, and one from al-Bayhaqi about the Quran being raised from the hearts. He then quotes al-Qurtubi, who states that the raising of the Quran occurs after Jesus's death and the destruction of the Ka'bah by the Abyssinians. Finally, the author notes that this is not the place for a detailed exposition of all signs; rather, it suffices to generally believe in them as reported in authentic narrations and clear Quranic verses, affirming that they are true and established.

Key Terms
علامات يوم القيامة
عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام
المهدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the Mahdi will lead the prayer with Jesus following him.
Correction: The correct view according to Ahl al-Sunnah is that Jesus will lead, with the Mahdi following, because Jesus is superior.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view regarding who leads the prayer during Jesus's descent?
A) The Mahdi leads and Jesus follows.
B) Jesus leads and the Mahdi follows.
C) They pray separately.
D) There is no prayer.

Key Takeaway
The signs of the Hour are true; Jesus will return, lead prayer, and be followed by the Mahdi.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Jesus could descend tomorrow, what concrete change would you make in your life today? Are you living with that urgency, or have you let the certainty of these signs slip into mere intellectual belief?
?
The passage states that Jesus is superior and therefore more fit to lead. Where in your life do you struggle to follow someone else's leadership, even when you know they are more qualified? How can you cultivate the humility to follow those who are more righteous?
?
The signs of the Hour are described as 'true and certain.' Do you carry that certainty in your heart, or do you find yourself doubting or neglecting it? What is one habit you can change starting today to reflect a heart that truly awaits the Hour?

Events After Jesus: Gog and Magog, the Sun from the West, and the Raising of the Quran
Author enumerates events after Jesus and provides hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of eschatological events following the descent of Jesus, including the appearance of Gog and Magog, the death of believers, the sun rising from the west, and the raising of the Quran, along with the supporting hadiths and scholarly commentary.

Core Idea
After Jesus's death, Gog and Magog appear, the Quran is raised, and final signs occur.

The author continues the sequence of signs after Jesus's descent. He describes the appearance of Gog and Magog and their destruction through Jesus's supplication, then the death of believers, the sun rising from the west, and the raising of the Quran. He supports these points with hadiths from Ibn Majah and al-Bayhaqi, and quotes al-Qurtubi to clarify the timing. This lesson emphasizes that these events are literal and certain.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the order of events and the use of 'then' (ثم) to indicate sequence.
2
List the events in order
Write down the four main events: Gog and Magog, death of believers, sun from west, raising of Quran.
3
Focus on the hadith evidence
Read the hadith from Ibn Majah about Islam wearing out and the Quran being taken; then the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud about raising from hearts. Understand how they support the author's claims.
The second hadith emphasizes that even memorized Quran will be removed.
4
Understand al-Qurtubi's clarification
Al-Qurtubi states that the raising of the Quran occurs after Jesus's death and the destruction of the Ka'bah. Note that this is one scholarly opinion on timing.
5
Reflect on the author's conclusion
The author concludes that general belief in these signs suffices; details are not expanded here. Why might he say this?
He is emphasizing the principle of tafwīd (accepting without delving into details).

وسائر علامات يوم القيامة على ما وردت به الأخبار الصحيحة حق كائن والمراد بالأربعين في الرواية الأولى مدة مكثه قبل الرفع وبعده، فإنه رفع وله ثلاث وثلاثون سنة. وفي شرح العقائد : الأصح أن عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام يصلي بالناس ويؤمهم ويقتدي به المهدي؛ لأنه أفضل وإمامته أولى. انتهى. ولا ينافي ما قدمناه كما لا يخفى(۱). ثم يظهر يأجوج ومأجوج فيهلكهم الله أجمعين ببركة دعائه عليهم. ثم يموت المؤمنون وتطلع الشمس من مغربها ويرفع القرآن كما روى ابن ماجه من حديث حذيفة: ((يدرس الإسلام كما يدرس وشي الثوب أي أطرافه حتى لا يدرى صيام ولا صلاة ولا نسك ولا صدقة، ويسرى على كتاب الله في ليلة فلا يبقى في الأرض منه (آية)). (۲) وروى البيهقي في "شعب الإيمان" عن ابن مسعود رضي الله الله عنه قال: ((اقرؤوا القرآن قبل أن يرفع فإنه لا تقوم الساعة حتى يرفع قالوا: هذه المصاحف ترفع فكيف ما في الصدور ؟ قال : يغدى عليهم ليلا فيرفع من صدورهم فيصبحون يقولون لكنا نعلم شيئا ثم يقعون في الشعر)). (۳) قال القرطبي: وهذا إنما يكون بعد موت عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام وبعد هدم الحبشة الكعبة. وتفاصيل هذه الأحوال ليس هذا المحل محل بيان بسطها ، وكذا ما أبهمه الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله بقوله : (وسائر علامات يوم القيامة) إذ يكفي الإيمان الإجمالي بما في الكتب والسنة على ما وردت أي على وفق ما جاءت به الأخبار الصحيحة بل الآيات الصريحة بالنسبة إلى بعض شرائطها حق كائن أي ثابت وأمر قويم.
And the rest of the signs of the Day of Resurrection, as reported by authentic narrations, are true and certain. The intended meaning of 'forty' in the first narration is the duration of his stay before his raising and after it, for he was raised at the age of thirty-three years. In Sharh al-‘Aqa’id: The correct view is that Jesus, peace be upon him, will lead the people in prayer and they will follow him, and the Mahdi will follow him because he is superior and his leadership is more appropriate. End. And it does not contradict what we have presented, as is not hidden. Then Gog and Magog will appear, and Allah will destroy them all through the blessing of his supplication against them. Then the believers will die, and the sun will rise from its west, and the Quran will be raised, as reported by Ibn Majah from the hadith of Hudhayfah: 'Islam will wear out like the embroidery of a garment (i.e., its edges) worn out, so that one will not know fasting, prayer, ritual sacrifice, or charity, and the Book of Allah will be taken away at night, so that no verse will remain on earth.' And al-Bayhaqi narrated in Shu‘ab al-Iman from Ibn Mas‘ud, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'Recite the Quran before it is raised, for the Hour will not come until it is raised. They said: The copies will be raised, so what about what is in the hearts? He said: It will come upon them at night and be raised from their hearts, and they will wake up saying: We do not know anything, and then they will fall into poetry.' Al-Qurtubi said: This will only be after the death of Jesus, peace be upon him, and after the Abyssinians demolish the Ka'bah. The details of these states are not a place for explanation here; likewise what the Great Imam, may Allah have mercy on him, left ambiguous in his statement: 'and the rest of the signs of the Day of Resurrection'—for general belief in what is in the Books and Sunnah, as they came, i.e., in accordance with what the authentic narrations brought, indeed the clear verses regarding some of their conditions, suffices. They are true, i.e., established and correct.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the eschatological signs mentioned in the Fiqh al-Akbar. The author first affirms that all signs of the Day of Judgment, as reported in authentic narrations, are true and real. He then clarifies the phrase 'the rest of the signs' by focusing on specific events. He explains the reference to 'forty' regarding the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him—it is the duration of his stay on earth before and after his being raised to heaven, noting that he was raised at age thirty-three. He then cites the preferred opinion from Sharh al-‘Aqa’id that Jesus will lead the prayer and the Mahdi will follow him, because Jesus is superior, and this does not contradict earlier statements. Next, he details events: the appearance of Gog and Magog, their destruction by Allah through Jesus's supplication, the death of believers, the sun rising from the west, and the raising of the Quran. He supports these with hadiths, including one from Ibn Majah about Islam wearing out and the Quran being taken up from the earth, and one from al-Bayhaqi about the Quran being raised from the hearts. He then quotes al-Qurtubi, who states that the raising of the Quran occurs after Jesus's death and the destruction of the Ka'bah by the Abyssinians. Finally, the author notes that this is not the place for a detailed exposition of all signs; rather, it suffices to generally believe in them as reported in authentic narrations and clear Quranic verses, affirming that they are true and established.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
رفع القرآن
شروق الشمس من مغربها

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the raising of the Quran only refers to physical copies.
Correction: The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud indicates it is raised from hearts as well.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, how is the Quran raised from the hearts?
A) By burning
B) By taking it at night
C) By people forgetting
D) By being destroyed

Key Takeaway
After Jesus's death, Gog and Magog are destroyed, believers die, sun rises from west, and the Quran is raised; these are true signs supported by sound hadiths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith says the Quran will be raised from the hearts so that people wake up saying, 'We do not know anything,' and then they fall into poetry. If the Quran were removed from your heart tonight, what would remain? What poetry or worldly speech would fill the void? Will you take action today to ensure the Quran is deeply rooted in your heart before it is too late?
?
The believers die before the sun rises from the west. Are you certain that you will be among the believers at that time? Do you live with the reality of these signs, or do you act as if they are distant and irrelevant? What change in your daily life would prove that you truly believe these events are near?
?
The author says general belief in these signs suffices, but the Prophet urged recitation before the Quran is raised. Do you recite the Quran daily with the intention of ingraining it in your heart? If you were to lose the Quran from your heart tonight, what spiritual loss would that be? Start now by reciting a portion and reflecting on its meaning, committing to never let it go.
